قلت : لا ، فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت/ الجزء الثاني · المزيل (كما يزول) هذا التعلق بالموت لا أن الفعل يرتفع) بالنسخ فأين هذا من ذاك، فإن يصح زوال هذا التعلق فإنه قبل الوجود كان معدوماً بالعدم الأصلي، فلا يكون بالرافع وبعد الوجود لا يتصور العدم لرافع، لأنه تحصيل الحاصل، وحال الوجود اجتماع النقيضين . قلت هذا بعينه شبهة أصحاب البخت والاتفاق على ثبوت حاجة الممكن إلى تأثير الجاعل . فالجواب : أن الرفع بعد الوجود حال العدم اللاحق الحاصل بهذا الرفع وهذا غير ممتنع فافهم (و) قالوا (رابعاً) الحكم الأول (في علم الباري تعالى (إما مستمر) بأن تعلق علمه بثبوت الاستمرار والدوام له فلا ينسخ وإلا لزم الجهل) فإن النسخ يقتضي وقوع عدم الحكم فالحكم بالدوام كذب والعلم به جهل (أو مؤقت) بأن تعلق العلم ببقائه إلى وقت معين (فلا رفع) فإنه يرتفع بمجيء الوقت فلا نسخ (قلنا) الحكم (مؤقت) لكن بالوقت الذي علم أنه ينسخه فيه وذلك موجب للنسخ لا مانع له ، لأنه لو لم ينسخ فيه لبقي بعده فيلزم الجهل، نعم : لو كان الحكم مؤقتاً لانتفى لمجيء الوقت من غير رفع فتدبر ولو قرر الدليل بأن الحكم مؤبد في علمه بأن تعلق العلم بالحكم المؤبد فلا يصح ،رفعه، وإلا لم يبق مؤبداً فيلزم الجهل. أو مؤقت بأن تعلق بالحكم المغيا بوقت فلا ينسخ لم يتوجه هذا الجواب وآل إلى الثاني، ويجاب بالجواب الذي مرَّ من منع الحصر واختيار الأول وتجويز ارتفاع المؤبد المعلوم فتذكر (أقول : ولك أن تقول في الجواب الحكم (مستمر قبل النسخ في علم الباري (وغير مستمر بعده) ولا يلزم الجهل، لأن هذا انقلاب وانقلاب العلم الانقلاب المعلوم، لا يلزم منه الجهل كما في الحوادث فافهم إنه دقيق فإنه سبحانه يعلم الحوادث حال الوجود موجودة، وحال العدم معدومة، فينقلب علمه لانقلاب ،المعلوم وهذا مبني على ما ذهب إليه بعض المتكلمين أن صفة العلم قديمة وتعلقاته حادثة، ومتبدلة حسب تبدل المعلوم في نفسه، وفيه بحث، أما :أولاً : فلأن هذا المبنى باطل، كيف ويلزم أن لا تكون الحوادث معلومة في الأزل وهو بداء وجهل، كما يقوله شياطين الرافضة خذلهم الله تعالى وأما ثانياً : فلأنه لو سلم هذا المبنى لكنه غير وافٍ، فإن تعلق العلم باستمرار الحكم وبالنسخ لم يستمر صار هذا العلم جهلاً البتة، وإن لم يتعلق بالاستمرار عاد إلى الجواب الأول فافهم. نعم : لو قرر الدليل بالتقرير المذكور الأوّل سابقاً، وقرر الجواب بأنه تعلق العلم بالحكم المقيد بالاستمرار ، ثم إذا زال هذا الحكم تعلق بمخالفه يبقى الإشكال الأول، إلا أن يقال : تعلق في الأزل بهذا الحكم وبقائه إلى مدة كذا. ثم وجود حكم مخالف لكن ينبو عنه العبارة فتدبر العتابية قالوا: لو نسخ شريعة موسى عليه وعلى نبينا وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام البطل قوله وهو متواتر عنه هذه شريعة مؤبدة) وهذا لا يدل على بطلان النسخ مطلقاً، بل نسخ شريعة موسى (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه يبطل، بل يجوز أن يكون هذا إنشاء فتنتسخ بشروق شمس الحقيقة وهي شريعة سيد العالم صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه وسلم ولو سلم أنه خبر فيجوز أن يكون مجازاً عن طول المكث فلا يبطل . فإن قلت : إن فيهما التزام التجوز وهو خلاف الأصل، قلت: نعم، لكن ههنا قد دل القاطع من الدليل، فإنه قد تواتر عن موسى عليه السلام الأخبار برسالة سيد العالم صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم، وإن قبلته تتحول إلى الكعبة، فلا معنى لدوام شريعة موسى عليه السلام إلا بأحد التأويلين فافهم ولو سلم الاستلزام) أي استلزم بطلان هذا القول (فلا نسلم أن (قوله أي قول موسى عليه السلام فلا استحالة في بطلانه (بل) هو (مختلق) ومفتري (قيل : اختلقه ابن الراوندي فإن اليهود كانوا قوماً بهتاً، وكانوا يفترون على الله ورسوله كذباً، ويحرّفون الكلم عن مواضعه فلا اعتماد في نقلهم، والتواتر ممنوع إنما هو يدعون تواتر قتل عيسى عليه السلام مع أنه شبه لهم، وكيف لا يكون مختلفاً (ولو قاله) عليه السلام (القضت العادة بمحاجتهم (به سيد العالم صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم كما حاجوا بسائر مزخرفاتهم، ولو وقعت المحاجة لنقلت لتوفر الدواعي على نقله فعلم أنه مختلق قطعاً (وما زعموا أن في التوراة تمسكوا بالسبت ما دامت السموات والأرض) وهذا يفيد أن لا ينسخ تعظيم السبت. وقد ادعيتم نسخه فمدفوع بأنه لا تواتر في التوراة الكائنة الآن) في أيديهم لأنه لم يكن أحبارهم الناقلون من زمن عيسى عليه السلام بالغين حد التواتر، بل على عدد كانوا يجتمعون على التحريف والاتفاق أهل النقل على إحراق بخت نصر) الظالم أسفارها) حين طغوا وقتلوا نبياً من أنبياء الله تعالى وقيل كان اسمه «شعياء» فبعث الله عليهم هذا الظالم فقتل ثلثهم وسبى ،ثلثهم وترك ثلثهم، وأحرق أسفار كتاب الله التوراة وبيت المقدس (وأنه لم يبق من يحفظها لأنه قتل الحفظة كلهم، ولم يكن حفاظ لها إلا أقل القليل (وذكر) في التاريخ (أن عزيراً) عليه السلام (ألهمها) بعدما أماته الله مائة عام ثم بعثه، فجاء فوجد القرية معمورة من بني إسرائيل، فطلب التوراة فلم يجدها عندهم، فدعا الله تعالى بأن يلهمها، وكان مجاب الدعوة، بل نبياً وكتبها ودفعها إلى تلميذه ليقرأها عليهم) فصار مدار النقل على هذا التلميذ فأين التواتر، بل قيل : زاد هذا التلميذ ونقص فلا اعتماد عليه، ونسبوا لهذا الإلهام إليه بنوته الله تعالى لادعائهم أن إلهام التوراة لا يكون إلاّ لابن الله تعالى عما يقول الظالمون، فكيف يعتمد على قول من له هذه الحماقة (ولذا) أي لكونها غير متواترة (لم يزل نسخها الثلاث التي بأيدي العتابية والتي بأيدي السامرية والتي بأيدي النصارى، وقيل: هي السامرية والعبرية واليونانية مختلفة في أعمار (الدنيا في نسخ السامرية زيادة ألف وكثير على ما في العتابية والتي في أيدي النصارى زيادة ألف وثلثمائة سنة، وفيها الوعد بخروج المسيح عليه السلام، وبخروج العربي صاحب الجمل وهو سيد العالم محمد صلاة الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه، وارتفاع تحريم السبت عند خروجهما كذا في «الحاشية» ناقلاً عن «التقرير» (كذا في التحرير)
I said: No. The remover (is like death) removes this attachment, not that the act itself is raised by abrogation. So where is this from that? If the removal of this attachment is valid, then before existence it was non-existent by original non-existence, so it is not by a remover; and after existence, non-existence by a remover is inconceivable because it would be obtaining what is already obtained, and in the state of existence it would be conjunction of two opposites. I said: This is exactly the doubt of the people of chance and the agreement on the need of the contingent for the effect of the Maker. The answer: Raising after existence is in the state of subsequent non-existence obtained by this raising, and this is not impossible. So understand. And they said fourthly: The first ruling in the knowledge of Allah the Exalted is either perpetual, because His knowledge attaches to its being permanent and eternal, so it cannot be abrogated, otherwise ignorance would follow. Indeed abrogation implies the occurrence of non-existence of the ruling, so the ruling of permanence is false and knowledge of it is ignorance. Or time-limited, because knowledge attaches to its remaining until a specific time, so there is no raising because it is raised by the arrival of that time, so no abrogation. We said: The ruling is time-limited, but to the time that He knows He will abrogate it therein, and that necessitates abrogation and is not an obstacle to it. For if He did not abrogate it therein, it would remain after it, thus ignorance would follow. Yes, if the ruling were time-limited, it would be negated by the arrival of the time without any raising. So ponder. And if the proof were established that the ruling is perpetual in His knowledge, because knowledge attaches to the perpetual ruling, then its raising is invalid, otherwise it would not remain perpetual, so ignorance would follow. Or time-limited, because it attaches to the ruling limited by a time, so it is not abrogated. This answer is not pertinent and returns to the second. And it is answered with the answer that passed of preventing the division and choosing the first and permitting the raising of the known perpetual. So remember. (I say: And you can say in the answer: The ruling is perpetual before abrogation in Allah's knowledge, and non-perpetual after it, and ignorance does not follow, because this is a change, and the change of knowledge with the change of the known does not necessitate ignorance, as in accidents. So understand that it is subtle. Indeed He the Glorious knows happenings: in the state of existence as existent, and in the state of non-existence as non-existent. So His knowledge changes with the change of the known. This is based on what some theologians went to: that the attribute of knowledge is eternal and its attachments are temporal and change according to the change of the known in itself. But there is discussion in it. First: because this basis is false, since it would entail that happenings are not known in eternity, which is bada' and ignorance, as the devils of the Rafida say, may Allah forsake them. Second: even if this basis is granted, it is insufficient. For if the attachment of knowledge to the permanence of the ruling and to abrogation did not continue, this knowledge becomes ignorance absolutely. And if it did not attach to permanence, it returns to the first answer. So understand. Yes, if the proof were established by the previous first formulation, and the answer was established that knowledge attaches to the ruling qualified by permanence, then when this ruling ceases, it attaches to its opposite, the first problem remains. Unless it is said: it attached in eternity to this ruling and its remaining until such a time, then the existence of a contrary ruling, but the expression shies from it. So ponder. The 'Attabiyya said: If the law of Moses is abrogated, his saying, which is mutawatir from him, 'This law is eternal,' becomes false. But this does not indicate the invalidity of abrogation absolutely, but rather the abrogation of Moses' law. We said: We do not concede that it becomes false. Rather it is possible that this was an announcement, then it is abrogated by the rising of the sun of truth, which is the law of the Master of the World. And if it is conceded that it is a report, it is possible that it is a metaphor for long duration, so it is not invalid. If you say: In both there is an adoption of metaphorical meaning which is against the principle. I say: Yes, but here a decisive proof has indicated. Indeed the reports of the message of the Master of the World have been mutawatir from Moses, and that his qibla shifts to the Ka'ba, so there is no meaning for the perpetuity of Moses' law except by one of the two interpretations. So understand. And if the implication is conceded, we do not concede that his statement is impossible to be false. Rather it is fabricated and forged. It was said: Ibn al-Rawandi fabricated it. For the Jews were a slanderous people, they used to fabricate lies against Allah and His messenger, and distort words from their places, so no reliance on their transmission. Tawatur is denied; they only claim tawatur of the killing of Jesus, though it was made ambiguous to them. And how could it not be different? And if he had said it, custom would have required them to argue with it against the Master of the World, as they argued with their other embellishments. And if the argument had occurred, it would have been transmitted due to the ample motives for its transmission, so it is known to be fabricated absolutely. And what they claim that in the Torah: 'Hold fast to the Sabbath as long as the heavens and the earth endure' indicates that the veneration of the Sabbath cannot be abrogated, and you claim its abrogation. It is refuted by the fact that there is no tawatur in the Torah currently in their hands, because their rabbis who transmitted from the time of Jesus did not reach the level of tawatur, rather they were a number who used to gather for distortion. And the people of transmission agree on the burning of its books by the oppressor Nebuchadnezzar when they transgressed and killed a prophet of Allah, said to be Isaiah. So Allah sent this oppressor against them; he killed a third, captured a third, left a third, and burned the books of the Torah and the Bayt al-Maqdis. And that none remained to memorize it because he killed all the memorizers, and there were only very few. And it is mentioned in history that Ezra was inspired with it after Allah caused him to die for a hundred years then raised him. He came and found the city inhabited by Bani Isra'il, asked for the Torah but did not find it with them, so he prayed to Allah to inspire him, and he was answered, indeed a prophet. He wrote it and gave it to his student to read to them. So the transmission became dependent on this student, so where is tawatur? Rather it is said: this student added and subtracted, so no reliance on it. And they attributed to this inspiration sonship to Allah, due to their claim that inspiration of the Torah is only for a son of Allah — exalted is Allah above what the oppressors say. So how can one rely on the word of one who has such foolishness? Therefore, because it is not mutawatir, its three versions have not ceased: that of the 'Attabiyya, that of the Samaritans, and that of the Christians. It is said: they are the Samaritan, Hebrew, and Greek, differing in the ages of the world: in the Samaritan version there is an increase of a thousand and much over what is in the 'Attabiyya version, and in the one in the hands of the Christians there is an increase of a thousand and three hundred years. And in it is the promise of the coming of the Messiah and the coming of the Arab with the camel, who is the Master of the World, Muhammad, and the lifting of the prohibition of the Sabbath at their coming. Thus in the 'Hashiya' quoting from 'Taqrir'. Thus in 'Tahrir'.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is part of a defense of the possibility of abrogation (naskh) in Islamic law. The author, commenting on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, addresses a series of objections raised against naskh. First, he refutes the claim that abrogation is impossible because it would require removing an existing ruling, which is like collecting something already obtained. He responds that the removal applies to the subsequent state, not the existing one. Then he takes up the fourth objection: that a ruling in God's eternal knowledge is either perpetual or time-limited, so no abrogation. The author insists the ruling is time-limited to the moment God knows He will abrogate it. The commentator adds a subtle point: God's knowledge changes with the change of the known, though this view is controversial and the commentator ultimately rejects it. Next, the author refutes the argument from the 'Attabiyya (a Jewish sect) that abrogation of Moses' law would falsify his statement that it is eternal. The author suggests this statement could be a metaphor for long duration, or was an announcement later abrogated by Muhammad's prophethood. He further undermines the reliability of the Torah by noting the lack of tawatur, the destruction of the original texts by Nebuchadnezzar, and the reconstruction by Ezra relying on a single student. The existence of multiple variant versions (Samaritan, Hebrew, Greek) with different chronologies further discredits any claim of uncorrupted mutawatir transmission. Thus, the objections to naskh are invalid.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a previously enacted legal ruling by a later revelation.
البداء (al-bada'): The false belief that God changes His mind or acquires new knowledge, attributed to some Rafidah (Shi'a groups).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, what is the nature of a ruling that is abrogated?
A) It was known to be perpetual but abrogated anyway.
B) It was time-limited to the moment of abrogation.
C) It was only apparent, not real.
D) It was known to be eternal but abrogated for a higher purpose.

Key Takeaway
A ruling subject to naskh is time-limited in divine knowledge to the exact moment of abrogation, preserving both divine omniscience and the possibility of legal change.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
12 min
Refuting the Objection from the Torah's Alleged Perpetuity and Its Unreliable Transmission
Refutes the objection from the Torah's alleged perpetuity and critiques its transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi critique of scriptural transmission to refute claims that Torah laws are perpetual, and distinguish between mutawatir and non-mutawatir transmission in evaluating scriptural authority.

Core Idea
The Torah's transmission is not mutawatir; its alleged perpetuity is fabricated, and Moses' statement is metaphorical or abrogated.

This lesson addresses the objection from the 'Attabiyya (a Jewish sect) who argue that abrogation of Moses' law is impossible because he declared it eternal. The Hanafi response is multi-pronged: Moses' statement may have been a metaphor for long duration, or an announcement later abrogated by Muhammad ﷺ. Moreover, the Torah itself is not reliably transmitted; its history shows destruction, reconstruction, and multiple variants. Hence, reliance on such texts is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The 'Attabiyya claim that Moses said 'This law is eternal' (mutawatir), so abrogation would falsify his statement.
This is an argument from authority and transmission.
2
Apply the first Hanafi response
The statement could be a metaphor for long duration, or an announcement that was later abrogated by a higher revelation (Muhammad's prophethood).
Metaphor and abrogation are valid interpretive tools.
3
Apply the second Hanafi response: questioning tawatur
Even if the statement was literal, the Torah's transmission is not mutawatir due to historical disruptions: destruction by Nebuchadnezzar, loss of memorizers, reconstruction by Ezra via a single student.
The author cites multiple versions (Samaritan, Hebrew, Greek) with differing chronologies.
4
Draw the conclusion
Without reliable (mutawatir) transmission, the Torah cannot be used as evidence against naskh. The Hanafi position on naskh stands.
This is a historical-critical argument that undermines the opponent's proof.

الإلهام إليه بنوته الله تعالى لادعائهم أن إلهام التوراة لا يكون إلاّ لابن الله تعالى عما يقول الظالمون، فكيف يعتمد على قول من له هذه الحماقة (ولذا) أي لكونها غير متواترة (لم يزل نسخها الثلاث التي بأيدي العتابية والتي بأيدي السامرية والتي بأيدي النصارى، وقيل: هي السامرية والعبرية واليونانية مختلفة في أعمار (الدنيا في نسخ السامرية زيادة ألف وكثير على ما في العتابية والتي في أيدي النصارى زيادة ألف وثلثمائة سنة، وفيها الوعد بخروج المسيح عليه السلام، وبخروج العربي صاحب الجمل وهو سيد العالم محمد صلاة الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه، وارتفاع تحريم السبت عند خروجهما كذا في «الحاشية» ناقلاً عن I said: No. The remover (is like death) removes this attachment, not that the act itself is raised by abrogation. So where is this from that? If the removal of this attachment is valid, then before existence it was non-existent by original non-existence, so it is not by a remover; and after existence, non-existence by a remover is inconceivable because it would be obtaining what is already obtained, and in the state of existence it would be conjunction of two opposites. I said: This is exactly the doubt of the people of chance and the agreement on the need of the contingent for the effect of the Maker. The answer: Raising after existence is in the state of subsequent non-existence obtained by this raising, and this is not impossible. So understand. And they said fourthly: The first ruling in the knowledge of Allah the Exalted is either perpetual, because His knowledge attaches to its being permanent and eternal, so it cannot be abrogated, otherwise ignorance would follow. Indeed abrogation implies the occurrence of non-existence of the ruling, so the ruling of permanence is false and knowledge of it is ignorance. Or time-limited, because knowledge attaches to its remaining until a specific time, so there is no raising because it is raised by the arrival of that time, so no abrogation. We said: The ruling is time-limited, but to the time that He knows He will abrogate it therein, and that necessitates abrogation and is not an obstacle to it. For if He did not abrogate it therein, it would remain after it, thus ignorance would follow. Yes, if the ruling were time-limited, it would be negated by the arrival of the time without any raising. So ponder. And if the proof were established that the ruling is perpetual in His knowledge, because knowledge attaches to the perpetual ruling, then its raising is invalid, otherwise it would not remain perpetual, so ignorance would follow. Or time-limited, because it attaches to the ruling limited by a time, so it is not abrogated. This answer is not pertinent and returns to the second. And it is answered with the answer that passed of preventing the division and choosing the first and permitting the raising of the known perpetual. So remember. (I say: And you can say in the answer: The ruling is perpetual before abrogation in Allah's knowledge, and non-perpetual after it, and ignorance does not follow, because this is a change, and the change of knowledge with the change of the known does not necessitate ignorance, as in accidents. So understand that it is subtle. Indeed He the Glorious knows happenings: in the state of existence as existent, and in the state of non-existence as non-existent. So His knowledge changes with the change of the known. This is based on what some theologians went to: that the attribute of knowledge is eternal and its attachments are temporal and change according to the change of the known in itself. But there is discussion in it. First: because this basis is false, since it would entail that happenings are not known in eternity, which is bada' and ignorance, as the devils of the Rafida say, may Allah forsake them. Second: even if this basis is granted, it is insufficient. For if the attachment of knowledge to the permanence of the ruling and to abrogation did not continue, this knowledge becomes ignorance absolutely. And if it did not attach to permanence, it returns to the first answer. So understand. Yes, if the proof were established by the previous first formulation, and the answer was established that knowledge attaches to the ruling qualified by permanence, then when this ruling ceases, it attaches to its opposite, the first problem remains. Unless it is said: it attached in eternity to this ruling and its remaining until such a time, then the existence of a contrary ruling, but the expression shies from it. So ponder. The 'Attabiyya said: If the law of Moses is abrogated, his saying, which is mutawatir from him, 'This law is eternal,' becomes false. But this does not indicate the invalidity of abrogation absolutely, but rather the abrogation of Moses' law. We said: We do not concede that it becomes false. Rather it is possible that this was an announcement, then it is abrogated by the rising of the sun of truth, which is the law of the Master of the World. And if it is conceded that it is a report, it is possible that it is a metaphor for long duration, so it is not invalid. If you say: In both there is an adoption of metaphorical meaning which is against the principle. I say: Yes, but here a decisive proof has indicated. Indeed the reports of the message of the Master of the World have been mutawatir from Moses, and that his qibla shifts to the Ka'ba, so there is no meaning for the perpetuity of Moses' law except by one of the two interpretations. So understand. And if the implication is conceded, we do not concede that his statement is impossible to be false. Rather it is fabricated and forged. It was said: Ibn al-Rawandi fabricated it. For the Jews were a slanderous people, they used to fabricate lies against Allah and His messenger, and distort words from their places, so no reliance on their transmission. Tawatur is denied; they only claim tawatur of the killing of Jesus, though it was made ambiguous to them. And how could it not be different? And if he had said it, custom would have required them to argue with it against the Master of the World, as they argued with their other embellishments. And if the argument had occurred, it would have been transmitted due to the ample motives for its transmission, so it is known to be fabricated absolutely. And what they claim that in the Torah: 'Hold fast to the Sabbath as long as the heavens and the earth endure' indicates that the veneration of the Sabbath cannot be abrogated, and you claim its abrogation. It is refuted by the fact that there is no tawatur in the Torah currently in their hands, because their rabbis who transmitted from the time of Jesus did not reach the level of tawatur, rather they were a number who used to gather for distortion. And the people of transmission agree on the burning of its books by the oppressor Nebuchadnezzar when they transgressed and killed a prophet of Allah, said to be Isaiah. So Allah sent this oppressor against them; he killed a third, captured a third, left a third, and burned the books of the Torah and the Bayt al-Maqdis. And that none remained to memorize it because he killed all the memorizers, and there were only very few. And it is mentioned in history that Ezra was inspired with it after Allah caused him to die for a hundred years then raised him. He came and found the city inhabited by Bani Isra'il, asked for the Torah but did not find it with them, so he prayed to Allah to inspire him, and he was answered, indeed a prophet. He wrote it and gave it to his student to read to them. So the transmission became dependent on this student, so where is tawatur? Rather it is said: this student added and subtracted, so no reliance on it. And they attributed to this inspiration sonship to Allah, due to their claim that inspiration of the Torah is only for a son of Allah — exalted is Allah above what the oppressors say. So how can one rely on the word of one who has such foolishness? Therefore, because it is not mutawatir, its three versions have not ceased: that of the 'Attabiyya, that of the Samaritans, and that of the Christians. It is said: they are the Samaritan, Hebrew, and Greek, differing in the ages of the world: in the Samaritan version there is an increase of a thousand and much over what is in the 'Attabiyya version, and in the one in the hands of the Christians there is an increase of a thousand and three hundred years. And in it is the promise of the coming of the Messiah and the coming of the Arab with the camel, who is the Master of the World, Muhammad, and the lifting of the prohibition of the Sabbath at their coming. Thus in the 'Hashiya' quoting from 'Taqrir'. Thus in 'Tahrir'.

Commentary
This passage is part of a defense of the possibility of abrogation (naskh) in Islamic law. The author, commenting on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, addresses a series of objections raised against naskh. First, he refutes the claim that abrogation is impossible because it would require removing an existing ruling, which is like collecting something already obtained. He responds that the removal applies to the subsequent state, not the existing one. Then he takes up the fourth objection: that a ruling in God's eternal knowledge is either perpetual or time-limited, so no abrogation. The author insists the ruling is time-limited to the moment God knows He will abrogate it. The commentator adds a subtle point: God's knowledge changes with the change of the known, though this view is controversial and the commentator ultimately rejects it. Next, the author refutes the argument from the 'Attabiyya (a Jewish sect) that abrogation of Moses' law would falsify his statement that it is eternal. The author suggests this statement could be a metaphor for long duration, or was an announcement later abrogated by Muhammad's prophethood. He further undermines the reliability of the Torah by noting the lack of tawatur, the destruction of the original texts by Nebuchadnezzar, and the reconstruction by Ezra relying on a single student. The existence of multiple variant versions (Samaritan, Hebrew, Greek) with different chronologies further discredits any claim of uncorrupted mutawatir transmission. Thus, the objections to naskh are invalid.

Key Terms
التواتر (al-tawatur): Transmission by such a large number of narrators that collusion on falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a previously enacted legal ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What historical event does the author cite as evidence that the Torah's chain of transmission was broken?
A) The destruction of the Second Temple by the Romans.
B) The burning of Torah scrolls by Nebuchadnezzar and the killing of memorizers.
C) The exile of the Jews to Babylon.
D) The translation of the Torah into Greek.

Key Takeaway
The Torah's transmission is not mutawatir; thus its alleged perpetuity cannot be used as a valid objection against naskh.

Naskh — Abrogation

Proof of Abrogation from the Change of Qibla
Establishes that Islamic law abrogates previous laws using qibla change example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the principle of naskh (abrogation) from the change of qibla and distinguish it from takhsis (restriction).

Core Idea
The change of qibla proves that Islamic law abrogates previous laws, not merely restricts them.

This passage begins by stating that Islamic law (Shari'ah) abrogates previous laws where they differ. An objection is raised: perhaps it only restricts (takhsis) them, not abrogate. The author uses the historical change of the direction of prayer (qibla) as definitive proof. By analyzing the narration from Ma'alim al-Tanzil, we will see how this event demonstrates the legal mechanism of naskh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Source Text
Locate the narration about the change of qibla in the passage. It states that Muslims first prayed towards the Ka'ba in Mecca, then after hijra were commanded to pray towards Jerusalem, and later towards the Ka'ba again.
This narration is the primary evidence for naskh.
2
Classify the Text
Determine the textual category of the command to pray towards Jerusalem after the earlier practice. It is a clear command (amr) that contradicts the earlier practice, indicating a change.
In Hanafi usul, a later command that contradicts an earlier one is a candidate for naskh.
3
Apply Hanafi Principle on Naskh
The principle: when a later command from the same source contradicts an earlier command, the later abrogates the earlier, provided it is of equal or higher authority. Here, both commands are from Allah.
This principle is derived from Quranic verses and established in Hanafi usul.
4
Derive the Ruling
The ruling is that the obligation to face Jerusalem was abrogated and replaced by the obligation to face the Ka'ba. This is naskh, not takhsis.
If it were takhsis, the earlier ruling would still apply to some cases, but here it is entirely replaced.
5
Address the Objection
The opponent claims it is takhsis (restriction). Respond by showing that the new command does not restrict the old one to a subset; it replaces the object of prayer entirely.
Thus the change is a clear example of naskh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن مسألة: (شريعتنا ناسخة للشرائع السابقة) فيما يخالفها (قيل) ليست ناسخة بل (مخصصة) وكان أحكامهن مقيدة (لنا نسخ التوجه إلى البيت المقدس الذي كان في شريعة موسى عليه السلام بإيجاب التوجه إلى الكعبة حين فرضت الصلاة في مكة فإنه روي في معالم التنزيل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وسلم وأصحابه كانوا يصلون بمكة إلى الكعبة فلما هاجر إلى المدينة المعظمة أمره الله تعالى أن يصلي نحو صخرة بيت المقدس، ولم يرد به نسخه بعدما صلى
That the issue: (Our Shari'ah is abrogating for the previous laws) in what contradicts them. It was said: it is not abrogating but restricting (mukhassis) and their rulings were restricted. For us: the abrogation of facing the Bayt al-Maqdis which was in the law of Moses by making facing the Ka'ba obligatory when prayer was made obligatory in Mecca. Indeed it is narrated in Ma'alim al-Tanzil that the Messenger of Allah and his Companions used to pray in Mecca facing the Ka'ba. When he migrated to Medina, Allah commanded him to pray towards the Rock of Bayt al-Maqdis, and it was not intended to abrogate it after he prayed...
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage begins a new argument to prove that Islamic law abrogates previous laws. The author presents the objection that earlier laws are not abrogated but merely restricted by Islam. The proof offered is the change of the qibla (direction of prayer). According to the narration, Muslims originally prayed towards the Ka'ba in Mecca. After the hijra to Medina, they were commanded to pray towards the Rock of Jerusalem (Bayt al-Maqdis). This shift shows that the previous practice (facing Jerusalem) was replaced, i.e., abrogated. The text ends abruptly, but the intended conclusion is clear: the change of qibla is a concrete example of naskh in Islamic law, demonstrating that Islamic rulings can override earlier revelatory commands.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later one, as exemplified by the qibla change.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Restriction of a general ruling to specific cases, as opposed to abrogation which is complete removal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Torah's statement about the Sabbath.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Rational argument about God's knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The change of qibla serves as a clear proof that Islamic law abrogates previous laws, distinguishing naskh from takhsis.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
12 min
Abrogation of Previous Sharias: Naskh vs. Takhsīs
Dispute on naskh vs. takhsīs of previous laws

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that the Sharia of Muhammad abrogates previous sharias and refute the argument that it merely specifies them.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that previous divine laws are abrogated (naskh), not merely specified (takhsīs), supported by mutawātir evidence and practical examples.

A central debate in Usul al-Fiqh is whether the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad (saw) abrogates the laws of previous prophets or merely restricts their applicability until his coming. This passage from Fawātih al-Raḥamūt presents the Hanafi case for naskh, countering the claim of takhsīs (specification). We will walk through the key evidence—change of qibla, Sabbath abrogation, monastic practices—and examine the Hanafi response to the specifiers' argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The central question: Does the Sharia of Muhammad abrogate earlier sharias (naskh) or merely specify that they apply only until his arrival (takhsīs)? This determines whether previous rulings are permanently lifted or suspended.
The difference has practical implications: under naskh, the earlier rule is entirely replaced; under takhsīs, it could theoretically be revived.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The author lists three concrete examples: (1) change of qibla from the Temple to the Ka'ba, (2) abrogation of the Sabbath prohibition (as seen in the Battle of Uhud), (3) replacement of monastic practices (castration and celibacy) with permission to marry. Each shows a clear replacement of a previous ruling.
The qibla change is particularly significant because it occurs within Muhammad's own Sharia, proving that naskh operates even within a single revelation.
3
Analyze the opponent's claim
The specifiers (al-mukhaṣṣiṣa) argue that previous prophets announced the coming of Muhammad, so their laws were inherently limited until his arrival—hence no naskh is needed. They claim the laws are merely 'specified' to that time.
This argument hinges on interpreting the prophecies as restricting the duration of the earlier laws, not as abrogating them.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes that the announcements necessarily imply specification of every ruling; they could be general news. Moreover, if specification meant the laws ended at Muhammad's coming, they would not be binding even after his time, which contradicts their status as divine laws. The Hanafis also attack the authenticity of the current Torah, showing it is not mutawātir and contains contradictions.
The response thus defends naskh as both logically necessary and textually supported.

Like Moses, the first principle/the book, peace be upon him and his family and companions. And if its qibla turns to the Ka'ba, then there is no meaning for the perpetuity of the law of Moses, peace be upon him, except with one of two interpretations, so understand. And if the entailment is granted, i.e., entails the invalidity of this statement, we do not concede that his statement, i.e., the statement of Moses, peace be upon him, so there is no impossibility in its invalidity. Rather, it is fabricated and slanderous. It is said: Ibn al-Rawandi fabricated it, for the Jews were a slanderous people, they used to fabricate lies against Allah and His Messenger and distort words from their places, so there is no reliance on their transmission. And tawatur is denied; they only claim tawatur of the killing of Jesus, peace be upon him, while it was made ambiguous to them. And how could it not be different? And if he, peace be upon him, had said it, custom would have required them to argue with it against the master of the world, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, just as they argued with their other embellishments. And if the argument had occurred, it would have been transmitted due to the abundant motives for its transmission, so it is known that it is absolutely fabricated. And what they claim that in the Torah they adhered to the Sabbath as long as the heavens and the earth endure, this implies that the veneration of the Sabbath cannot be abrogated, and you have claimed its abrogation. So Allah sent this oppressor against them; he killed a third of them, captured a third, and left a third, and he burned the books of the Book of Allah, the Torah, and the Temple. And there remained no one who memorized it because he killed all the memorizers, and there were only very few memorizers. And it is mentioned in history that 'Uzair, peace be upon him, was inspired with it after Allah caused him to die for a hundred years and then resurrected him. He came and found the village inhabited by the Children of Israel, and he asked for the Torah but did not find it with them. So he supplicated Allah to inspire him with it, and his supplication was answered; rather he was a prophet and wrote it and gave it to his student to read it to them. So the transmission came to depend on this student; where is tawatur? Rather it is said: this student added and omitted, so there is no reliance on it. And they attributed to this inspiration his sonship to Allah due to their claim that inspiration of the Torah only occurs for the son of Allah—exalted is Allah above what the wrongdoers say. So how can one rely on the statement of those who have such foolishness? Therefore, because it is not mutawatir, its three versions—the one with the 'Utabiyya, the one with the Samaritans, and the one with the Christians—have not ceased to differ regarding the ages of the world. In the Samaritan version there is an increase of a thousand and much more compared to the 'Utabiyya version, and in the version with the Christians there is an increase of a thousand three hundred years. And in it is the promise of the coming of the Messiah, peace be upon him, and of the coming of the Arab, the owner of the camel, who is the master of the world Muhammad, peace be upon him and his family and companions, and the lifting of the prohibition of the Sabbath at their coming. (It is said) it is not abrogating but specifying, and their rulings were restricted. (We have the abrogation of facing the Temple which was in the law of Moses, peace be upon him, by the obligation of facing the Ka'ba when prayer was prescribed in Mecca. For it is narrated in 'Ma'alim al-Tanzil' that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family and companions, used to pray in Mecca facing the Ka'ba. When he migrated to the honored city, Allah commanded him to pray towards the rock of the Temple. This does not involve abrogation after he prayed towards it for sixteen or seventeen months in Medina after the migration, because it is not relevant at all, since it is an abrogation of what was first revealed in this pure Sharia of facing the Temple. However, Ibn Abi Shayba, Abu Dawud in his 'Nasikh', and al-Bayhaqi in his 'Sunan' narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet used to pray while in Mecca towards the Temple with the Ka'ba in front of him, and after he moved to Medina for sixteen months, then Allah turned him to the Ka'ba. This indicates that both were qibla that must be faced, so it does not harm much. Therefore, one deduces the abrogation of facing the Temple alone by facing both. And the meaning of the tradition is not what was thought that the qibla was the Temple; rather he used to place the Ka'ba in front of him out of veneration for it because it was the qibla of his father Abraham, for this type of veneration is not legislated and does not befit his station, peace be upon him and his family and companions, to be imagined with such, so understand. Then there remains something here: facing the Temple was abrogated in the law of Jesus, peace be upon him, for his qibla is the direction of the East. So the correct approach is to deduce by the abrogation of facing the East by facing the Ka'ba, whether the Ka'ba was in Mecca or facing the Temple, on condition that the Ka'ba be in front of him, according to the different narrations, so understand. And know that the well-known deduction by the matter of the qibla is for the occurrence of abrogation within a single Sharia, and this is valid by the abrogation which is after the migration by sixteen or seventeen months of facing the rock by facing the Ka'ba, so understand. (And) we also have the abrogation of (the prohibition of the Sabbath) by its allowance, and it occurred in the battle of Uhud. (And many) such as the ruling on castration for monasticism and the recommendation of seclusion by abandoning marriage, which were in the law of Jesus, peace be upon him, to prohibition and the recommendation of marriage, and other than that. In summary, the claim of abrogation of some rulings of the previous sharias by his Sharia has been mutawatir from him, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, and the consensus of the Companions has been established upon it, and it is known by tawatur ma'nawi. And upon us is only to resolve the doubts of the opponents. The specifiers said: All of the previous messengers, peace be upon them, informed about the existence of our Prophet, the master of the world, peace be upon him and his family and companions, so their sharias were restricted until the time of his coming. I say: Mentioned news does not necessitate the restriction of all rulings of the previous sharias. Rather, if it necessitates, it only necessitates the non-continuation of a ruling in a general way, and the general does not negate the abrogation of the specific itself, because it did not restrict it and does not negate its continuation and its assumption in the absence of a remover. Otherwise, it would negate the abrogation of the specific and necessitate restriction, then the sharias before us would not be binding because it would necessitate the restriction of all until the time of the coming of the master of the world, peace be upon him and his family and companions, so they would not remain binding afterwards. The conclusion is that this news does not necessitate the restriction of rulings, for it is rationally possible at the time of the news that the Sharia of the Seal of the Prophets would be in agreement with the previous Sharia. Also, it is possible that the news is news of abrogation, so it does not necessitate. Also, if it necessarily restricts until the time of his mission, then the obligation to act upon the previous sharias would be invalidated, and it is not intended that it necessitates general specification in rulings, and that does not negate abrogation. How so, and it is contrary to reality, for the ruling ends by the end of the limit that is now known, and this is not from abrogation at all, so reflect, and reflect well. Issue: Abrogation occurs within a single Sharia and in the Quran, and it is attributed to Abu Muslim al-Jahiz.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute on whether the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad (saw) abrogates (naskh) previous divine laws or merely specifies (takhsīs) them. The author presents the Hanafi/Ash'ari position that naskh is established, then refutes objections. First, he addresses the claim that the Torah contains a command to observe the Sabbath forever. He argues that the current Torah is not mutawatir (mass-transmitted) but was corrupted, burned, and later reconstructed by a single student of 'Uzair, so it cannot prove perpetual obligation. Moreover, the three existing versions differ on ages and include promises of the coming of Muhammad (saw) and the lifting of Sabbath prohibition, which actually supports naskh. Second, he gives the classic example of the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba, showing that previously obligatory orientation to the Temple was abrogated by the new obligation to face the Ka'ba. He clarifies that the Prophet's initial practice in Mecca of facing both the Temple and Ka'ba was not a single qibla but veneration of Abraham's qibla. After Hijra, he prayed towards the Temple for sixteen/seventeen months, then Allah abrogated that by commanding the Ka'ba. This is valid naskh within one Sharia. Third, other examples like the Sabbath prohibition (allowed in Islam, proven by the battle of Uhud on Saturday) and monastic practices (castration and celibacy) were abrogated. Fourth, the author refutes the specifiers' argument that previous prophets' announcements of Muhammad (saw) restricted their laws until his time. He replies: such news does not necessitate specification of every ruling; at most it indicates general limitation, which does not preclude later naskh. Also, the news could be about future abrogation itself. If specification were meant, it would invalidate all previous sharias as binding after his coming, which is not the case. Finally, he notes the general issue that naskh occurs within a single Sharia and in the Quran, attributing denial to Abu Muslim al-Jahiz.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): The lifting of a shar'i ruling by a later shar'i evidence, indicating its cessation or replacement.
التواتر (al-tawātur): A transmission by a numerous group that cannot conspire on a lie, yielding certain knowledge.
المخصصة (al-mukhaṣṣiṣa): The claim that previous sharias were only specified (i.e., their applicability was limited to before the coming of Muhammad) rather than abrogated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which example is NOT used in the passage as evidence for naskh of previous sharias?
A) Change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba
B) Abrogation of the Sabbath prohibition (permission to fight on Saturday)
C) Replacement of monastic celibacy with permission to marry
D) Abrogation of inheritance laws from previous sharias

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes naskh of previous sharias through mutawātir proof, including the change of qibla, Sabbath abrogation, and monastic practices, and rejects the specification (takhsīs) argument as insufficient and contradictory.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Refuting the Restricters' Objection to Naskh Across Sharias
Responding to the claim that previous laws are restricted to before our Prophet's advent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument against the claim that previous prophets' announcements restrict their sharias, and apply the qibla hadith as evidence for naskh within and across sharias.

Core Idea
The announcement of a future prophet does not necessarily restrict all previous laws; naskh remains possible.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, the author defends the Hanafi position that naskh (abrogation) of rulings from previous sharias is valid and occurred. He responds to the 'Mukhasisun' who argue that because all earlier prophets announced the coming of Muhammad (peace be upon him), their sharias were restricted to before his time, leaving no room for naskh. Through textual evidence and rational analysis, the author demonstrates that this claim is unfounded and that naskh is both possible and attested.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponents' claim
What do the Mukhasisun argue regarding the effect of previous prophets announcing the coming of Prophet Muhammad?
Their claim is that such announcements restrict all rulings of previous sharias to before his time, thus naskh is impossible.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence for naskh
What examples does the author provide to demonstrate naskh within one sharia and across sharias?
Examples include the change of qibla (from Bayt al-Maqdis to Ka'ba), the abrogation of Saturday prohibition, and the change in monasticism rulings.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
How does the author refute the claim that the announcement necessitates restriction?
The announcement at most implies general termination, not specific restriction; it could be an announcement of abrogation itself; even if it implies restriction, it only ends obligation, not prevents naskh.
4
Evaluate the logical implications
What would be the consequence if the Mukhasisun's view were accepted?
It would contradict established naskh cases and render many proofs invalid, which is contrary to reality and consensus.
5
Conclude with the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position preferred?
It is supported by textual evidence (hadith, ijma) and rational argument, while the opposing view lacks proof and conflicts with reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنه ليس من الباب في شيء، لأن نسخ لما نزل أولاً في هذه الشريعة المطهرة من التوجه إلى بيت المقدس، إلا أن ابن أبي شيبة وأبا داود في «ناسخه» والبيهقي في سننه» رووا عن ابن عباس أن أن النبي كان يصلي وهو بمكة نحو بيت المقدس والكعبة بين يديه وبعدما تحول إلى المدينة ستة عشر شهراً، ثم صرفه الله تعالى إلى الكعبة، فهذا يدل على أن كليهما كانا قبلة يجب التوجه إليها فلا يضر كثيراً، وحينئذ يستدل بانتساخ التوجه إلى البيت المقدس فقط بالتوجه إليهما وليس معنى الأثر ما ظن أن القبلة بيت المقدس، وإنما كان يجعل الكعبة بين يديه تعظيماً لها لكونها قبلة أبيه إبراهيم لأن هذا النحو من التعظيم غير مشروع لا يليق بجنابه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم التوهم به فافهم. ثم بقي ههنا شيء وهو أن التوجه إلى البيت المقدس انتسخ في شرع عيسى عليه السلام فإن قبلته جهة الشرق، فالأصوب أن يستدل بانتساخ التوجه إلى جهة الشرق بالتوجه إلى الكعبة كانت هي بمكة أو إلى البيت المقدس، بشرط أن تكون الكعبة بين يديه على اختلاف الرواية فافهم. واعلم أن المشهور الاستدلال بأمر القبلة لوقوع النسخ في شريعة واحدة، وهذا يصح بالانتساخ الذي هو بعد الهجرة بستة عشر أو سبعة عشر شهراً للتوجه إلى الصخرة بالتوجه إلى الكعبة فافهم (و) لنا أيضاً نسخ (تحريم السبت) بتحليله وقد وقع غزوة أحد فيه (وكثير) كحل الاختصاء للرهبانية واستحباب العزلة بترك النكاح اللذين كانا في شريعة عيسى عليه السلام إلى الحرمة وسنية النكاح وغير ذلك، وبالجملة قد تواتر عنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام دعوى انتساخ بعض أحكام الشرائع السابقة بشريعته الحنيفية المطهرة البيضاء، وانعقد عليه إجماع الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم وعلم بالتواتر المعنوي وليس علينا إلا حلّ شبه المخالفين. المخصصون قالوا: أخبر (الكل من الرسل السابقين عليهم الصلاة والسلام عن وجود نبينا سيد العالم (صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم فتقيد) شرائعهم إلى زمان مجيئه (أقول) لا يوجب الأخبار المذكور تقييد جميع أحكام الشرائع السابقة، بل إن أوجب فإنما يوجب عدم بقاء حكم ما إجمالاً، والإجمال لا ينافي نسخ الخصوص) بعينه (لأنه) لم يقيده ولا ينافي دوامه وظنه لولا الرافع (وإلا) يكن كذلك، بل ينافي نسخ الخصوص، ويوجب التقييد لم تكن شرائع من قبلنا حجة فإنه يوجب حينئذ تقييد الكل إلى زمان مجيء سيد العالم صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم فلا يبقى حجة بعده، والحاصل أن هذا الأخبار لا يوجب تقييد الأحكام، فإنه يجوز العقل حين الخبر أن تكون شريعة خاتم الرسل موافقة للشريعة السابقة، وأيضاً : يجوز أن يكون الإخبار إخباراً بالانتساخ فلا يوجب، وأيضاً: لو أوجب فإنما يوجب التقييد إلى زمان بعثه ، وحينئذ يبطل وجوب العمل بالشرائع المتقدمة، ولم يرد أنه يوجب التخصيص الإجمالي في الأحكام وهو لا ينافي النسخ، كيف وإنه خلاف الواقع فإنه ينتهي الحكم بانتهاء الغاية التي علمت الآن، وهذا ليس من النسخ في شيء فتدبر) وأحسن التدبر .
For it is not at all relevant, because [the abrogation] of what was revealed first in this pure sharia of facing Bayt al-Maqdis, except that Ibn Abi Shayba, Abu Dawud in his 'Nasikh', and al-Bayhaqi in his 'Sunan' narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet used to pray in Mecca towards Bayt al-Maqdis with the Ka'ba in front of him, and after he moved to Medina for sixteen months, then Allah turned him to the Ka'ba. This indicates that both were a qibla that must be faced, so it does not harm much. Then it is used as evidence for the abrogation of facing Bayt al-Maqdis only by facing both, and the meaning of the narration is not what one thought that the qibla was Bayt al-Maqdis, but rather he used to put the Ka'ba in front of him as a veneration for it because it was the qibla of his father Ibrahim, because this kind of veneration is not legislated and is not befitting his station, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so do not delude. Then there remains something here: that facing Bayt al-Maqdis was abrogated in the sharia of Jesus, peace be upon him, for his qibla is the direction of the east, so the more correct is to use as evidence the abrogation of facing the east by facing the Ka'ba, whether it was in Mecca or [by facing] Bayt al-Maqdis, on condition that the Ka'ba be in front of him according to the difference in narration, so understand. And know that the famous use of the qibla matter as evidence for the occurrence of naskh in one sharia is correct by the abrogation that was after the migration by sixteen or seventeen months of facing the Rock by facing the Ka'ba, so understand. And for us also the abrogation of the prohibition of Saturday by making it permissible, and the Battle of Uhud occurred on it; and many [other examples] like the permissibility of castration for monasticism and the recommendation of seclusion by abandoning marriage, both of which were in the sharia of Jesus, peace be upon him, being [abrogated] to prohibition and the recommendation of marriage, etc. In summary, the claim of abrogation of some rulings of the previous sharias by his pure, white, Hanif sharia has been transmitted mutawatir from him, peace be upon him and his family and companions, and the consensus of the Companions has been established upon it, and it is known by moral tawatur, and we have only to resolve the doubts of the opponents. The restricters said: All of the previous messengers, peace be upon them, informed about the existence of our Prophet, the master of the worlds (may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace), so their sharias are restricted to the time of his coming. I say: The mentioned informing does not necessitate the restriction of all rulings of the previous sharias. Rather, if it necessitates, it only necessitates the non-continuation of a ruling in general, and generality does not contradict the abrogation of a specific [ruling] because it did not restrict it, nor does it contradict its continuation and assumption without a remover. Otherwise, if it were not so, but rather contradicts specific abrogation and necessitates restriction, then the sharias before us would not be a proof, for it would then necessitate the restriction of everything to the time of the coming of the master of the worlds, so no proof would remain after him. The conclusion is that this informing does not necessitate the restriction of rulings, for it is rationally possible at the time of the informing that the sharia of the Seal of the Messengers be in agreement with the previous sharia. Also, it is possible that the informing is an informing of abrogation, so it does not necessitate. Also, if it necessitates, it only necessitates restriction to the time of his mission, and then the obligation to act upon the previous sharias would be invalidated. It is not reported that it necessitates general specification in rulings, and that does not contradict naskh. Moreover, it is contrary to reality, for the ruling ends with the end of the limitation that is now known, and this is not at all a naskh, so reflect and reflect well.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) against the objection of the 'Mukhasisun' (the restricters) who argue that since all previous prophets informed about the advent of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), their sharias were restricted to before his time, and thus there is no abrogation (naskh) across sharias. The author first establishes examples of naskh within one sharia (the qibla change) and across sharias (abrogation of Saturday prohibition, monasticism, etc.) relying on hadith and consensus. He then directly refutes the objection: the informing does not necessarily restrict all rulings; it may only imply general termination, which does not preclude specific abrogation; it could be an announcement of the abrogation itself; and even if it imposes restriction, it only ends the obligation of the previous sharia, not prevent naskh within them. The argument is based on rational possibility and textual evidence, emphasizing that the claim of restriction is not proven and contradicts practical reality where rulings ended with specified terms. The passage is drawn from Fawatih al-Rahamut, a Hanafi usul commentary, and reflects the hanafi methodology of defending naskh across sharias.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: the removal of a legal ruling by a later textual evidence from the Lawgiver.
المخصصون (al-mukhasisun): Those who claim that the previous sharias are all restricted to before the coming of the Prophet Muhammad, thus denying naskh.
التواتر المعنوي (al-tawatur al-ma'nawi): Moral tawatur: knowledge derived from multiple reports that convey a common meaning even if the exact wording varies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to the 'Mukhasisun', what is the effect of previous prophets informing about the coming of Prophet Muhammad?
A) It automatically restricts all previous sharias to before his time, so no naskh occurs.
B) It necessitates that the previous sharias continue unchanged until the Day of Judgment.
C) It at most implies a general termination of rulings, not specific restriction, and does not preclude naskh.
D) It proves that the Islamic sharia is the only valid sharia and previous ones are invalid.

Key Takeaway
The announcement of Prophet Muhammad by previous prophets does not restrict their sharias; naskh of specific rulings within them is possible and proven.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Proofs of Naskh within One Sharia and in the Quran
Usul rule presenting two key examples of naskh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the evidence for naskh in the Quran and sunna, and explain why the Hanafi school considers naskh a legitimate phenomenon.

Core Idea
Naskh is established: the change from 1:10 to 1:2 and from one year to four months proves it.

This lesson examines two concrete examples of abrogation in the Quran, as presented in Fawatih al-Rahamut. These examples answer those who deny naskh and clarify that both abrogated and abrogating verses are true from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The author asserts that naskh occurs within one sharia and in the Quran, contrary to the claim of Abu Muslim al-Jahiz.
The claim is a response to those who deny naskh.
2
Analyze the first evidence: steadfastness
The verse al-Anfal 8:65 originally required one believer to stand against ten; later verse 8:66 lightened it to one against two. A hadith from Bukhari confirms this change.
This shows naskh by a lighter ruling.
3
Analyze the second evidence: 'iddah
Verse al-Baqara 2:240 prescribed a full year 'iddah with bequest; verse 2:234 replaced it with four months and ten days. Inheritance verse 4:12 abrogated the bequest.
Naskh occurs for both the 'iddah duration and the financial provisions.
4
Address objections
Two objections: (a) the year 'iddah might still apply for pregnant women – answer: pregnancy 'iddah is based on delivery; (b) al-Jahiz argues Quran cannot be abrogated – answer: naskh is not falsehood; both verses are true, but the ruling is superseded.
The author refutes both using clear reasoning.
5
Conclude the proof
Both examples conclusively demonstrate naskh in the Quran. The Hanafi position is supported by Quran, authentic hadith, and Companion practice.
The Quran as a whole remains protected; individual rulings can be replaced.

Source Text

مسألة: النسخ واقع في شريعة واحدة وفي القرآن وعزي إلى أبي مسلم الجاحظ) وهذا أحد التأويلات المذكورة لقوله : (لنا نسخ ثبات الواحد للعشرة) عند المقابلة بثبات الواحد للاثنين عندها روى البخاري عن ابن دينار عن ابن عباس قال : لما زلت وإن يَكُن مِّنكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَبِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ وَإِن يَكُن مِّنكُم مِائَةٌ يَغْلِبُوا أَلْفَا [الأنفال : ٦٥] فكتب عليهم أن لا يفرّ واحد من عشرة، وأن لا يفرّ عشرون من مائتين، ثم الآن خفف الله عنكم الآية فكتب أن لا يفرّ مائة من مائتين (و) لنا (نسخ الاعتداد بالحول) قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةُ لِأَزْوَاجِهِم مَّتَلَعًا إِلَى الْحَوْلِ غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٌ فَإِنْ خَرَجْنَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي مَا فَعَلْنَ فِي أَنفُسِهِنَّ مِن مَعْرُوفٍ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٠] (بآية الأشهر) وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فالآية الأولى تفيد وجوب الاعتداد على المتوفى عنها زوجها سنة، والوصية على الزوج بالنفقة والسكني، فننسخ عدة السنة بالعدة بالأشهر والوصية بالميراث . روى البيهقي في «سننه عن ابن عباس في قوله وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ ﴾ الآية . قال : كان الرجل إذا مات وترك امرأته اعتدت في بيته ينفق عليها من ماله ثم أنزل الله : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فهذه عدة المتوفى عنها إلا أن تكون حاملاً فعدتها أن تضع ما في بطنها. وقال في ميراثها : ﴿وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲] فبين ميراث المرأة وترك الوصية والنفقة فإذا بلغن أجلهن فلا جناح عليها أن تتزين وتتصنع وتتعرض للتزويج فذلك المعروف كذا في الدرر المنثورة». وفي صحيح البخاري : قال ابن الزبير : قلت لعثمان : وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة : ٤٣٢] الآية وقد نسختها الآية الأخرى، وهي : ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فلم تكتبها، فقال: يا ابن أخي لا أغير شيئاً من مكانه وهذا إخبار أجل الصحابة بالنسخ وقول الصحابي فيه مقبول فلا يعارضه قول مجاهد إن الآية ثابتة غير منسوخة ومعناه : أن تمام السنة على أربعة أشهر وعشراً إنما هو بالوصية، إن شاءت سكنت في وصيتها وإن شاءت خرجت وهو تأويل قوله تعالى : غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٌ فَإِن خَرَجْنَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٠] فالعدة كما هي واجبة عليها ثم جاء الميراث فنسخ السكنى فتعتد حيث شاءت فلا سكنى لها هذا خلاصة ما في صحيح «البخاري (قيل لا نسلم أن الاعتداد بالسنة منسوخ فإنه قد يعمل به، إذ قد يمكث الحمل وعدة الحامل وضع الحمل والجواب : أن العبرة ههنا للوضع وخصوص السنة لاغ) فليس فيه عمل بالمنسوخ، ولو سلم أن العبرة هناك لخصوص السنة فلا يوجب ذلك بقاء حكم الآية، لأن حكمها كان الاعتداد بالسنة مطلقاً، وهو منسوخ قطعاً. الجاحظ (احتج بقوله تعالى في صفة القرآن : ولا يَأْتِيهِ الْبَطِلُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ ﴾ [فصلت : ٤٢] فلا يبطل شيء منه بالناسخ (قلنا : النسخ ليس بباطل بل المنسوخ والناسخ كلاهما حقان من عند الله تعالى إلا أن العمل بأحدهما ينقطع بالآخر على أن الضمير للمجموع) أي مجموع القرآن والمجموع لا ينتسخ أصلاً فافهم.
Issue: Naskh occurs in one sharia and in the Quran, and it is attributed to Abu Muslim al-Jahiz (his contrary opinion). This is one of the interpretations mentioned for his statement: (We have the abrogation of steadfastness of one against ten) when compared with steadfastness of one against two when it was revealed: 'If there are twenty steadfast among you, they will overcome two hundred, and if there are a hundred among you, they will overcome a thousand' [al-Anfal:65]. So it was written upon them that one should not flee from ten, and twenty should not flee from two hundred. Then He lightened it upon you, so it is written that a hundred should not flee from two hundred. And we have the abrogation of the 'iddah of a year: Allah says: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, a bequest for their wives, provision for one year without expulsion; but if they leave, there is no sin upon you in what they do of themselves in a reasonable manner' [al-Baqara:240] (by the verse of months) which is His saying: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait for themselves four months and ten days' [al-Baqara:234]. The first verse indicates the obligation of 'iddah for the deceased's wife for a year, and a bequest upon the husband for maintenance and housing. So we abrogate the 'iddah of a year by the 'iddah of months, and the bequest by inheritance. Al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan from Ibn Abbas concerning the verse 'And those of you who die...' He said: When a man died and left his wife, she observed 'iddah in his house and was provided for from his wealth. Then Allah revealed: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait for themselves four months and ten days' [al-Baqara:234]. This is the 'iddah for the deceased's wife unless she is pregnant, then her 'iddah is until she gives birth. And He said concerning her inheritance: 'And for them a quarter of what you leave' [al-Nisa:12]. So He clarified the woman's inheritance and abandoned the bequest and maintenance. When they reach their term, there is no sin upon her to adorn herself, make herself attractive, and seek marriage, that is the reasonable [conduct]. As in al-Durar al-Manthur. In Sahih al-Bukhari: Ibn al-Zubayr said: I said to Uthman: 'And those of you who die...' [al-Baqara:240] the verse, and it has been abrogated by the other verse, which is 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait for themselves four months and ten days' [al-Baqara:234], so why do you not write it? He said: O son of my brother, I will not change anything from its place. This is a report of the most knowledgeable of the Companions about abrogation, and the statement of a Companion is acceptable in this, so it is not contradicted by the statement of Mujahid that the verse is established and not abrogated, and its meaning: that the completion of the year to four months and ten days is only by the bequest; if she wishes, she may stay in her bequest, and if she wishes, she may leave. This is an interpretation of His saying 'without expulsion, but if they leave, there is no sin upon you' [al-Baqara:240]. Thus the 'iddah is obligatory upon her as before, then inheritance came and abrogated the housing, so she observes 'iddah wherever she wishes, and she has no housing. This is the summary of what is in Sahih al-Bukhari. (It is said: We do not concede that the 'iddah of a year is abrogated, for it may still be acted upon when the pregnancy lasts long, and the 'iddah of a pregnant woman is until she delivers. The answer: The consideration here is for delivery, and the specificity of a year is irrelevant.) So there is no acting upon the abrogated. Even if we concede that the consideration is for the specificity of a year, that does not necessitate the survival of the ruling of the verse, for its ruling was the 'iddah of a year absolutely, and it is definitively abrogated. Al-Jahiz argued with His saying describing the Quran: 'Falsehood does not approach it from before or from behind' [Fussilat:42], so nothing from it is invalidated by the abrogator. We say: Abrogation is not falsehood; rather, the abrogated and the abrogator are both truth from Allah, except that the action on one is terminated by the other. Moreover, the pronoun refers to the whole, i.e., the entirety of the Quran, and the entirety is not abrogated at all. Understand.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule (usul_rule) that demonstrates the occurrence of naskh within one sharia (Islam) and specifically within the Quran. The author first states the issue (mas'ala) that naskh occurs in one sharia and in the Quran, contrary to the claim of some (like Abu Muslim al-Jahiz). He provides two clear examples: 1) The abrogation of the verse requiring one believer to stand against ten disbelievers (al-Anfal 8:65) to the verse requiring one against two, as narrated in Bukhari from Ibn Abbas, illustrating a practical example of naskh by a lighter ruling. 2) The abrogation of the 'iddah (waiting period) for widows from one year (al-Baqara 2:240) to four months and ten days (al-Baqara 2:234), along with the abrogation of the bequest of maintenance and housing by inheritance shares (al-Nisa 4:12). The author supports this with narrations from al-Bayhaqi and al-Bukhari, including an explicit statement of the Companion Ibn al-Zubayr and Caliph Uthman acknowledging the naskh. He then addresses two objections: first, that the year-long 'iddah might still be applied in case of pregnancy, which he refutes by noting that the pregnancy 'iddah is based on delivery, not the year; second, the objection of al-Jahiz that the Quran cannot be abrogated because it is immune to falsehood. The author responds that naskh is not falsehood but a valid termination of one ruling by another, both being true, and the Quran as a whole remains unchanged. The passage is from Fawatih al-Rahamut, a Hanafi usul commentary, and reflects the Hanafi acceptance of naskh within the Quran and sunna.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: lifting a shari ruling by a later address from the Lawgiver.
الاعتداد بالحول (al-i'tidad bil-hawl): The 'iddah of a full year for a widow, originally prescribed in al-Baqara 2:240.
الناسخ والمنسوخ (al-nasikh wal-mansukh): The abrogating and abrogated texts; both are true but the legal effect of the mansukh is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the 'iddah of a widow who is not pregnant?
A) One full year, as originally prescribed.
B) Four months and ten days, abrogating the year-long 'iddah.
C) Until she remarries, whichever comes first.
D) There is no 'iddah for widows.

Key Takeaway
Naskh is established in the Quran through clear examples, and it does not imply falsehood but a change in applicable ruling.

Naskh Before Ability to Act
Stating a rule about naskh with justification from authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the permissibility of naskh before ability to act and identify the role of i'tiqad (belief) in justifying it.

Core Idea
Naskh is valid before action if belief in the ruling was possible — obligation is about faith, not just deed.

In Hanafi usul, the permissibility of naskh (abrogation) before a person can physically act on a ruling is a debated point. This passage establishes that naskh is allowed as long as belief (i'tiqad) in the ruling was possible. This principle, upheld by the two leading Hanafi imams al-Bazdawi and al-Sarakhsi, emphasizes that the primary purpose of obligation is to test faith, not merely to enforce action. The lesson explores the rationale behind this rule and its implications in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the Arabic statement: 'يجوز النسخ قبل التمكن من الفعل بعد التمكن من الاعتقاد'. Naskh is permissible before ability to act, after ability to believe.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Distinguish between two types of tamakkun
Notice the two conditions: tamakkun min al-fi'l (ability to act) and tamakkun min al-i'tiqad (ability to believe). The rule allows naskh after the latter but before the former.
This distinction is key in Hanafi usul.
3
Recognize the authority: al-Shaykhan
The passage attributes this view to 'al-Shaykhan' — Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. Their agreement gives the rule strong support in the Hanafi school.
Their authority is high, but not absolute; other Hanafis may differ.
4
Address the anticipated objection
The text raises: 'What benefit is there in obligation then naskh before ability to act?' The answer implied by the Hanafi view is that the benefit lies in the belief (i'tiqad) itself — the ruling tests faith even if never acted upon.
This shows the priority of i'tiqad in Hanafi thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (يجوز النسخ قبل التمكن من الفعل بعد التمكن من الاعتقاد) وعليه الشيخان الإمامان فخر الإسلام وشمس الأئمة فإن قلت: فأي فائدة في التكليف ثم النسخ قبل التمكن؟
Issue: (Naskh is permissible before the ability to act, after the ability to believe). Upon this are the two shaykhs, the imams Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma. If you say: What benefit is there in the obligation then naskh before the ability [to act]?
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage states a usul rule: naskh (abrogation) is permissible even before a person has the ability to physically perform the ruling, provided that belief in the ruling was possible. For example, a ruling may be revealed and then abrogated before anyone had a chance to act on it, as long as they could have believed in its obligation. This position is attributed to the two great Hanafi scholars Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) and Shams al-A'imma (al-Sarakhsi). The author anticipates an objection: what benefit is there in imposing an obligation that is then abrogated before anyone can act? The passage leaves the answer to the broader discussion in usul, but the implied benefit is in testing belief and showing divine wisdom. This illustrates the Hanafi acceptance of naskh even in cases where the ruling was never acted upon.

Key Terms
التمكن من الفعل (al-tamakkun min al-fi'l): The ability to physically perform the required act.
الشيخان (al-shaykhan): Two leading Hanafi imams: Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view supported by Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma, when is naskh permissible?
A) Only after the ruling has been acted upon by many people.
B) Only after one has fully performed the required act.
C) Before one is able to act, as long as belief in the ruling was possible.
D) Only if the ruling is physically impossible to perform.

Key Takeaway
Naskh is permissible even before action, as long as belief in the ruling was possible; the focus of obligation is on faith, not just practice.

Naskh — Abrogation
