The Abrogation of the Fighting Ratio: A Quranic Case Study
Providing Quranic example of naskh with Sahaba evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Quranic verses on fighting ratios, explain how the second abrogates the first, and state the Hanafi evidence from Sahaba consensus.

Core Idea
Naskh changes the ruling, not the text: one against ten becomes one against two.

Deniers of naskh claim the Quran cannot be abrogated. The Hanafi response is to present actual Quranic examples. The first is the change in fighting ratios from Surah Anfal, where the initial obligation to stand one against ten was lightened to one against two. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the Sahaba understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Quranic verses
Locate Surah Anfal 8:65 and 8:66. Recognize that 8:65 prescribes one Muslim against ten disbelievers, and 8:66 lightens it to one against two.
Both verses are in the same surah, indicating sequential revelation.
2
Understand the initial ruling
The first verse imposed a strict obligation: flee not from ten. This was a heavy burden requiring exceptional steadfastness.
3
Identify the abrogating verse
Verse 8:66 begins with 'Now has Allah lightened your burden,' explicitly indicating a change. The new ruling is one against two.
The word 'thumma' (then) and 'khaffafa' (lightened) signal naskh.
4
Examine the Sahaba testimony
Ibn Abbas narrates the abrogation, and Uthman's practice of keeping both verses in the Mushaf shows the text remains while the ruling changes.
Uthman refused to remove the earlier verse, confirming the text's preservation.
5
Formulate the Hanafi proof
The combination of Quranic text (8:66) and Sahaba consensus (ijma) establishes naskh. This refutes the Mu'tazili objection based on 41:42.
Naskh is not falsehood; both verses are true, but the later ruling supersedes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول/ الكتاب المعتزلي (خلافه) وهذا أحد التأويلات المذكورة لقوله : (لنا نسخ ثبات الواحد للعشرة) عند المقابلة بثبات الواحد للاثنين عندها روى البخاري عن ابن دينار عن ابن عباس قال : لما زلت وإن يَكُن مِّنكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَبِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ وَإِن يَكُن مِّنكُم مِائَةٌ يَغْلِبُوا أَلْفَا [الأنفال : ٦٥] فكتب عليهم أن لا يفرّ واحد من عشرة، وأن لا يفرّ عشرون من مائتين، ثم الآن خفف الله عنكم الآية فكتب أن لا يفرّ مائة من مائتين (و) لنا (نسخ الاعتداد بالحول) قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةُ لِأَزْوَاجِهِم مَّتَلَعًا إِلَى الْحَوْلِ غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٌ فَإِنْ خَرَجْنَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي مَا فَعَلْنَ فِي أَنفُسِهِنَّ مِن مَعْرُوفٍ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٠] (بآية الأشهر) وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فالآية الأولى تفيد وجوب الاعتداد على المتوفى عنها زوجها سنة، والوصية على الزوج بالنفقة والسكني، فننسخ عدة السنة بالعدة بالأشهر والوصية بالميراث . روى البيهقي في «سننه عن ابن عباس في قوله وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ ﴾ الآية . قال : كان الرجل إذا مات وترك امرأته اعتدت في بيته ينفق عليها من ماله ثم أنزل الله : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فهذه عدة المتوفى عنها إلا أن تكون حاملاً فعدتها أن تضع ما في بطنها. وقال في ميراثها : ﴿وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲] فبين ميراث المرأة وترك الوصية والنفقة فإذا بلغن أجلهن فلا جناح عليها أن تتزين وتتصنع وتتعرض للتزويج فذلك المعروف كذا في الدرر المنثورة». وفي صحيح البخاري : قال ابن الزبير : قلت لعثمان : وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة : ٤٣٢] الآية وقد نسختها الآية الأخرى، وهي : ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فلم تكتبها، فقال: يا ابن أخي لا أغير شيئاً من مكانه وهذا إخبار أجل الصحابة بالنسخ وقول الصحابي فيه مقبول فلا يعارضه قول مجاهد إن الآية ثابتة غير منسوخة ومعناه : أن تمام السنة على أربعة أشهر وعشراً إنما هو بالوصية، إن شاءت سكنت في وصيتها وإن شاءت خرجت وهو تأويل قوله تعالى : غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٌ فَإِن خَرَجْنَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٠] فالعدة كما هي واجبة عليها ثم جاء الميراث فنسخ السكنى فتعتد حيث شاءت فلا سكنى لها هذا خلاصة ما في صحيح «البخاري (قيل لا نسلم أن الاعتداد بالسنة منسوخ فإنه قد يعمل به، إذ قد يمكث الحمل وعدة الحامل وضع الحمل والجواب : أن العبرة ههنا للوضع وخصوص السنة لاغ) فليس فيه عمل بالمنسوخ، ولو سلم أن العبرة هناك لخصوص السنة فلا يوجب ذلك بقاء حكم الآية، لأن حكمها كان الاعتداد بالسنة مطلقاً، وهو منسوخ قطعاً. الجاحظ (احتج بقوله تعالى في صفة القرآن : ولا يَأْتِيهِ الْبَطِلُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ ﴾ [فصلت : ٤٢] فلا يبطل شيء منه بالناسخ (قلنا : النسخ ليس بباطل بل المنسوخ والناسخ كلاهما حقان من عند الله تعالى إلا أن العمل بأحدهما ينقطع بالآخر على أن الضمير للمجموع) أي مجموع القرآن والمجموع لا ينتسخ أصلاً فافهم.
The first source / The Mu'tazili book (its opposition) and this is one of the interpretations mentioned for his statement: (We have abrogation of the firmness of one against ten) when compared to the firmness of one against two; Al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn Dinar from Ibn Abbas: When 'If there be of you twenty steadfast they shall overcome two hundred...' [Anfal 8:65] was revealed, they were required not to flee from ten, nor twenty from two hundred, then Allah lightened it: 'Now has Allah lightened your burden' so they were required not to flee a hundred from two hundred. (And) we have (abrogation of the year-long waiting period) Allah said: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, a bequest for their wives, provision for a year, without expulsion...' [Baqarah 2:240] (with the verse of months) which is: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves four months and ten days' [Baqarah 2:234]. So the first verse indicates the obligation of waiting a year and a bequest of maintenance and housing; so we abrogate the year-long waiting with the months-long waiting and the bequest with inheritance. Al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan from Ibn Abbas regarding the verse: He said: When a man died and left his wife, she would observe waiting in his house with maintenance from his estate; then Allah revealed: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves four months and ten days' [Baqarah 2:234] - this is the waiting for the widow unless she is pregnant, then her waiting is until delivery. And regarding inheritance He said: 'And for them is a quarter of what you leave' [Nisa 4:12]; so He clarified the woman's inheritance and left the bequest and maintenance. Then when they reach their term, there is no sin upon her to adorn herself, prepare herself, and seek marriage - that is the good conduct. So it is in al-Durar al-Manthur. And in Sahih al-Bukhari: Ibn al-Zubayr said: I said to Uthman: The verse [Baqarah 2:240] has been abrogated by the other verse [2:234]; why do you write it? He said: O son of my brother, I will not change anything from its place. This is the report of the greatest of the Companions about abrogation, and the statement of a Companion is accepted; so it is not opposed by the statement of Mujahid that the verse is firm and not abrogated. Its meaning: that the completion of the year to four months and ten is only by the bequest; if she wishes she stays by her bequest, if she wishes she goes out. This is the interpretation of His statement: 'without expulsion, then if they go out there is no sin upon you' [Baqarah 2:240]. So the waiting period is obligatory upon her, then inheritance came and abrogated the housing; so she observes waiting wherever she wishes, and she has no housing. This is the summary of what is in Sahih al-Bukhari. (It is said: we do not accept that the year-long waiting is abrogated because it is still acted upon, for the pregnancy may last and the waiting of a pregnant woman is delivery. The answer: the consideration here is for delivery, and the specificity of the year is null.) So there is no acting upon the abrogated. Even if it is granted that the consideration is the specificity of the year, that does not require the survival of the verse's ruling, because its ruling was the absolute year-long waiting, and that is definitely abrogated. Al-Jahiz argued with His statement describing the Quran: 'Falsehood does not come to it from before it or behind it' [Fussilat 42:42], so nothing from it is invalidated by an abrogator. We said: abrogation is not falsehood; rather the abrogated and the abrogator are both truth from Allah, but the action upon one is terminated by the other. Moreover, the pronoun refers to the whole (i.e., the whole Quran) and the whole is not abrogated at all. So understand.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents two concrete examples of naskh (abrogation) from the Quran to counter the Mu'tazili claim that abrogation is impossible. First, the verse on fighting ratios (Surah Anfal 8:65) initially required one Muslim to stand firm against ten disbelievers, but this was later abrogated by verse 8:66, lightening it to one against two. Second, the waiting period for widows was originally one year with a bequest for maintenance and housing (Surah Baqarah 2:240), but was abrogated by the verse of four months and ten days (2:234) and the inheritance verse (4:12). The author supports this with the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of Uthman, who kept both verses in the Mushaf despite acknowledging abrogation, showing that the text remains but the ruling is changed. The argument of al-Jahiz, who cited Quran 41:42 to deny abrogation, is refuted: naskh does not invalidate the text; both abrogated and abrogating verses are divine truth, only the legal effect shifts.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation – lifting a shar'i ruling by a later shar'i evidence while the text remains.
ثبات الواحد للعشرة (thubat al-wahid li'l-ashara): The ruling that one Muslim must stand firm against ten disbelievers in battle – abrogated later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'Now has Allah lightened your burden' in Surah Anfal 8:66 indicate?
A) The earlier verse was a lie.
B) The earlier ruling is abrogated and replaced.
C) The earlier verse is removed from the Quran.
D) The earlier ruling still applies but is optional.

Key Takeaway
Naskh is demonstrated by Quranic examples like the fighting ratio and affirmed by Sahaba consensus; the text remains, the ruling changes.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
The Abrogation of the Widow's Waiting Period and Refutation of Deniers
Providing second Quranic example of naskh and refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Quran 2:240 was abrogated by 2:234, cite the Sahaba evidence, and refute the Mu'tazili objection using the Hanafi argument.

Core Idea
The one-year waiting period for widows was abrogated to four months and ten days, proving naskh in the Quran.

The second example of naskh in this lesson is the change in the widow's waiting period. The original verse (2:240) prescribed one year with a bequest; it was abrogated by 2:234 and 4:12. This lesson also addresses the objection of al-Jahiz and provides the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting verses
Locate Surah Baqarah 2:240 (one-year waiting with bequest) and 2:234 (four months and ten days). Also note 4:12 which gives inheritance instead of bequest.
Both verses are in Surah al-Baqarah, but 2:234 is later in revelation order.
2
Understand the initial ruling
Verse 2:240 required a year-long waiting period with housing and maintenance from the deceased's estate. This was a heavy obligation on the widow and the family.
The bequest was a separate obligation on the husband.
3
Identify the abrogating ruling
Verse 2:234 reduced the waiting to four months and ten days, and 4:12 gave the widow a fixed inheritance instead of the bequest. The waiting period no longer requires staying in the husband's house; she may go where she wishes.
The abrogation affects both the length and the conditions of waiting.
4
Examine the Sahaba testimony
Ibn Abbas and Uthman both acknowledged the abrogation. Uthman kept both verses in the Mushaf, showing the text remains while the ruling changes. Ibn al-Zubayr questioned Uthman, and Uthman replied he would not change the arrangement.
This is key evidence that naskh does not involve removal of the text.
5
Refute the objection of al-Jahiz
Al-Jahiz argued from 41:42 that naskh is impossible. The Hanafi response: naskh is not falsehood; both verses are true. The pronoun in 41:42 refers to the whole Quran, which as a book is not abrogated.
The refutation preserves the integrity of the Quran while allowing for change in specific rulings.

أنزل الله : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فهذه عدة المتوفى عنها إلا أن تكون حاملاً فعدتها أن تضع وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فلم تكتبها، فقال: يا ابن أخي لا أغير شيئاً من مكانه وهذا إخبار أجل الصحابة بالنسخ وقول الصحابي فيه مقبول فلا يعارضه قول مجاهد إن الآية ثابتة غير منسوخة ومعناه : أن تمام السنة على أربعة أشهر وعشراً إنما هو بالوصية، إن شاءت سكنت في وصيتها وإن شاءت خرجت وهو تأويل قوله تعالى : غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٌ فَإِن المنسوخ والناسخ كلاهما حقان من عند الله تعالى إلا أن العمل بأحدهما ينقطع بالآخر على أن الضمير للمجموع) أي مجموع القرآن والمجموع لا ينتسخ أصلاً فافهم.
The first source / The Mu'tazili book (its opposition) and this is one of the interpretations mentioned for his statement: (We have abrogation of the firmness of one against ten) when compared to the firmness of one against two; Al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn Dinar from Ibn Abbas: When 'If there be of you twenty steadfast they shall overcome two hundred...' [Anfal 8:65] was revealed, they were required not to flee from ten, nor twenty from two hundred, then Allah lightened it: 'Now has Allah lightened your burden' so they were required not to flee a hundred from two hundred. (And) we have (abrogation of the year-long waiting period) Allah said: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, a bequest for their wives, provision for a year, without expulsion...' [Baqarah 2:240] (with the verse of months) which is: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves four months and ten days' [Baqarah 2:234]. So the first verse indicates the obligation of waiting a year and a bequest of maintenance and housing; so we abrogate the year-long waiting with the months-long waiting and the bequest with inheritance. Al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan from Ibn Abbas regarding the verse: He said: When a man died and left his wife, she would observe waiting in his house with maintenance from his estate; then Allah revealed: 'And those of you who die and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves four months and ten days' [Baqarah 2:234] - this is the waiting for the widow unless she is pregnant, then her waiting is until delivery. And regarding inheritance He said: 'And for them is a quarter of what you leave' [Nisa 4:12]; so He clarified the woman's inheritance and left the bequest and maintenance. Then when they reach their term, there is no sin upon her to adorn herself, prepare herself, and seek marriage - that is the good conduct. So it is in al-Durar al-Manthur. And in Sahih al-Bukhari: Ibn al-Zubayr said: I said to Uthman: The verse [Baqarah 2:240] has been abrogated by the other verse [2:234]; why do you write it? He said: O son of my brother, I will not change anything from its place. This is the report of the greatest of the Companions about abrogation, and the statement of a Companion is accepted; so it is not opposed by the statement of Mujahid that the verse is firm and not abrogated. Its meaning: that the completion of the year to four months and ten is only by the bequest; if she wishes she stays by her bequest, if she wishes she goes out. This is the interpretation of His statement: 'without expulsion, then if they go out there is no sin upon you' [Baqarah 2:240]. So the waiting period is obligatory upon her, then inheritance came and abrogated the housing; so she observes waiting wherever she wishes, and she has no housing. This is the summary of what is in Sahih al-Bukhari. (It is said: we do not accept that the year-long waiting is abrogated because it is still acted upon, for the pregnancy may last and the waiting of a pregnant woman is delivery. The answer: the consideration here is for delivery, and the specificity of the year is null.) So there is no acting upon the abrogated. Even if it is granted that the consideration is the specificity of the year, that does not require the survival of the verse's ruling, because its ruling was the absolute year-long waiting, and that is definitely abrogated. Al-Jahiz argued with His statement describing the Quran: 'Falsehood does not come to it from before it or behind it' [Fussilat 42:42], so nothing from it is invalidated by an abrogator. We said: abrogation is not falsehood; rather the abrogated and the abrogator are both truth from Allah, but the action upon one is terminated by the other. Moreover, the pronoun refers to the whole (i.e., the whole Quran) and the whole is not abrogated at all. So understand.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents two concrete examples of naskh (abrogation) from the Quran to counter the Mu'tazili claim that abrogation is impossible. First, the verse on fighting ratios (Surah Anfal 8:65) initially required one Muslim to stand firm against ten disbelievers, but this was later abrogated by verse 8:66, lightening it to one against two. Second, the waiting period for widows was originally one year with a bequest for maintenance and housing (Surah Baqarah 2:240), but was abrogated by the verse of four months and ten days (2:234) and the inheritance verse (4:12). The author supports this with the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of Uthman, who kept both verses in the Mushaf despite acknowledging abrogation, showing that the text remains but the ruling is changed. The argument of al-Jahiz, who cited Quran 41:42 to deny abrogation, is refuted: naskh does not invalidate the text; both abrogated and abrogating verses are divine truth, only the legal effect shifts.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation – lifting a shar'i ruling by a later shar'i evidence while the text remains.
اعتداد بالحول (i'tidad bi'l-hawl): The one-year waiting period for a widow, which was abrogated by the four months and ten days verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the waiting period for a non-pregnant widow after her husband's death?
A) One year with maintenance from the estate
B) Four months and ten days
C) Until she remarries
D) No waiting period is required

Key Takeaway
The widow's waiting period example confirms that naskh occurs in the Quran, and the later ruling governs despite the earlier text remaining.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
12 min
The Ruling on Naskh Before Ability to Act
Defense of naskh before ability with rational proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on naskh before ability to act, identify the key proof (belief), and evaluate the objections and responses as presented in this passage.

Core Idea
Naskh before action is valid because the benefit is belief in the command, not performance.

This passage tackles a core usul dispute: can Allah abrogate a command before any person is able to perform it? The Hanafi school, led by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, affirms this possibility, grounding it in the benefit of belief (i'tiqad) itself. Opponents—including many Mu'tazila, some Hanafis, Hanabila, and al-Sayrafi—argue it is absurd. The text walks through objections, responses, and refutations, ultimately defending the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Recognize that the debate is about naskh qabl al-tamakkun: abrogation of a command before anyone is able to act upon it. The Hanafi position permits it; opponents forbid it.
The key condition is that belief in the command must be possible (al-tamakkun min al-i'tiqad).
2
State the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is that the benefit of the command is not necessarily action; it can be the act of believing in the obligation itself. Belief (i'tiqad) is the head of obedience.
This is a rational argument based on the purpose of taklif.
3
Analyze the first objection and response
The opponent asks: if the command is abrogated before ability, what benefit is there? The response: belief is a benefit. But the text then critiques this response, arguing that if the obligation never truly binds, then belief in it is false, not beneficial.
The author presents the objection and then refines the Hanafi defense.
4
Examine additional objections and refutations
The text presents three further objections (trial of belief, analogy to lying to save a life, other benefits like recitation) and refutes each. Understand the structure of each refutation.
Each refutation shows why the objection fails to prove impossibility.
5
Evaluate the analogy to death
Ibn al-Hajib compared naskh to death, which lifts obligation before ability. The Hanafi response: death lifts obligation because of a rational condition (safety), whereas naskh removes obligation without such a condition. Thus the analogy fails.
This highlights the difference between a condition (shart) and abrogation (naskh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (يجوز النسخ قبل التمكن من الفعل بعد التمكن من الاعتقاد) وعليه الشيخان الإمامان فخر الإسلام وشمس الأئمة فإن قلت: فأي فائدة في التكليف ثم النسخ قبل التمكن؟ قال : (وهو) أي الاعتقاد رأس الطاعات وأساس العبادات وهو حاصل فأي فائدة تكون فوقها، وهذا غير وافٍ عند هذا العبد فإنه هب أن الاعتقاد عمل القلب ورأس الطاعات، لكن إذا كان مطابقاً للواقع وههنا المفروض أن لا وجوب وقت التمكن كيف وهو إن كان حسناً فيه تعلق النهي الناسخ، هذا خلف فلا بد أن يكون قبيحاً، فلا وجوب فيه، وقبله لا وجوب أيضاً، لأن التمكن شرط التكليف والوجوب لا يتعلق إلا بما هو حسن، والنهي لا يتعلق إلا بما هو قبيح في ذاته مع قطع العمل وههنا هذا القبيل فافهم (خلافاً لجمهور المعتزلة وبعض الحنفية بل رؤسائهم كالشيخ الإمام أبي من الحسن الكرخي وشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي والشيخ الإمام الجصاص أبي بكر الرازي والقاضي يلزم من ارتفاعه محال ولا مانع فيجوز) أن ارتفاع التكليف قبل التمكن من المحالات وإن كان ممكناً في الجملة، فإن الإمكان وجوابه لا ينافي استحالة نحو عدمه لاستلزامه محذوراً، وكيف لا يكون محالاً، وإن وجود التكليف ينادي أعلى نداء على حسن الفعل زمان التمكن فيستحيل على الحكيم رفعه، والنهي عما ليس بفحش مستحيل، ودفع بأن المقصود من التكليف الابتلاء بالإيمان به والعزم على الفعل ليصيب به حسنة لا لابتلاء بإيقاع الفعل وهو فاسد، لأن الفعل هل اتصف بالوجوب قبل التمكن وهو تكليف بغير المقدور أو بعد التمكن فلا بد من حسنة فيه كما مر في باب الحاكم، فلا يتصور ارتفاعه، لأن الحسن لا ينهى من الحكيم أو لم يتصف بالوجوب أصلاً، فالابتلاء بالإيمان به ابتلاء بخلاف الواقع وطلب للجهل المركب فافهم. وقد يدفع بأنه يجوز يكون الفعل المنسوخ على حسنه والنهي لغلبة قبح من غيره كالكذب لإنجاء بريء، وهو أيضاً فاسد فإن غلبة جهة القبح هل هي مانعة عن إيجابه؟ فلا يصح به التكليف بالوجوب المنسوخ أم لا ، فلا ينسخ بل يكون من وجه واجباً ومن وجه حراماً، كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة فافهم. وقد يدفع أيضاً بأن المقصود من الخطاب فوائد أخرى متعلقة بالنظم كالقراءة في الصلاة وغيرها، وهذه فوائد عظيمة، وبه يظهر الجواب عن الإشكال المتقدم أيضاً، وهذا في غاية السخافة، فإنا لا ننكر هذه الفوائد ونقول : هل يفيد تعلق التكليف بالفعل فيكون حسناً فلا ينسخ بالنهي عنه، أو لا يفيد تعلق التكليف، فأي شيء ينسخ فافهم (وقياس) الشيخ ابن الحاجب على الموت فإنه رافع للتكليف قبل التمكن فكذا الناسخ (مندفع لأنه مخصص عقلا) فالتكليف مقيد بشرط السلامة، فليس هناك ارتفاع بخلاف النسخ فإن التكليف فيه مطلق، وإلا لم يصح النسخ على أنه بعد مضي بعض الأفراد أفراد الفعل من المكلف الميت، وقد كان الكلام في النسخ قبل التمكن من أحد من المكلفين فافهم والحق في الجواب أن موت
Issue: (It is permissible for abrogation to occur before the ability to act, after the ability to believe) – and upon it are the two shaykhs, the two imams Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma. If you say: What benefit is there in the obligation then abrogation before ability? He said: (It is) i.e., belief is the head of acts of obedience and the foundation of worship, and it is attained, so what benefit is above it? This is insufficient for this servant, for suppose belief is an act of the heart and head of acts of obedience, but if it conforms to reality, and here it is assumed that there is no obligation at the time of ability – how? If it were good, it would be connected to the prohibitory abrogator, this is absurd; so it must be evil, so there is no obligation in it, and before it there is also no obligation, because ability is a condition of obligation, and obligation is only attached to what is good, and prohibition is only attached to what is intrinsically evil, regardless of the coming of the law as explained in the principles of rulings. So if in reality there is no obligation, then belief in it is evil, so it is not obedience, let alone being the head of acts of obedience. From here the corruption of what was established becomes clear – that the purpose may be only belief, not action, and this is such a case, so understand. (Contrary to the majority of the Mu'tazila and some Hanafis, indeed their leaders such as al-Shaykh al-Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, Shaykh al-Imam 'Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, Shaykh al-Imam al-Jassas Abu Bakr al-Razi, and al-Qadi al-Imam Abu Zayd al-Dabusi, may Allah have mercy on them, and their statement is the truth accepted with approval – AND contrary to the majority of the Hanabila and al-Sayrafi from the Shafi'is. (For us: obligation before the act as passed) in the principles of rulings (and it is possible, admitting of lifting, and no impossibility follows from its lifting, and no preventer, so it is permissible). That lifting of obligation before ability from the impossible things, although possible in general, for possibility and its answer do not contradict the impossibility of its non-existence due to necessitating a harm. How can it not be impossible? The existence of obligation calls out loudly for the goodness of the act at the time of ability, so it is impossible for the Wise to lift it, and prohibition of what is not indecent is impossible. (And it is repelled by saying) that the purpose of obligation is the trial of belief in it and resolve to do the act to attain a good deed, not the trial of performing the act, and this is corrupt, because the act: did it come to have obligation before ability (which is obligation of the impossible) or after ability (which requires there be a good deed in it, as passed in the chapter of the Ruler)? So its lifting cannot be imagined, because the good is not prohibited by the Wise. Or it did not come to have obligation at all, so the trial of belief in it is a trial contrary to reality and a seeking of compounded ignorance, so understand. (And it may also be repelled by saying) that it is permissible for the abrogated act to remain good, and the prohibition due to the preponderance of evil from something else, like lying to save an innocent person, and this is also corrupt: for is the preponderance of evil a preventer from making it obligatory? Then obligation of the abrogated act would not be valid, or not, so it would not be abrogated but would be obligatory in one respect and forbidden in another, like prayer in usurped land, so understand. (And it may also be repelled by saying) that the purpose of the address is other benefits related to order, like recitation in prayer and others, and these are great benefits, and with this the answer to the previous problem also appears, but this is extremely flimsy. For we do not deny these benefits; we say: does it bring about the attachment of obligation to the act so that it is good and thus not abrogated by prohibition, or does it not bring about attachment of obligation? Then what is being abrogated? So understand. (And the analogy) of Shaykh Ibn al-Hajib to death, for it lifts obligation before ability, so likewise the abrogator – (is repelled because it is rationally specified). For obligation is conditioned by safety, so there is no lifting there, contrary to abrogation where obligation is absolute. Otherwise abrogation would not be valid. Moreover, it is after some individuals of the act have passed from the deceased obligee, whereas the discussion is about abrogation before ability from any of the obligees. So understand. And the truth in the answer is that death...
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning whether naskh (abrogation) can occur after a command is issued but before any person is able to act upon it (qabl al-tamakkun min al-fi'l). The Hanafi position, upheld by Imams Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, is that it is permissible, provided the ability to believe (al-tamakkun min al-i'tiqad) is present. The author anticipates the objection: What benefit is there in commanding something that is immediately abrogated? The response given is that the benefit is the belief (i'tiqad) itself—the act of believing is a fundamental obedience. However, this response is criticized within the text: if the command is not genuinely obligatory at the time of ability, then believing in its obligation is actually evil, not good. The author then clarifies that the correct Hanafi proof is that taklif (obligation) before the act is possible and can be lifted without impossibility; this is supported by the earlier discussion in the principles of rulings. The text lists the opponents: the majority of Mu'tazila, some Hanafis (including al-Karkhi, al-Maturidi, al-Jassas, al-Dabusi), the majority of Hanabila, and al-Sayrafi from the Shafi'is. A series of objections and refutations follow: (1) the idea that the purpose is merely trial of belief is rejected because it would be trial of false belief; (2) the analogy of lying to save an innocent is rejected because it conflates two different moral aspects; (3) the claim that there are other benefits like recitation is deemed insufficient because it does not attach obligation. Finally, the analogy of Ibn al-Hajib comparing naskh to death is refuted: death lifts obligation due to a condition (safety) being removed, whereas naskh lifts obligation unconditionally. The passage ends abruptly with 'the truth is that death...', likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
النسخ قبل التمكن (al-naskh qabl al-tamakkun): Abrogation of a command before the obliged person is able to perform the act, while belief in the command is possible.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability to perform an act; a condition for the obligation to become fully binding.
الاعتقاد (al-i'tiqad): Belief in the heart; considered an act of obedience and the primary benefit of a command even if abrogated before action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two Hanafi shaykhs (Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma), what is the primary benefit of a command that is abrogated before anyone can act upon it?
A) The reward of the act itself
B) The belief (i'tiqad) in the command
C) The avoidance of sin
D) The test of obedience through action

Key Takeaway
Naskh before ability to act is permissible in the Hanafi school because the benefit of the command lies in the act of belief (i'tiqad), which is possible even if actual performance is not.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
12 min
Naskh Before Tamakkun: Possibility and Proofs
Arguing for the possibility of naskh before ability to act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on naskh before tamakkun, identify the rational proof, and refute the main objections.

Core Idea
Naskh before tamakkun is possible because obligation before action is valid and can be removed without logical impossibility.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut engages a contentious usul issue: can a legal obligation be abrogated before the obligatee has the ability to act? The author defends the permissibility (jawaz) of such abrogation, against opponents including some leading Hanafis and the Mu'tazila. Dense with rational arguments, the text serves as a model of Hanafi usul reasoning on the nature of taklif and its removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule under discussion
Determine the exact question: Is naskh before tamakkun permissible? Recognize that the author defends jawaz.
2
Understand the Hanafi rational proof
The author’s core proof: taklif before the act is possible (mumkin) and admits removal (qabil li al-raf‘), and no impossibility follows from its removal.
This is a dalil aqli, not naqli.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
Three main objection-counter cycles: (1) belief in a non-obligatory act is evil; (2) the act remains good but prohibition due to external evil; (3) the purpose of the address is test/benefits other than obligation.
Follow the 'yudfa‘' markers in the text.
4
Evaluate the analogy to death
Ibn al-Hajib’s analogy: death removes obligation before tamakkun, so should naskh. But the author rejects it because death is a rational specification (takhsis bi al-‘aql) while naskh is legal (takhsis bi al-shar‘).
Also, death does not negate the goodness of the act, unlike an abrogating prohibition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if naskh before tamakkun is impossible, an obligation cannot be abrogated until someone has performed it. The Hanafi view allows abrogation at any time before performance.
Relevant for understanding instances of naskh in the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يصح (قال: (وهو) أي الاعتقاد رأس الطاعات وأساس العبادات وهو حاصل فأي فائدة تكون فوقها، وهذا غير وافٍ عند هذا العبد فإنه هب أن الاعتقاد عمل القلب ورأس الطاعات، لكن إذا كان مطابقاً للواقع وههنا المبادىء الإحكامية (وهو ممكن يقبل الرفع ولا يلزم من ارتفاعه محال ولا مانع فيجوز) أن ارتفاع التكليف قبل التمكن من المحالات وإن كان ممكناً في الجملة، فإن الإمكان وجوابه لا ينافي استحالة نحو عدمه لاستلزامه محذوراً، وكيف لا يكون محالاً، وإن وجود التكليف ينادي أعلى نداء على حسن الفعل زمان التمكن فيستحيل على الحكيم رفعه، والنهي عما ليس بفحش مستحيل، ودفع بأن المقصود من التكليف الابتلاء بالإيمان به والعزم على الفعل ليصيب به حسنة لا لابتلاء بإيقاع الفعل وهو فاسد، لأن الفعل هل اتصف بالوجوب قبل التمكن وهو تكليف بغير المقدور أو بعد التمكن فلا بد من حسنة فيه كما مر في باب الحاكم، فلا يتصور ارتفاعه، لأن الحسن لا ينهى من الحكيم أو لم يتصف بالوجوب أصلاً، فالابتلاء بالإيمان به ابتلاء بخلاف الواقع وطلب للجهل المركب فافهم. وقد يدفع بأنه يجوز يكون الفعل المنسوخ على حسنه والنهي لغلبة قبح من غيره كالكذب لإنجاء بريء، وهو أيضاً فاسد فإن غلبة جهة القبح هل هي مانعة عن إيجابه؟ فلا يصح به التكليف بالوجوب المنسوخ أم لا، فلا ينسخ بل يكون من وجه واجباً ومن وجه حراماً، كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة فافهم. وقد يدفع أيضاً بأن المقصود من الخطاب فوائد أخرى متعلقة بالنظم كالقراءة في الصلاة وغيرها، وهذه فوائد عظيمة، وبه يظهر الجواب عن الإشكال المتقدم أيضاً، وهذا في غاية السخافة، فإنا لا ننكر هذه الفوائد ونقول: هل يفيد تعلق التكليف بالفعل فيكون حسناً فلا ينسخ بالنهي عنه، أو لا يفيد تعلق التكليف، فأي شيء ينسخ فافهم (وقياس) الشيخ ابن الحاجب على الموت فإنه رافع للتكليف قبل التمكن فكذا الناسخ (مندفع لأنه مخصص عقلا) فالتكليف مقيد بشرط السلامة، فليس هناك ارتفاع بخلاف النسخ فإن التكليف فيه مطلق، وإلا لم يصح النسخ على أنه بعد مضي بعض الأفراد أفراد الفعل من المكلف الميت، وقد كان الكلام في النسخ قبل التمكن من أحد من المكلفين فافهم والحق في الجواب أن موت المكلف لا ينافي حسن الفعل بخلاف النهي الناسخ فافترقا ولعل ابن الحاجب لم يقصد القياس بل تمثيل النسخ بالموت في ارتفاع التكليف فتدبر
So it is not valid. He said: 'And it' i.e. belief is the head of acts of obedience and the foundation of worship, and it is present, so what benefit could be above it? And this is not sufficient according to this servant, for suppose that belief is an act of the heart and the head of acts of obedience, but if it corresponds to reality, and here it is assumed that there is no obligation at the time of ability—how so? Because if it were good, the abrogating prohibition would attach to it; this is an impossibility, so it must be evil, so there is no obligation in it. And before it there is also no obligation, because ability is a condition of obligation, and obligation only attaches to what is good, and prohibition only attaches to what is intrinsically evil regardless of the revealed law, as explained in the principles of rulings. So since in reality there is no obligation, belief in it is evil, so it is not an act of obedience, let alone being the head of acts of obedience. From here the corruption of what was established becomes clear: that the purpose may be only belief without action, and this is of that kind—so understand. Contrary to the majority of the Mu'tazila and some Hanafis, indeed their leaders, such as the shaykh imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and the shaykh imam Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and the shaykh imam al-Jassas Abu Bakr al-Razi, and the qadi imam Abu Zayd al-Dabusi—may Allah have mercy on them—and their statement is the truth accepted with approval. And contrary to the majority of the Hanbali school and al-Sayrafi of the Shafi'is. Our proof: Obligation before the act, as previously mentioned in the principles of rulings, is possible and admits of removal, and no impossibility follows from its removal, nor is there any preventer, so it is permissible that the removal of obligation before the ability to act, even if it is possible in general, for possibility and its answer do not negate the impossibility of something like its non-existence due to entailing a contradiction. But how could it not be impossible? For the existence of obligation proclaims loudly the goodness of the act at the time of ability, so it is impossible for the Wise to remove it, and prohibiting what is not obscene is impossible. And it is repelled by [the argument] that the purpose of obligation is to test by believing in it and resolving to act, so that one obtains a good deed, not to test by performing the act. And that is corrupt, because the act either becomes obligatory before ability—which is commanding what is impossible—or after ability, so it must have goodness in it as mentioned in the chapter on the ruler, so its removal is inconceivable, because the good is not prohibited by the Wise; or it does not become obligatory at all, so the test of belief in it is a test contrary to reality and a seeking of compound ignorance—so understand. And it may be repelled by [arguing] that it is permissible for the abrogated act to remain good, and the prohibition is due to the preponderance of evil from something else, like lying to save an innocent person. And that too is corrupt, for the preponderance of the aspect of evil: does it prevent its obligation? Then obligation with the abrogated obligation is not valid, or does it not prevent? Then it is not abrogated, but rather it is wajib in one respect and haram in another, like prayer in usurped land—so understand. And it may also be repelled by [arguing] that the purpose of the address is other benefits related to order, like recitation in prayer and others, and these are great benefits, and by this the answer to the previous objection becomes clear. And this is extremely foolish, for we do not deny these benefits; we ask: does it benefit the attachment of obligation to the act, so that it becomes good and thus is not abrogated by the prohibition? Or does it not benefit the attachment of obligation, so then what is being abrogated?—so understand. And the analogy of shaykh Ibn al-Hajib to death, for it removes obligation before ability, so likewise the abrogator—is repelled because it is rationally specified: obligation is conditioned by safety, so there is no removal there, unlike abrogation, for the obligation there is absolute, otherwise abrogation would not be valid—and that after the passing of some individuals of the act from the deceased obligatee, while the discussion was about abrogation before ability from any of the obligatees—so understand. And the correct answer is that the death of the obligatee does not negate the goodness of the act, unlike the abrogating prohibition, so they differ. Perhaps Ibn al-Hajib did not intend analogy but rather an example of abrogation by death in the removal of obligation, so reflect.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof regarding the permissibility of abrogation (naskh) before the obligatee is able to perform the act (qabl al-tamakkun). The author argues against those who deny this possibility, including the majority of the Mu'tazila and some prominent Hanafis like al-Karkhi, al-Maturidi, al-Jassas, and al-Dabusi, as well as the Hanbalis and al-Sayrafi from the Shafi'is. The core argument is that obligation before the act is possible and can be removed; no impossibility follows. The author refutes various objections: (1) that the purpose of obligation is merely belief and resolve, which is corrupt because belief in a non-obligatory act is evil; (2) that the abrogated act might remain good and the prohibition due to an external evil, like lying to save a life, which fails because the act would be both wajib and haram simultaneously, like prayer in usurped land; (3) that the address has other benefits like order, but this does not prevent the act from being obligatory and thus abrogated. The analogy to death (by Ibn al-Hajib) is rejected because death is a rational specification (the obligation is conditioned on life), whereas abrogation is unconditional. The correct distinction is that death does not imply the act was evil, but an abrogating prohibition does. Thus, naskh before tamakkun is possible.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): رفع الحكم الشرعي بدليل شرعي متأخر
التمكن (al-tamakkun): القدرة على الفعل مع بقاء وقت الأداء
التكليف (al-taklif): خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بفعل المكلف على سبيل الاقتضاء أو التخيير

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the text, what is the Hanafi position regarding naskh before tamakkun?
A) It is impossible because obligation requires ability.
B) It is permissible based on rational reasoning.
C) It is only permissible for prohibitions, not obligations.
D) It is unanimously rejected by all Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that naskh before tamakkun is permissible, based on the rational principle that obligation can exist and be removed before the act.

Naskh — Abrogation

Evidence from Mi'raj for Naskh Before Tamakkun
Using the Isra' and Mi'raj story as proof for naskh before ability to act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of naskh qabl al-tamakkun using the Mi'raj hadith as a dalil and evaluate the objections and responses.

Core Idea
The reduction of fifty prayers before performance shows naskh can occur before ability to act.

This passage presents the first explicit proof for the permissibility of naskh before tamakkun: the Mi'raj hadith. The Hanafi scholars argue that since the obligation of fifty prayers was abrogated before the Prophet (ﷺ) acted upon it, naskh before tamakkun is possible. The passage also addresses key objections, including the Mu'tazila denial of the Mi'raj and the question of whether the Prophet was able to perform the prayers. By working through this proof, you will see how the Hanafi school derives a foundational usul principle from a specific hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and the dalil
The claim is that naskh before tamakkun is permissible. The dalil is the Mi'raj hadith where fifty prayers were reduced to five before the Prophet performed them.
2
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The abrogation occurred before the Prophet acted; thus the ruling was lifted before he could implement it. This is the direct proof that naskh can precede performance.
The key is that the obligation existed for a time but was removed before any individual act of obedience occurred.
3
Analyze the objections
Three objections are raised: (1) Mu'tazila deny the Mi'raj. (2) The abrogation was before ability to believe, not before ability to act. (3) The Prophet was able to perform the fifty prayers, so the abrogation was after tamakkun.
4
Examine the Hanafi responses
Each objection is rebutted: (1) The hadith is mutawatir in meaning. (2) The Prophet's belief suffices for obligation. (3) Though able, he did not perform them before abrogation; the miraculous context shows tamakkun is not negated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(واستدل) على الجواز (أولاً) بنسخ ما زاد على الصلوات الخمس ليلة المعراج فإنه أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ليلة المعراج بخمسين صلاة فرجع إلى موسى عليه السلام فقال: سل التخفيف، فإن أمتك من حماقتهم الكبرى الصحة النقل الصحيحين وغيرهما واشتهاره كالشمس على نصف النهار لكن من لم يجعل الله له نوراً فما له من نور (واعترض عليه بأنه قبل التمكن من (الاعتقاد فهذا كما يضرنا يضركم أيضاً (وأجيب بأن قبل التمكن من الفعل هذا والجواب عن هذا الاستدلال أن التكليف بما زاد على الخمسين لم يتعلق إلا بالنبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وأزواجه وسلم دون الأمة، لأنه لم يبلغ إليهم هو صلى الله عليه وسلم وآله وأصحابه وسلم وقد نسخ بعد المراجعة إلى موسى عليه السلام في الفلك الخامس، فكما أنه كان متمكناً على الاعتقاد كان متمكناً على الإتيان بالخمسين، بل أزيد، فإن قلت: وقت المعراج كان أقل من ساعة كما روي والعروج كان على خرق العادة، ولو كان متمكناً على الفعل فتركه معصية، وهو صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم بريء عنها؛ قلت: كما كان متمكناً على العروج على سبيل خرق العادة كذلك على أداء الخمسين، ومن آمن بقبض الزمان وبسطه لطاعة الأنبياء والأولياء فلا يشك في تمكنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لأداء الخمسين كيف وآحاد الأولياء من أمته قد صلوا ثلثمائة ركعة في بعض الليل ولا عصيان، لأن الوجوب كان موسعاً في اليوم بليلته، إذ ليس في حديث المعراج ما يدل على تعيين الأوقات فافهم، ولا تزل فإنه مزلة (و) استدل: (ثانياً: كل نسخ قبل الفعل لأنه لو لم يكن قبل لكان بعده أو معه وهو باطل لأن الفعل في وقته وبعد وقته يمتنع نسخه إذ لا وجوب حين وجود الفعل وبعده حتى ينسخ ورد أولاً كما أقول غاية ما لزم منه الانتساخ قبل وجود الفعل و(لا يلزم منه قبل التمكن والمدعي هذا دون ذلك (و) رد (ثانياً: الكلام) ههنا (فيما لم يفعل) المكلف شيئاً من الأفراد للفعل وليس كل نسخ كذلك فالاستدلال خارج عن المتنازع فيه، وحاصل هذا الجواب: أنا سلمنا أن المدعي النسخ قبل الفعل وهو غير لازم، فإن المقصود منه القبلية بحيث لم يفعل شيء من أفراده، وهذا غير لازم من الدليل، فقد بان افتراقه من فافهم وتأمل فيه (أقول: لو قيل في تقرير الدليل التكليف بالثاني) في الفعل (تكليف آخر
And he adduced as evidence for permissibility, firstly, the abrogation of what exceeded the five prayers on the night of the Mi'raj, for the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, commanded on the night of Mi'raj fifty prayers. He returned to Moses, peace be upon him, who said: 'Ask for reduction, for your community will not be able to bear it.' So he asked, and ten were reduced. Then he returned, and Moses said likewise, until only five remained. Thus abrogation occurred before the ability to act. If you say: The Mu'tazila deny the Mi'raj, so it is not a proof against them. He said: The Mu'tazila's denial is rejected, for that is one of their great follies, due to its authenticity in the two Sahihs and others, and its widespread knowledge like the sun at midday, but whoever Allah does not give light, he has no light. And an objection was raised: [This happened] before ability to believe, so this harms us as it harms you. And it was answered that the Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, is the origin in obligation, so his belief is like the belief of all. But there is something in this, because it will come that no ruling is established after the address reaches him, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, before he conveys it to the community, so the community did not become obliged by it such that the test of belief would be valid. Rather, the answer is that the point is that the Messenger became obliged by it before the community and believed, then it was abrogated before he was able to act. Similarly, it is permissible for the community to be commanded and the command conveyed to them, then abrogated after belief before ability to act. And the answer to this evidence is that the obligation for what exceeded fifty did not apply except to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, and his family and wives, not to the community, because he did not convey it to them, may Allah bless him and grant him peace and his family and grant them peace. And it was abrogated after returning to Moses, peace be upon him, in the fifth heaven. So just as he was able to believe, he was able to perform the fifty, indeed more. If you say: The time of Mi'raj was less than an hour as narrated, and the ascension was by breaking custom. If he was able to perform the act, then leaving it would be disobedience, and he, blessings and peace of Allah be upon him and his family and grant them peace, is innocent of that. I say: Just as he was able to ascend by breaking custom, similarly he was able to perform the fifty. And whoever believes in the contraction and expansion of time for the obedience of prophets and saints will not doubt his ability, peace and blessings be upon him, to perform the fifty. How, indeed, individuals of the saints of his community have prayed three hundred rak'ahs in part of the night without sin, because the obligation was broad within the day and night, as there is nothing in the hadith of Mi'raj indicating the specification of times—so understand. And do not slip, for it is a slippery place. And he adduced evidence, secondly: Every abrogation is before the act, because if it were not before, it would be after or simultaneous, and that is invalid because the act in its time and after its time cannot be abrogated, as there is no obligation at the time of the act's existence or after it to be abrogated. This was refuted, firstly, as I say: the utmost that follows is abrogation before the existence of the act, and it does not necessarily follow that it is before ability, and the claimant is this without that. And secondly, it was refuted: The discussion here is about what the obligatee has not done any of the individuals of the act, and not every abrogation is like that, so the evidence is outside the disputed matter. The gist of this answer is: we grant that the claimant is abrogation before the act, but it is not necessary, because the intended meaning is priority such that none of its individuals have been done, and this does not necessarily follow from the evidence—so understand and reflect on this. I say: If it were said in formulating the evidence: the obligation of the second [command] is another obligation on the act.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the first explicit proof for the permissibility of naskh before tamakkun, using the well-known story of the Isra' and Mi'raj where fifty daily prayers were eventually reduced to five. The author argues that the abrogation occurred before the Prophet (ﷺ) had the opportunity to perform the fifty prayers (or before the community was able to act). Objections are raised: (1) The Mu'tazila deny the Mi'raj, but their denial is baseless due to the authenticity of the hadith. (2) The abrogation was before the ability to believe, but the answer is that the Prophet's belief suffices, and the obligation was specifically on him, not yet on the community. (3) The Prophet was indeed able to perform the fifty prayers, given the miraculous nature of the event and the contraction of time; hence he was able to act, yet the abrogation occurred before he acted, proving the permissibility. The author also discusses a second proof: every abrogation is before the act, because after the act there is no obligation to abrogate. But this is refuted because the discussion concerns before ability, not merely before the act. The passage ends with a note that the second proof fails to address the core issue.

Key Terms
المعراج (al-Mi'raj): الإسراء بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى السماء وما رأى من الآيات
النسخ قبل التمكن (al-naskh qabl al-tamakkun): رفع الحكم الشرعي قبل أن يتمكن المكلف من الإتيان بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the story of Mi'raj serve as evidence for naskh before tamakkun according to the text?
A) The Prophet was unable to perform the fifty prayers when commanded.
B) The obligation of fifty prayers was abrogated before the Prophet acted upon it.
C) The community was commanded but then the command was lifted before they knew.
D) The Mu'tazila accept the Mi'raj as proof.

Key Takeaway
The Mi'raj hadith provides a key proof that naskh can occur before the obligatee is able to act, as the reduction of prayers occurred before the Prophet performed them.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
15 min
Naskh Before Tamkin: Proofs and Refutations
Presenting three proofs for permissibility and their refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three proofs for the permissibility of naskh before tamkin and evaluate the Hanafi refutations, applying the definition of naskh as bayan al-mudda.

Core Idea
Naskh is a clarification of duration, not a lifting; thus it cannot occur before the capacity to act.

Can a legal ruling be abrogated before the obligated person has a chance to act? This question touches the very nature of naskh. In this passage, the author of Musallam al-Thubut presents three arguments from those who permit naskh before tamkin—based on the Mi'raj event, a logical syllogism, and the command to Ibrahim to sacrifice his son—and then systematically refutes them from the Hanafi perspective. Understanding this debate clarifies whether naskh is a mere lifting of obligation or a clarification of its temporal scope.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dispute's nature
Identify the core question: Is naskh before the mukallaf has the capacity to perform the commanded act permissible? Note the two positions: al-mujawwizun (permitters) and al-mani'un (prohibiters).
The dispute hinges on the definition of naskh itself.
2
Analyze the Mi'raj argument
Read the first proof: the reduction of prayers from fifty to five on the night of Mi'raj, before the Prophet acted on the fifty. Follow the objections and responses, noting the reply that the command was specific to the Prophet and he had capacity due to miraculous circumstances.
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the community was not obligated until conveyed.
3
Evaluate the logical argument
Examine the second proof: a syllogism that naskh must be before the act because after the act there is no obligation. Understand the refutation: it shows naskh before the act's existence, not necessarily before tamkin.
The refutation distinguishes between 'before the act' and 'before capacity'.
4
Examine the Ibrahim argument
Review the third proof: the command to Ibrahim to sacrifice his son, which was abrogated before he performed it. Note the extensive discussion on whether the son was Isma'il or Ishaq. The refutation is that the command was specific to Ibrahim and he had capacity.
This proof is historical; its strength depends on the authenticity of the narrative.
5
Synthesize the definitional conclusion
The passage concludes that if naskh is defined as bayan al-mudda (clarification of duration), it cannot occur before tamkin. Recognize that the dispute is partly verbal: the permitters mean raf' (lifting), the prohibiters mean bayan.
The Hanafi position rests on the conception of naskh as bayan, not raf'.

يعقوب بن إسحاق ذبيح الله» هذا كله خلاصة ما في الدرر المنثورة ، والذي يهدي إلى الذبيح أن الولد ولد بالبشارة بعد العجزة حال الكبر، وقد نص الله تعالى في سورة هود أن المبشر به إسحاق، فوجب كونه ذبيحاً، اللهم إلا أن يقال إن الذبيح إنما بشر به إبراهيم، والذي نص في سورة هود إنما المبشر به لامرأته إسحاق، فيجوز أن تكون البشارتان متغايرتين والذي يرشدك إليه أيضاً القصة الطويلة المروية في صحيح البخاري لبناء الكعبة فإنها تدل دلالة واضحة على أن إبراهيم لم يلق إسماعيل
As in the first principle: The responsible person (mukallaf) does not negate the goodness of an act, unlike the abrogating prohibition, so they differ. Perhaps Ibn al-Hajib did not intend analogy but rather the representation of naskh by death in the lifting of obligation, so ponder in al-Mukhtasar. (He argued) for permissibility (first) by the abrogation of what was added to the five prayers on the night of Mi'raj: Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (saws) was commanded on the night of Mi'raj with fifty prayers. He returned to Musa (as) who said: Ask for alleviation, for your community cannot bear it. So he asked, and ten were reduced, then he returned, and Musa said similarly until five remained. So naskh occurred before the capacity to act. If you say: The Mu'tazila deny Mi'raj, so it is not a proof against them. He said: The Mu'tazila's denial of it is rejected, for that is from their great foolishness, due to the authenticity of transmission in the Sahihayn and others, and its fame like the sun at midday; but whom Allah does not give light, he has no light. (And it was objected) that it was before the capacity for belief, so this harms us as it harms you. (And it was answered) that the Messenger of Allah (saws) is the origin in obligation, so his belief is like the belief of all. But there is something in this, because it will come that a ruling is not established after the address reaches him (saws) before he conveys it to the community, so the community does not become obligated by it so that the test of belief is valid. Rather, the answer is that the intended point is that the Messenger became obligated by it before the community and believed, then it was abrogated before he was able to act. So similarly, it is permissible for the community to be commanded and the command reaches them, then it is abrogated after belief before the capacity to act. And the answer to this proof is that the obligation of what exceeds fifty was only connected to the Prophet (saws), not the community, because he (saws) did not convey it to them, and it was abrogated after the return to Musa (as) in the fifth heaven. So just as he was capable of belief, he was capable of performing the fifty, indeed more. If you say: The time of Mi'raj was less than an hour as narrated, and the ascent was by breaking custom; if he was capable of the act and left it, it would be a sin, and he (saws) is innocent of it. I say: Just as he was capable of the ascent by way of breaking custom, so too was he capable of performing the fifty. And whoever believes in the contraction and expansion of time for the obedience of prophets and saints will not doubt his (saws) capability to perform the fifty. How so, when individual saints of his community have prayed three hundred rak'ahs in part of the night without sin, because the obligation was broad for the day and night, since there is nothing in the hadith of Mi'raj indicating specific times, so understand, and do not slip, for it is a slippery place. (And he argued) second: Every naskh is before the act, because if it were not before, it would be after or with it, which is invalid since the act at its time and after its time cannot be abrogated because there is no obligation at the time of the act and after it to be abrogated. And it was refuted first: As I say, the utmost that follows is that naskh is before the existence of the act, but it does not follow that it is before capacity, and the claimant claims this without that. (And) it was refuted second: The discussion here is about what the mukallaf has not done any individual instances of the act; and not every naskh is like that, so the proof is outside the subject of dispute. The summary of this answer is: We accept that the claimant claims naskh before the act, but it is not necessary, because the intended meaning is that no individual instance has been done, and this is not necessary from the proof, so its difference is clear; so understand and ponder it. (I say: If it were said in explaining the proof: The obligation of the second in the act is another obligation, and therefore one obeys by complying or disobeys by leaving it, so to allow its lifting without the first is arbitrary, while each is before capacity.) And the answer: The obligation in what we are discussing necessitates its goodness, and its naskh necessitates its ugliness, that in one time; and here, since time passes and the mukallaf becomes capable of performing it, there is no blame. So it is good, so it is commanded, and then it becomes ugly, so it is prohibited. So it is not arbitrary, rather it is the most correct, obligatory to accept, so preserve it. (Except if it is said: Naskh according to them is a clarification of the duration of action by the body.) And this is not conceivable before the capacity to act, unlike death, because it is valid to specify the duration for the action. And on this, the dispute is verbal because the permitters intended by naskh before capacity the lifting of the ruling, and the prohibiters intended the clarification of the duration of action by the body. But there is that the author had previously shown that the dispute is whether naskh is a clarification of the duration or a lifting, and building the dispute on the semantic dispute does not necessitate verbality. Its detail is that naskh is a clarification of the estimated duration for the connection of the ruling to the bodily action, so naskh before capacity is not valid since there is no duration to estimate. On this, there is no basis for the verbality of the dispute. If you say: No proof indicates that naskh is a clarification of the term restricted by the ruling. I say: No, it is not indicated, but it is sufficient for reliance, so understand. (And he argued) third: The command to Ibrahim (as) to slaughter his son Isma'il (as) – this is narrated from Imam Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Ibn Umar, Abu Hurayra, Abdullah ibn Salam, Ibn Abbas in the narration of al-Hakim, and it is the saying of al-Sha'bi, Mujahid, al-Hasan, Yusuf ibn Mihran, Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr (or Ishaq, which is the saying of Imam Ali (kmm), narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, and it is held by Ibn Mas'ud as narrated by al-Tabarani and Abd al-Razzaq and al-Hakim who authenticated it, and Jabir ibn Abdullah according to al-Hakim, and Ibn Abbas in the narration of al-Hakim from Ata', and al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib narrated by al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, and it is the saying of Masruq narrated by Ibn Jarir, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr narrated by Ibn Ahmad, and Ka'b al-Ahbar narrated by Abd al-Razzaq and al-Hakim who authenticated it in a long story, and al-Hasan al-Basri in the narration of Ibn Abi Hatim, and Mujahid in the narration of Abd ibn Hamid, and Qatada narrated by Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim, and al-Sha'bi in the narration of Ibn Abi Hatim, and it is the view of the greatest Shaykh, the seal of Muhammadan sainthood, may Allah be pleased with him. It is reported that the People of the Two Books agreed that the text in the Torah states that the sacrifice was Ishaq, but Abdullah ibn Salam refutes that it was Isma'il. And it is narrated in that regard by marfu' hadith through many chains: al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Mas'ud that the Messenger of Allah (saws) said: 'The sacrifice is Ishaq.' And al-Tabarani narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (saws) was asked: Who is the most honorable of people? He said: 'Yusuf ibn Ya'qub ibn Ishaq, the sacrifice of Allah.' This is all a summary of what is in al-Durr al-Manthur. And what guides to the sacrifice is that the child was born by glad tidings after barrenness in old age, and Allah (swt) stated in Surah Hud that the one given glad tidings was Ishaq, so he must be the sacrifice. Unless it is said that the sacrifice was given glad tidings to Ibrahim, and what is stated in Surah Hud is the glad tidings to his wife of Ishaq, so the two glad tidings may be different. What also guides you is the long story narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari about the building of the Ka'bah, for it clearly indicates that Ibrahim did not meet Isma'il.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about whether abrogation (naskh) can occur before the mukallaf has the capacity (tamkin) to perform the commanded act. The text presents three proofs from the proponents of permissibility (al-mujawwizun) and their refutations by the opponents (al-mani'un).

First proof: The abrogation of the fifty prayers on the night of Mi'raj. The Prophet (saws) was commanded with fifty prayers, then after negotiation with Musa (as) they were reduced to five before he could actually perform the fifty. Proponents argue this shows naskh before tamkin. Opponents object that the Prophet (saws) had the capacity to believe the command, which is the first stage, and the reduction occurred before he acted. They also argue that the command was specifically for the Prophet, not the community, and he was capable of performing them given the miraculous nature of Mi'raj. The author discusses various counterpoints, including the nature of the obligation being broad (wasi') for the day, not specific times.

Second proof: A logical argument that every naskh must be before the act because after the act there is no obligation to abrogate. Opponents respond that this only proves naskh before the act's existence, not before the capacity to act. The dispute is refined to specify that the discussion concerns acts of which the mukallaf has not performed any individual instance. Further, the opponents argue that the obligation itself necessitates its goodness, and naskh changes it to ugliness, which can only happen after time passes and capacity is achieved; thus naskh before capacity is impossible. The discussion also touches on whether naskh is a clarification of the duration of the ruling or a lifting (raf'). The author notes that if naskh is merely a clarification of the term, it cannot occur before capacity because no term has been set. However, the author argues that this does not make the dispute merely verbal because the underlying disagreement is about the nature of naskh.

Third proof: The command to Ibrahim (as) to sacrifice his son. This is adduced as an example of naskh before tamkin because Ibrahim had the intention and commitment but the command was abrogated before he performed the act. The text delves into the historical debate about whether the son was Isma'il or Ishaq, citing many Companions, narrators, and later scholars. The author concludes that the evidence points to Ishaq, based on the glad tidings in Surah Hud and other narrations.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that the permissibility of naskh before tamkin depends on whether one defines naskh as a lifting (raf') or a clarification (bayan). The Hanafi position in this text, as represented by the commentators, leans toward the view that naskh is a clarification of the duration, which cannot occur before capacity. However, the final resolution is nuanced, and the author advises careful understanding.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): رفع الحكم الشرعي أو بيان انتهاء مدته
التمكن (al-tamkin): القدرة على الفعل مع وجود المانع أو عدمه
بيان المدة (bayan al-mudda): توضيح الفترة الزمنية التي يستمر فيها الحكم
المجوزون (al-mujawwizun): الذين يجوزون النسخ قبل التمكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the fundamental reason that naskh before tamkin is not permissible?
A) Because naskh can only occur after the act is performed.
B) Because naskh is a clarification of the duration of the ruling, and a duration cannot be set before the mukallaf has the capacity to act.
C) Because the proofs for naskh before tamkin are all weak and inauthentic.
D) Because naskh is a lifting (raf') and lifting before capacity is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of naskh before tamkin hinges on whether naskh is a lifting or a clarification; the Hanafi view treats it as a clarification, making pre-tamkin naskh inconceivable.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
8 min
Ibrahim's Sacrifice: Proof for Naskh Before Tamakkun
Analyzing the story of Ibrahim's sacrifice as proof for naskh before tamakkun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that naskh can occur before tamakkun by analyzing the story of Ibrahim's sacrifice and responding to the four standard objections.

Core Idea
The command was lifted before action; praise without disobedience proves naskh before tamakkun.

This lesson examines the third proof used by Hanafi usul scholars to establish that naskh (abrogation) can occur before the commanded person has the ability (tamakkun) to act. The proof is derived from the Quranic account of Prophet Ibrahim's dream commanding him to sacrifice his son. We will follow the argument, the four objections raised, and the Hanafi responses, including the alternative interpretation that no naskh actually occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the command and its nature
Recognize that Ibrahim's dream is revelation for prophets, so the vision constitutes a genuine divine command to sacrifice his son.
Ruo'ya al-anbiya' wahy
2
Observe the outcome and divine praise
Ibrahim prepared for the sacrifice but did not complete it; yet Allah praised him. This indicates no sin was committed.
Praise despite non-performance
3
Infer the naskh
Since disobedience would have occurred if the obligation remained, but there was no disobedience, the obligation must have been lifted before tamakkun. Thus naskh before tamakkun is proven.
Necessity of naskh
4
Engage with the objections
The passage presents four objections: (1) the dream was not a direct command; (2) only preliminaries were performed; (3) actual slaughter occurred via a miracle; (4) the ransom was the true fulfillment. The Hanafi response refutes each, reinforcing the naskh conclusion.
Four objections and answers
5
Consider the alternative Hanafi reading
Imam Fakhr al-Islam argues that this was not naskh but a test: the original ruling was always the ransom, and the dream was a test of Ibrahim's willingness. This alternative does not undermine the permissibility of naskh before tamakkun.
Hanafi nuance: not naskh but bayan al-mudda

الصفحة، وعلى هذا أيضاً، يتم المطلوب من عدم لزوم جواز النسخ قبل التمكن وما قيل إنه معجزة، فلو كان لنقل ولو بسند ضعیف ساقط، لأنه روى ابن أبي حاتم عن السدي كما في الدرر المنثورة» (و) أورد رابعاً (لو سلم الأمر بالذبح وعدم الامتثال به (فما ترك المأمور به (لأن الفداء بدل) وقد أتى به فقد سقط الوجوب فلا نسخ وهو قول الحنفية قال الإمام فخر الإسلام لم يكن ذلك لنسخ الحكم، بل ذلك الحكم كان ثابتاً، والنسخ هو انتهاء الحكم، ولم يكن، بل كان ثابتاً إلا أن المحل الذي أضيف إليه لم يحله الحكم على طريق الفداء دون النسخ فكان ذلك ابتلاء استقر حكم الأمر عند المخاطب في آخر الحال على أن المبتغى منه في حق العبد أن
