الأصل الأول/ الكتاب وإنما ذبح الكبش خلفاً عنه، وانحصار ارتفاع الوجوب في الإتيان به أو ارتفاعه من الأصل ممنوع، بل وجه ثالث هو إتيان خلفه هذا غاية الكلام الذي حصل لهذا العبد إلى الآن وتأمل فيه. والحق لا يجاوز عن التوجيه الأول فافهم (و) أورد خامساً : (لو سلم) انتساخ الوجوب فالأمر (موسع) فلا يلزم العصيان لأن التأخير كان جائزاً إلى حين التضييق، والنسخ قبله، وإنما يلزم لو كان مضيقاً، فإن قيل المبادرة دليل التضييق قال : (والمبادرة لدفع مظنة المداهنة) من المنافقين سقيمي الاعتقاد لئلا يقولوا هو لا يمتثل أمر الله حباً لابنه، والأولى أن يقال : المبادرة للمسارعة لأداء الواجب، وأجيب بأن الواجب الموسع واجب في كل جزء، ففي وقت الانتساخ كان واجباً، وقد انتسخ، فهو نسخ قبل التمكن، وهو غير واف، فإن الوقت في الموسع إذ قد فضل على الواجب، ففي بعضه الوجوب والتمكن من العمل وفي الآخر النسخ والتحريم، ونحن إنما نمنع الانتساخ قبل التمكن على الفعل أصلاً، فإن قيل : قد مر عن المصنف أن التكليف في كل جزء متجدد قلت : قد أجبنا عنه سابقاً فتذكر (و) أورد سادساً : (لو سلم أنه مضيق فلا نسلم أنه قبل (التمكن لأن الفداء بعد الشروع في الفعل، لكن لم يتم من غير تقصير فتأمل فيه، واعلم أن هذه الإيرادات أكثرها متباينة بالسند ويدفع الثلاثة الأول بالفداء) فإن الفداء يقتضي سبق الوجوب فيندفع الأولان، وكذا يقتضي عدم وقوع المفدي عنه، وقد يدفع الأول بقول الابن عليه السلام ﴿يَابَتِ افْعَلْ مَا تُؤْمَرُ ﴾ [الصافات: ۱۰۲] واعلم أن الإيراد الأول هو الحق المتلقى بالقبول واجب الإطاعة والإذعان، وقد مر تقريره في تقريره في أثناء تقرير كلام الإمام فخر الإسلام، والآن نزيدك إيضاحاً فنقول رأى إبراهيم عليه وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام في المنام أن يذبح ابنه ، وهذا المنام كان معبراً البتة وإلا لوقع الذبح، فإنه رأى الذبح منه واقعاً لا أنه رأى أنه يؤمر به فعرض على الابن طلباً للمشورة فقال : إِنِّي أَرَى فِي الْمَنَامِ أَنِّي أَذْبَحُكَ فَانظُرْ مَاذَا تَرَى [الصافات: ۱۰۲] فظنه الابن أمراً بناءً على أن رؤيا الأنبياء وحي، أو على أمر آخر فقد أصاب في ظنه أمراً لكن أخطأ في ظنه أمراً بذبح الولد كما يخطىء المجتهد في الاجتهاد، فقال: ﴿يَابَتِ افْعَلْ مَا تُؤْمَرُ سَتَجِدُنِي إِن شَاءَ اللهُ مِنَ الصَّبِرِينَ وتقرر هذا في رأي إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام كما كان غالباً على عادته حينئذ عدم كون رؤياه معبرة، ولما وصل اجتهاده إليه وجب الامتثال إلى أن يظهر الخطأ فهم بالذبح فلم ينقطع حلقومه إما بصفيحة ضربت كما قيل أو بغيره، ولا تصغ إلى قول من يقول إن الأنبياء كيف يخطئون في أحكام الله تعالى؟ فإن هذا القول قد صدر من شياطين أهل البدع كالروافض ،وغيرهم، ألم تر أهل الحق من أهل السنة والجماعة القامعين للبدعة كثرهم الله تعالى يجوزون على الأنبياء الخطأ ، كما ظهر في أسارى بدر من سيد العالم صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه أجمعين كيف وقد وقع من داود عليه السلام في الحرث وفي الحكم لإحدى المرأتين مع كونه الأخرى كما هو مشروح في الصحيحين، كيف وقد وقع من موسى عليه السلام حين فعل بأخيه هارون عليه السلام ما فعل وحين قال لمن سأل : هل أحد أعلم منك؟ لا أحد أعلم مني، فأوحى الله تعالى بل عبدنا خضر، كما أخرجه الشيخان، وكيف لا وقع النوح عليه السلام حيث سأل نجاة ابنه من الغرق على ما هو المشهور، ثم إن في إراءة الرؤيا على هذا الوجه وعدم الإعلام بالتعبير ابتلاء عظيماً لهما عليهما السلام ونيل المرتبة الرفيعة، لكن لما لم يكن الأنبياء مقرين على الخطأ أعلمه الله تعالى وناداه : أَن يَابْرَاهِيمُ قَدْ صَدَّقْتَ الرُّؤْيَا ﴾ [الصافات : ۱۰۵] واختار صيغة التفعيل ولم يقل : صدقت في الرؤيا لأنه لم يصدق فيه، وإنما صدقه أن هذا لهو البلاء المبين وأرسل الذبح العظيم وسماه فداء على حسب ظن إبراهيم، وإلا كان هذا أصل الواجب وفي هذا الخطأ والعزم على ذبح الولد سر آخر مذکور في شرح فصوص الحكم للشيخ الغلام السامي عبد الرحمن الجامي قدس سره فليطلب منه ، ولنذكر من كلام الشيخ الأكبر تبركاً، قال رضي الله عنه في فصوص الحكم : اعلم أيدنا الله وإياك أن إبراهيم الخليل عليه السلام قال لابنه : إِنّ أَرَى فِي الْمَنَاءِ اَنّي أَذْبَحُكَ ﴾ [الصافات: ١٠٢] والمنام حضرة الخيال فلم يعبرها، وكان كبشاً ظهر في صورة ابن إبراهيم في المثال، فصدق إبراهيم الرؤيا، ففداه ربه من وهم إبراهيم بالذبح العظيم وهو تعبير رؤياه عند الله وهو يشعر بالتجلي الصوري في حضرة الخيال محتاج إلى علم آخر يدرك به ما أراد الله بتلك الصورة، ألا ترى كيف قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم لأمير المؤمنين أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه في تعبير الرؤيا: أصبت بعضاً وأخطأت بعضاً فسأله أبو بكر أن يعرفه ما أصاب منه وما أخطأ فلم يفعل عليه السلام قال تعالى لإبراهيم حين ناداه : هو أن يتك ابراهيمُ قَدْ صَدَّقْتَ الرُّؤْيَا ﴾ [الصافات: ١٠٤، ١٠٥] وما قال قد صدقت في الرؤيا لأنه ابنك لأنه ما عبرها، بل أخذ بظاهر ما رأى والرؤيا تطلب التعبير انتهى كلماته الشريفة.
The first principle: The book. Rather, he slaughtered the ram as a substitute for him. The restriction of the lifting of obligation to performing it or lifting it from the origin is denied. Rather, there is a third aspect: performing a substitute. This is the utmost discourse that has occurred to this servant until now; reflect on it. The truth does not go beyond the first direction, so understand. And a fifth objection was raised: If the abrogation of obligation is granted, the command is broad, so disobedience does not necessarily follow because delay was permissible until the time of restriction, and abrogation before it. Disobedience would follow only if it were restricted. If it is said: Haste is evidence of restriction, he said: And haste is to repel the suspicion of hypocrisy from the weak of belief, lest they say he does not comply with God's command due to love for his son. It is better to say: Haste is to rush to perform the obligation. It was answered: The broad obligation is obligatory in every part, so at the time of abrogation it was obligatory, and it was abrogated, so it is abrogation before ability, and it is insufficient. For the time in the broad [obligation] is in excess of the obligation, so in some of it there is obligation and ability, and in the other abrogation and prohibition. We only deny abrogation before ability on the act entirely. If it is said: The author has stated that the obligation is renewed in every part, I say: We have answered that earlier, so remember. And a sixth objection was raised: If granted that it is restricted, we do not grant that it is before ability because the ransom after beginning the act, but it was not completed without negligence, so reflect on it. Know that most of these objections are diverse in basis, and the first three are repelled by the ransom, for the ransom implies priority of obligation, thus the first two are repelled, and likewise it implies the non-occurrence of the ransomed thing. And the first may be repelled by the son's statement, peace be upon him: 'O my father, do as you are commanded' (Surah al-Saffat: 102). Know that the first objection is the truth accepted with acceptance, obligatory to obey and submit. Its determination has passed in the course of the discourse of Imam Fakhr al-Islam, and now we add clarification: We say: Ibrahim, peace be upon him and upon our Prophet and his family and companions, saw in a dream that he slaughters his son. This dream was definitely interpretable, otherwise the slaughter would have occurred. For he saw the slaughter occurring from him, not that he saw he was commanded to do it. So he presented it to his son seeking counsel: 'I see in a dream that I slaughter you, so consider what you see' (al-Saffat: 102). The son thought it a command based on the fact that the dreams of prophets are revelation, or on another matter. He was correct in his assumption of a command but mistaken in his assumption of a command to slaughter the son, as a mujtahid errs in ijtihad. So he said: 'O my father, do as you are commanded; you will find me, if God wills, among the patient.' And this was established in the view of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, as was prevalent in his custom at that time: his dream not being interpretative. When his ijtihad reached that conclusion, compliance became obligatory until the error became apparent. So he intended to slaughter, but his throat was not cut, either by a copper sheet as was said or otherwise. Do not listen to those who say: How can prophets err in the rulings of God? For this statement came from the devils of the innovators like the Rawafid and others. Do you not see that the people of truth from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, the suppressors of innovation, may God multiply them, allow error from prophets, as appeared in the captives of Badr from the Master of the Worlds, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions and all his wives? How, and it occurred from Dawud, peace be upon him, regarding the crop and in the judgment for one of the two women while the other was the case, as detailed in the Sahihs? How, and it occurred from Musa, peace be upon him, when he did to his brother Harun what he did, and when he said to the one who asked: Is there anyone more knowledgeable than you? No one is more knowledgeable than me. So God revealed: Yes, Our servant al-Khidr, as narrated by the two Shaykhs. How, and it occurred from Nuh, peace be upon him, when he asked for his son's salvation from drowning as is well-known. Then in showing the dream in this manner and not informing of the interpretation, there was a great trial for both of them, peace be upon them, and attaining a high station. But since prophets are not settled upon error, God informed him and called out: 'O Ibrahim, you have confirmed the dream' (al-Saffat: 105). He chose the intensive form and did not say: 'You were truthful in the dream' because he was not truthful in it. Rather, his confirmation was that 'this is indeed a manifest trial' and He sent a great slaughter and called it a ransom according to Ibrahim's assumption. Otherwise, this was the original obligation. In this error and resolve to slaughter the son, there is another secret mentioned in Sharh Fusus al-Hikam by al-Shaykh al-Ghulam al-Sami 'Abd al-Rahman al-Jami, may God sanctify his secret. Let it be sought from there. And let us mention from the speech of the Greatest Shaykh for blessing. He said, may God be pleased with him, in Fusus al-Hikam: Know, may God support us and you, that Ibrahim al-Khalil, peace be upon him, said to his son: 'I see in a dream that I slaughter you' (al-Saffat: 102). And the dream is the realm of imagination, so he did not interpret it. It was a ram appearing in the form of Ibrahim's son in the image. So Ibrahim confirmed the dream, so his Lord ransomed him from Ibrahim's illusion with a great slaughter, and that is the interpretation of his dream with God. It indicates that a pictorial manifestation in the realm of imagination requires another science to understand what God intended by that form. Do you not see how the Messenger of God, peace be upon him and his family and companions, said to the Commander of the Faithful Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him, about dream interpretation: 'You got some right and some wrong.' So Abu Bakr asked him to tell him what he got right and what he got wrong, but he did not do so, peace be upon him. God said to Ibrahim when He called out: 'O Ibrahim, you have confirmed the dream' (al-Saffat: 104-105), and He did not say: 'You were truthful in the dream' because it was his son, because he did not interpret it. Rather, he took the outward meaning of what he saw, and the dream requires interpretation. End of his blessed words.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul analysis defending the possibility of abrogation (naskh) before one is able to act (qabl al-tamakkun). The author, a commentator on 'Muslim al-Thubut', addresses objections raised against this position. He first discusses the story of Prophet Ibrahim's sacrifice as a case study. The objection was that if naskh before ability were allowed, then the sacrifice story would show it, but the story actually demonstrates an error in ijtihad (ijtihad error), not naskh. The author explains that Ibrahim saw a dream and thought it was a command, but it required interpretation. His son's response 'do as you are commanded' shows he assumed it was a command. The actual command was to sacrifice a ram, not his son. So the obligation was never truly present for the son's sacrifice. This shows that the apparent obligation was based on a mistaken ijtihad, not a real obligation that was later abrogated. Thus, the story does not support the objection. The author also defends the possibility of prophets erring in ijtihad, citing examples from the Quran and Hadith. He then quotes from Ibn al-'Arabi and al-Jami to reinforce the point that the dream required interpretation.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability or capacity to perform an act.
الفداء (al-fida'): Ransom or substitution, as with the ram for Ishmael.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis, why does the story of Ibrahim's sacrifice not refute the principle of naskh before tamakkun?
A) Because the command was not abrogated but was never obligatory in the first place.
B) Because Ibrahim was not a prophet.
C) Because the abrogation occurred after the act was complete.
D) Because the dream was from Satan.

Key Takeaway
The story of Ibrahim's sacrifice is reinterpreted by Hanafi usul scholars as an example of ijtihad error, not as a case of naskh before tamakkun.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Naskh Before Tamakkun: Defending Against the Charge of Contradiction
Refuting the argument that naskh before tamakkun entails simultaneous command and prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi response to the objection that naskh before tamakkun entails simultaneous command and prohibition, and apply the time-distinction argument to resolve the apparent contradiction.

Core Idea
Naskh before tamakkun does not create contradiction because the abrogated ruling is lifted before the time of ability.

A key objection raised against the possibility of naskh (abrogation) before the obligated person is able to act (tamakkun) is that it would force a single act to be both commanded and prohibited at the same time. The Hanafi school rejects this objection, arguing that the two rulings never coexist in the same time frame. In this lesson, we unpack the logical reasoning that resolves the apparent contradiction, focusing on the distinction between the time of obligation and the time of ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Recognize the opponent's claim: if naskh occurs before tamakkun, then at the moment of ability the same person would be simultaneously commanded (by the abrogated command) and prohibited (by the abrogator). This is logically impossible (taklif ma la yutaq).
2
Examine the Hanafi initial response
Understand the first part of the Hanafi answer: the two rulings do not coexist because the abrogated command is lifted (raf') by the abrogator before the time of ability, or the attachment of the rulings occurs at different times.
The text says: 'There is no coexistence in the obligation... Rather, one is lifted by the other.'
3
Analyze the two scenarios of obligation attachment
Consider whether the obligation attaches to the abrogated command at the time of ability or not. If it does not attach (scenario 2), then there is no obligation to begin with, so no naskh. If it attaches (scenario 1), then the act becomes wajib in the dhimma and later forbidden at the same time – this seems problematic, but the resolution lies in the time of obligation being distinct from the time of prohibition.
The author distinguishes between the time of obligation (prior to ability) and the time of ability (when prohibition arises).
4
Refute the 'intention of the heart' counter-argument
The opponent might suggest that the abrogated command was only for intending the act in the heart ('aqd al-qalb), not actual performance. The Hanafi reply shows that if there was obligation, the problem returns; if no obligation, then the intention is based on false assumption, leading to compound ignorance.
This shows the absurdity of the counter-proposal.
5
Apply the time multiplicity argument
Conclude with the key principle: in non-disputed cases, the time of obligation and the time of prohibition are multiple (e.g., a command binding for a specific period that is later abrogated). The abrogation merely clarifies the term (bayan al-amad), so no contradiction arises.
This argument works for all cases of naskh, not just the disputed one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنكرون للنسخ قبل التمكن (قالوا) لو جاز النسخ لزم صيرورة الشخص الواحد حال التمكن مأموراً ومنهياً والمكلف الواحد) بالواحد من الفعل في الواحد من الزمان (لا يؤمر ولا ينهى عنه (قلنا : لا معية في التكليف لحكم المنسوخ والناسخ ولا) في التعلق أي تعلق الحكمين به (بل يرفع أحدهما الآخر فلا يلزم صيرورة شيء واحد مأموراً ومنهياً في زمان واحد، وقد مر منا ما يفي لدفع هذا الجواب ولا بأس بالإعادة ليزداد وضوحاً فاعلم أنه تعلق التكليف وقت التمكن بالأمر المنسوخ أم لا وعلى الثاني لا تكليف، فلا ينسخ إذ لا تكليف قبل التمكن، لأنه شرط التكليف، وعلى الأول صار الفعل واجباً في الذمة ثم صار حراماً في ذلك الوقت أيضاً بالناسخ فلزم اجتماعهما قطعاً، فإن قيل المقصود من أمر المنسوخ الإتيان بعقد القلب وبالنهي الكف عنه وقت التمكن ؟ قلت : عقد القلب بأي شيء إن كان هناك وجوب فيلزم المحذور قهقرى، وإن لم يكن هناك وجوب صار المقصود عقد القلب خلاف الواقع والمطلوب جهلاً مركباً فتدبر ولا تغلط قيل : هذا الدليل منقوض بجميع صور (النسخ) فإنه يلزم أن يكون شيء واحد مأموراً بالمنسوخ ومنهياً بالناسخ (أقول) الانتقاض (ممنوع، فإن الوقت في غير محل النزاع متعدد فيصح أن يبقى الوجوب بالأمر المنسوخ إلى أمد ويكون النسخ بيانه (فيصح بيان الأمد فتأمل ولك أن تطرح حديث بيان الأمد من البين وتقول : لما كان الوقت في غير محل النزاع متعدّداً فيجوز تعلق الوجوب به في وقت وارتفاعه في وقت آخر فلا محذور أصلاً سواء من
Those who deny abrogation before ability said: If abrogation were permitted, it would necessitate that a single person at the time of ability is both commanded and prohibited, and a single obligated person with respect to a single act in a single time is neither commanded nor prohibited. We said: There is no coexistence in the obligation for the abrogated and abrogating rulings, nor in the attachment, i.e., the attachment of both rulings to it. Rather, one (the abrogated) is lifted by the other, so it does not necessitate a single thing being commanded and prohibited in a single time. We have already said what suffices to repel this answer, but it is good to repeat for clarity. Know that the obligation at the time of ability either attaches to the abrogated command or not. In the second case, there is no obligation, so there is no abrogation since there is no obligation before ability, because it is a condition for obligation. In the first case, the act becomes obligatory in the liability, then it becomes forbidden in that same time by the abrogator, so their coexistence is certain. If it is said: The purpose of the abrogated command is to bring about an intention of the heart, and by the prohibition to refrain from it at the time of ability? I say: Intention of the heart by what? If there is obligation, then the problem returns; if there is no obligation, then the purpose becomes intention contrary to reality, which is compound ignorance. So reflect and do not err. It was said: This argument is refutable by all cases of abrogation, for it would necessitate that a single thing be commanded by the abrogated and prohibited by the abrogator. I say: The refutation is denied. For the time in other than the disputed case is multiple, so it is valid for the obligation to remain with the abrogated command until a term, and the abrogation is its clarification. Thus, clarifying the term is valid. Reflect. You may also discard the talk of clarifying the term altogether and say: Since the time in other than the disputed case is multiple, it is permissible for the obligation to attach to it at one time and be lifted at another time; there is no problem at all, whether from...
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage continues the Hanafi defense of naskh before tamakkun by addressing a logical objection. The objectors argue that if naskh occurs before one is able to act, then at the moment of ability the same person would be both commanded (by the abrogated command) and prohibited (by the abrogator), which is impossible. The Hanafi response is twofold: First, there is no simultaneous existence of both rulings; the abrogated ruling is lifted by the abrogator, so at any given time only one applies. Second, the time of obligation and ability may be different periods. If the obligation attaches at a time prior to ability, then when ability arrives, the command may have already been abrogated, so no conflict. The author also refutes a counter-argument that the intention of the heart would be problematic. He concludes that the time factor resolves the apparent contradiction.

Key Terms
المكلف الواحد (al-mukallaf al-wahid): A single legally responsible person.
عقد القلب (aqd al-qalb): The intention or determination of the heart to perform an act.
بيان الأمد (bayan al-amad): Clarification of the term or duration of an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main Hanafi response to the objection that naskh before tamakkun leads to simultaneous command and prohibition?
A) The abrogated command was never truly obligatory.
B) The abrogated command is lifted before the time of ability, so no coexistence occurs.
C) The same act can be both obligatory and forbidden without contradiction.
D) The intention of the heart resolves the issue.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends naskh before tamakkun by arguing that the abrogated ruling is lifted before the time of ability, thereby avoiding any logical contradiction of simultaneous command and prohibition.

The Impermissibility of Naskh Before Tamakkun: A Rational Proof
Rational argument against naskh before tamakkun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits abrogation of a ruling before the obligated person has capability (tamakkun) and evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
Abrogating a ruling before one can act creates impossible simultaneous command and prohibition.

This usul al-fiqh lesson examines a rational proof (dalil aqli) concerning naskh (abrogation). The question is whether a Shari'ah ruling can be abrogated before the obligated person has the ability (tamakkun) to act upon it. The Hanafi muhaqqiqeen hold that it is impermissible, because it would entail contradictory commands at the same moment. The passage presents a layered argument, with objections and responses, ultimately affirming the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: naskh before tamakkun is not permissible. This is the position of most Hanafi muhaqqiqeen.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that some scholars permit it. Their proof: the time is multiple, so the abrogated ruling applies until a term and the abrogating applies later, avoiding contradiction.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: in the specific case of naskh before tamakkun, the time of capability is single, so obligation and prohibition would coincide. The multiple-time argument fails here.
The passage also considers a deeper objection about intention (عقد القلب) vs. action.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a ruling is revealed and then abrogated before anyone can act, according to Hanafis it is not valid abrogation; the ruling is considered never applicable.
5
Reflect on the rational basis
Understand that the proof is based on logical impossibility (societal impossibility of simultaneous command and prohibition) not merely textual evidence.

Source Text

المنكرون للنسخ قبل التمكن (قالوا) لو جاز النسخ لزم صيرورة الشخص الواحد حال التمكن مأموراً ومنهياً والمكلف الواحد) بالواحد من الفعل في الواحد من الزمان (لا يؤمر ولا ينهى عنه (قلنا : لا معية في التكليف لحكم المنسوخ والناسخ ولا) في التعلق أي تعلق الحكمين به (بل يرفع أحدهما الآخر فلا يلزم صيرورة شيء واحد مأموراً ومنهياً في زمان واحد، وقد مر منا ما يفي لدفع هذا الجواب ولا بأس بالإعادة ليزداد وضوحاً فاعلم أنه تعلق التكليف وقت التمكن بالأمر المنسوخ أم لا وعلى الثاني لا تكليف، فلا ينسخ إذ لا تكليف قبل التمكن، لأنه شرط التكليف، وعلى الأول صار الفعل واجباً في الذمة ثم صار حراماً في ذلك الوقت أيضاً بالناسخ فلزم اجتماعهما قطعاً، فإن قيل المقصود من أمر المنسوخ الإتيان بعقد القلب وبالنهي الكف عنه وقت التمكن ؟ قلت : عقد القلب بأي شيء إن كان هناك وجوب فيلزم المحذور قهقرى، وإن لم يكن هناك وجوب صار المقصود عقد القلب خلاف الواقع والمطلوب جهلاً مركباً فتدبر ولا تغلط قيل : هذا الدليل منقوض بجميع صور (النسخ) فإنه يلزم أن يكون شيء واحد مأموراً بالمنسوخ ومنهياً بالناسخ (أقول) الانتقاض (ممنوع، فإن الوقت في غير محل النزاع متعدد فيصح أن يبقى الوجوب بالأمر المنسوخ إلى أمد ويكون النسخ بيانه (فيصح بيان الأمد فتأمل ولك أن تطرح حديث بيان الأمد من البين وتقول : لما كان الوقت في غير محل النزاع متعدّداً فيجوز تعلق الوجوب به في وقت وارتفاعه في وقت آخر فلا محذور أصلاً سواء كان النسخ نفس بيان مدة بقاء المنسوخ أو الرفع فافهم. نعم : لو قرر الدليل هكذا يلزم في النسخ قبل التمكن تعلق الوجوب والحرمة وقت النسخ لتوجه النقض البتة، ولا يفيد الجواب بتعدد زمان الوجوب والرفع، فإن الوجوب قبل الرفع لأنه يعود إلى أصل الدليل، فإن الوجوب هناك أيضاً قبل الارتفاع، لكن المقصود هنا الإتيان بعقد القلب، وفي سائر الصور الإتيان بالفعل، لكن ليس المقصود هذا بل لزوم توارد التكليف بالفعل وقت التمكن وبالانتهاء في وهو لازم من غير مرد وكذا اجتماع الحسن والقبح أيضاً كما مر فتذكر، فقد بان لك عدم جواز نسخ التكليف قبل تمكن الفعل كما ذهب إليه أكثر محققي الحنفية
Those who deny abrogation before capability say: If abrogation were allowed, it would necessitate a single person at the time of capability being both commanded and prohibited, and the single obligated person with respect to a single act at a single time is neither commanded nor prohibited. We reply: There is no simultaneity in the obligation due to the abrogated and abrogating rulings, nor in the attachment of the two rulings to him. Rather, one lifts the other, so it does not necessitate a single thing being commanded and prohibited at one time. We have already stated enough to refute this answer, but repetition is fine for clarity. Know that the obligation at the time of capability with the abrogated command either exists or not. If not, there is no obligation and no abrogation since there is no obligation before capability, for it is a condition of obligation. If yes, then the act became obligatory in the liability and then became prohibited at that very time by the abrogating ruling, so they necessarily coexist. If it is said that the purpose of the abrogated command is to perform an intention and the prohibition is to refrain from it at the time of capability, I say: Intention of what? If there was obligation, the problem recurs; if no obligation, then the intended intention is contrary to reality and the required thing is compound ignorance. Reflect and do not err. It is said that this proof is refuted by all instances of abrogation, for it would necessitate a single thing being commanded by the abrogated and prohibited by the abrogating. I say: The refutation is denied, for the time in the non-disputed case is multiple, so it is valid for the obligation by the abrogated command to remain until a term and for abrogation to be its clarification. So it is valid to clarify the term. But you can discard the term clarification argument and say: Since the time in the non-disputed case is multiple, it is valid for obligation to attach at one time and be lifted at another time, so there is no problem at all, whether abrogation is the same as clarifying the duration of the abrogated ruling or lifting. Understand. Yes, if the proof is formulated thus, then in abrogation before capability, obligation and prohibition would attach at the time of abrogation, and the objection would be inevitable. And the answer of multiple times for obligation and lifting does not help, for obligation exists before lifting, which goes back to the original proof: obligation there is also before lifting. But here the purpose is to perform a mental intention, while in other cases it is to perform an act. But the point is not this; rather, it is the necessary occurrence of obligation and prohibition with respect to the act at the time of capability and at the end, which is unavoidable. Similarly, the combination of good and evil, as mentioned, so reflect. Thus it has become clear to you that abrogation of obligation before capability to perform the act is not permissible, as most Hanafi muhaqqiqeen hold.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents a rational argument (dalil aqli) within a dispute about whether a ruling can be abrogated before the obligated person has the ability (tamakkun) to act. The opponents argue that abrogation before tamakkun would lead to simultaneous command and prohibition at the same time for the same act, which is impossible. The text offers a Hanafi response: the abrogating ruling lifts the abrogated one, so there is no simultaneity. However, a deeper analysis shows that if the ruling applied at the time of tamakkun, then both obligation and prohibition would coincide. The text refines this by considering the intention (عقد القلب) versus actual performance. Ultimately, the relied-upon position of the Hanafi muhaqqiqeen is that such abrogation is impermissible. This is a complex usul dispute with multiple layers of rebuttal.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): The lifting of a Shari'ah ruling by a later ruling, whether by clarification of the term or by actual removal.
التمكن (al-tamakkun): The ability or capability of the obligated person to perform the required act, a condition for obligation.
المنسوخ (al-mansūkh): The earlier ruling that is abrogated.
الناسخ (al-nāsikh): The later ruling that abrogates the earlier one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as stated in this passage, is it permissible to abrogate a ruling before the obligated person has the ability (tamakkun) to act upon it?
A) Yes, because Allah can do as He wills
B) No, because it would lead to simultaneous command and prohibition
C) Yes, because the time is multiple
D) No, because the person is not yet obligated

Key Takeaway
Naskh before tamakkun is impermissible because it entails logically impossible simultaneous command and prohibition for the same act at the same moment.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
6 min
Abrogation of Belief Rulings: Hanafi vs Ash'ari
Dispute over the permissibility of abrogating rulings on essential beliefs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument against the abrogation of rulings on essential beliefs and distinguish it from the Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
Intrinsic moral values cannot be changed by abrogation; faith is always obligatory and disbelief always prohibited.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul dispute: can Allah abrogate the obligation of faith and prohibition of disbelief? The Hanafi position relies on the concept of intrinsic goodness/badness (ḥusn/qubḥ dhātī), while Ash'aris hold that moral values are determined solely by Shari'ah. Let us examine the arguments and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
What specific rulings are in dispute? The passage focuses on the obligation of faith (wujūb al-īmān) and the prohibition of disbelief (ḥurmat al-kufr), and all false beliefs.
These are considered essential beliefs, not merely practical acts.
2
State the Hanafi position and its rationale
Hanafis (and Mu'tazila except Juba'iyyah) hold that these rulings cannot be abrogated because the acts have intrinsic goodness or badness that cannot be removed by any later ruling.
The argument is based on the nature of the acts themselves, not on a textual command.
3
State the Ash'ari position and its rationale
Ash'aris (including Shafi'is) hold that goodness and badness are determined only by Shari'ah; thus, Allah can abrogate any ruling, including those on faith and disbelief.
For Ash'aris, faith and disbelief are morally neutral until Shari'ah assigns a value.
4
Understand the practical consequence
If abrogation were permissible, then faith could become non-obligatory and disbelief non-prohibited. Hanafis consider this impossible because it would change the essence of the acts.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in legal theory.
5
Analyze the sub-discussion on knowing abrogation
The text includes a debate about whether it is obligatory for the mukallaf to know the abrogating and abrogated rulings. Imam al-Ghazali argued it is obligatory; others rebutted.
This sub-issue shows the complexity of applying the dispute to actual practice.

على المكلف اعتقاد أن الناسخ خطاب من الله تعالى (وإلا ) أي وإن لم يجب فهو يعمل بالمنسوخ ولو عمل به لأثم قطعاً فإن العمل بالمنسوخ حرام (فهذا العقد مطلوب منه) وهو تكليف (فتدبر) واعترض عليه مطلع الأسرار Issue: According to the Hanafis and Mu'tazila, it is not permissible to abrogate a ruling of an act whose goodness or badness does not admit of removal, such as the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief and all false beliefs. It has already passed that you said: All according to the Mu'tazila other than the Juba'iyyah are such, because for them the goodness and badness of every act is due to the essence of the act, and what is intrinsic does not change. I said: What is due to something else may overcome what is intrinsic, so what is intrinsic may be absent, as in the case of water's coolness. And it has passed in the principles of rulings. And it is permissible to abrogate the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief according to the Ash'aris, the followers of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and among them are the Shafi'is, since for them there is no goodness or badness except by Shari'ah. So for them, faith and disbelief are equal; what Shari'ah makes obligatory is good and what it forbids is evil. Therefore they allowed abrogation of obligations rationally. Except for Imam Hujjat al-Islam (al-Ghazali), may Allah sanctify his spirit, who said: He must know the secret of the abrogating and the abrogated, and that is an obligation. It was said in response: We grant that such knowledge is necessary, but it is not obligatory upon the obligated person to acquire that knowledge; rather, it is obligatory upon Allah rationally, according to the principles of the Mu'tazila, or according to the principles of the Ahl al-Sunnah, it is a grace from Allah to inform the people. If it is not obligatory upon the obligated person, then there is no obligation. I say: It is obligatory upon the obligated person to believe that the abrogating (naskh) is a speech from Allah. Otherwise, even if not obligatory, he acts upon the abrogated ruling, and if he does so, he certainly sins, for acting upon the abrogated ruling is forbidden. So this intention is required of him, and it is an obligation. Reflect. And it was objected by the one who is the key to divine secrets, al-Walid? may Allah sanctify his secret: First, because when he assumed that it is obligatory for Allah to inform of abrogation, then he will not approach acting upon the abrogated, so he does not sin; and if he acts with this knowledge, the obligation does not help to remove this sin. Second, because the assumption is that there are no obligations at all, neither by command nor prohibition. So if one assumes the absence of this knowledge and acts upon the abrogated, then no sin follows. How is this case similar to the case of the absence of prophethood? Then all acts are permissible, and acting upon the abrogated and the abrogating are equal, so no sin. Yes, if this knowledge were absent, one would fall into the trouble of acting upon abrogated rulings without benefit, which is futile, but that does not necessitate the obligation of this knowledge, since for the Ash'aris it is not impossible for Allah to place His servants in futility. Understand. And the answer to the Imam's words: First, as they said: If he knows both, the obligation lapses because it ceases after the act, by agreement between us and him. And the obligation has been lifted by other than them through abrogation, so there is no obligation at all. It is said: The lifting by the act, i.e., the lifting of obligation by performing the act, is called naskh? So this lifting is not naskh, so it does not necessitate the abrogation of all obligations, but rather

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) over whether rulings on essential beliefs—such as the obligation of iman and the prohibition of kufr—can be abrogated. The Hanafi and Mu'tazili position is that these rulings cannot be abrogated because the goodness (husn) of faith and badness (qubh) of disbelief are intrinsic to the acts themselves. The Ash'ari position is that goodness and badness are determined solely by Shari'ah, so abrogation is possible. The text also discusses a sub-issue raised by Imam al-Ghazali regarding the obligation to know the abrogating and abrogated rulings, with a rebuttal from another scholar. Ultimately, the Hanafi position is that such abrogation is impermissible, and the discussion reinforces the usul principle that intrinsic moral qualities are immutable.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): The lifting of a Shari'ah ruling by a later ruling, discussed here in the context of essential beliefs.
الحسن والقبح الذاتيان (al-ḥusn wa al-qubḥ al-dhātiyān): Intrinsic goodness and badness inherent in acts themselves, independent of Shari'ah.
العقائد الباطلة (al-'aqā'id al-bāṭila): False beliefs, including disbelief (kufr), which are prohibited intrinsically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the obligation of faith and prohibition of disbelief cannot be abrogated because they are intrinsically good and bad, respectively.

Naskh — Abrogation

The Impermissibility of Naskh Before Tamakkun
Ruling on naskh before tamakkun with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rational proof that naskh cannot precede the ability to act, and identify the logical impossibility it entails.

Core Idea
Abrogating an obligation before one can act on it is impossible—it forces simultaneous obligation and prohibition.

The Hanafi school holds that abrogation (naskh) of a legal ruling cannot occur before the mukallaf has had the ability to act upon the original ruling. This lesson unpacks the rational proof (dalil aqli) for this principle, demonstrating why naskh before tamakkun leads to a logical contradiction. Understanding this proof sharpens your ability to analyze the coherence of divine commands within Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by clearly stating the rule: naskh before tamakkun is invalid. Recognize that this is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul, not merely a preference.
The text uses 'عدم جواز' – impermissibility, not just dislike.
2
Understand the hypothetical scenario
Imagine an obligation revealed, but before anyone can perform it, it is abrogated. The author asks: what happens at the moment of naskh?
The key time is 'وقت النسخ' – the exact moment of abrogation.
3
Trace the logical contradiction
At the moment of naskh, the original obligation (wujub) is still in effect until abrogated, but the new prohibition (hurmah) is simultaneously applied. This creates tawarud al-taklif – two contradictory commands on the same act at the same time.
The text says 'تعلق الوجوب والحرمة وقت النسخ' – attachment of both obligation and prohibition.
4
Reject the counter-argument
The objection that the times are different (obligation before removal) is rejected because the obligation must exist before its removal, and at the moment of naskh both are present in the same instant of ability.
The author says 'لا يفيد الجواب بتعدد زمان الوجوب والرفع' – the multiplicity answer is useless.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi position
Thus, naskh before tamakkun is impossible because it entails both good and evil (husn and qubh) simultaneously for the same act. The majority of Hanafi muhaqqiqun hold this view.
The text ends with 'فقد بان لك عدم جواز' – it has become clear to you the impermissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول/ الكتاب كان النسخ نفس بيان مدة بقاء المنسوخ أو الرفع فافهم. نعم : لو قرر الدليل هكذا يلزم في النسخ قبل التمكن تعلق الوجوب والحرمة وقت النسخ لتوجه النقض البتة، ولا يفيد الجواب بتعدد زمان الوجوب والرفع، فإن الوجوب قبل الرفع لأنه يعود إلى أصل الدليل، فإن الوجوب هناك أيضاً قبل الارتفاع، لكن المقصود هنا الإتيان بعقد القلب، وفي سائر الصور الإتيان بالفعل، لكن ليس المقصود هذا بل لزوم توارد التكليف بالفعل وقت التمكن وبالانتهاء في وهو لازم من غير مرد وكذا اجتماع الحسن والقبح أيضاً كما مر فتذكر، فقد بان لك عدم جواز نسخ التكليف قبل تمكن الفعل كما ذهب إليه أكثر محققي الحنفية .
First principle: The book — naskh itself is a statement of the duration of the abrogated [ruling] or its removal, so understand. Yes: if the proof is set thus, then in naskh before ability, the attachment of obligation and prohibition at the time of naskh would necessarily entail definitive rebuttal. And the answer by multiplicity of time of obligation and removal is not useful, for the obligation is before removal because it returns to the original proof, for obligation there is also before elevation. But the intent here is bringing a mental act, and in other cases bringing a physical act. But this is not the intent; rather the necessity of the simultaneous occurrence of obligation with the act at the time of ability and with the ending, and it is necessary without repellant, and similarly the conjunction of good and evil as well, as mentioned, so remember. So it has become clear to you the impermissibility of abrogation of obligation before ability to perform the act, as held by most verifying Hanafis.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on naskh before tamakkun (ability to perform). The author states that abrogating a ruling before the mukallaf has had the ability to act upon it is invalid. The rational proof is that if naskh occurred before ability, it would necessitate the impossible: both obligation and prohibition attaching simultaneously at the time of naskh. The counter-argument that the times of obligation and removal are multiple is rejected because the obligation must precede the removal. The real issue is the impossibility of having both obligation and its removal at the exact moment of ability. This leads to a conjunction of good (if one acts) and evil (if one refrains) which is impossible. Therefore, naskh before tamakkun is impermissible, a position held by the majority of Hanafi muhaqqiqun.

Key Terms
النسخ قبل التمكن (al-naskh qabl al-tamakkun): Abrogation of a legal obligation before the mukallaf has had the ability to perform it.
توارد التكليف (tawarud al-taklif): The simultaneous occurrence of obligation and prohibition on a single act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it would require a new prophet to deliver the abrogation
B) Because it would necessitate simultaneous obligation and prohibition
C) Because it contradicts istihsan
D) Because it is only permissible for acts of worship

Key Takeaway
Naskh before tamakkun is invalid in Hanafi Usul because it creates a logically impossible simultaneous obligation and prohibition.

Naskh — Abrogation

Abrogation of Iman and Kufr: Hanafi vs. Ash'ari
Dispute on abrogating essential beliefs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that acts with intrinsic goodness (like iman) cannot be abrogated, and evaluate the Ash'ari counterargument based on the nature of husn wa qubh.

Core Idea
Goodness and evil are intrinsic to acts; what is due to essence cannot be removed by abrogation.

This passage presents a core usul dispute: can the rulings of fundamental beliefs like iman and kufr be abrogated? The Hanafis and Mu'tazila argue that the goodness of iman and evil of kufr are inseparable from their essences, so abrogation is impossible. The Ash'aris, denying intrinsic moral properties, permit abrogation. The debate turns on the epistemological question of husn wa qubh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
State the Hanafi/Mu'tazili view that naskh is not allowed, and the Ash'ari view that naskh is allowed.
2
Locate the root cause of disagreement
The nature of husn wa qubh: intrinsic (Hanafis/Mu'tazila) vs. revealed (Ash'aris).
This is an epistemological difference.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Husn and qubh are due to dhat (essence); what is due to dhat does not change. Refer to the water coldness analogy for possible override but not removal.
The analogy shows intrinsic qualities can be overridden but not eliminated.
4
Analyze the Ash'ari proof
No intrinsic husn/qubh; all moral values come from divine command. Hence faith and disbelief are equal in themselves.
This allows abrogation of any ruling in principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
For Hanafis, the obligation of iman is eternal; for Ash'aris, it could in principle be abrogated, though historically it is not.
This has implications for the stability of core beliefs.

مسألة: (لا يجوز عند الحنفية والمعتزلة نسخ حكم فعل لا يقبل حسنه أو قبحه السقوط، كوجوب الإيمان وحرمة الكفر وسائر العقائد الباطلة، وقد مر من قبل أن قلت : الكل عند · المعتزلة غير الجبائية كذلك لأن حسن كل عقلاً) على أصول أهل الاعتزال (أو) إعادة على ما تقتضيه أصول أهل السنة القامعين للبدعة كثرهم الله تعالى تعريف الناسخ) للعباد تفضلاً منه تعالى على عباده، وإذا لم يجب على المكلف فلا تكليف به (أقول : يجب) على المكلف اعتقاد أن الناسخ خطاب من الله تعالى (وإلا ) أي وإن لم يجب فهو يعمل بالمنسوخ ولو عمل به لأثم قطعاً فإن العمل بالمنسوخ حرام (فهذا العقد مطلوب منه) وهو تكليف (فتدبر) واعترض عليه مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره، أما أولاً : فلأنه لما فرض وجوب إعلام الله تعالى انتساخ الحكم فلا يقرب إلى العمل به فلا يأثم وإن عمل به مع هذا العلم فلا ينفع الوجوب عليه دفعاً لهذا الإثم . وأما ثانياً فلأن الفرض انتفاء التكاليف رأساً لا بالإيجاب ولا بالتحريم، فلو فرض انتفاء هذه المعرفة والعمل بالمنسوخ حينئذ لا يلزم الإثم، كيف صار هذا الحال حال انتفاء البعثة فالأفعال كلها على الإباحة، فالعمل بالمنسوخ والناسخ سيان فلا إثم. نعم : لو لم تكن هذه المعرفة وقع في تعب العمل بالأحكام المنسوخة من غير فائدة فيلزم العبث، لكن لا يلزم منه وجوب هذه المعرفة، إذ لا استحالة عند الأشعرية في إيقاع الله تعالى عبيده في العبث فافهم (والجواب عن كلام الإمام (أولاً كما قالوا : إذا علمهما يرتفع التكليف بهما لانقطاعه بعد الفعل (اتفاقاً بيننا وبينه (وقد ارتفع) التكليف (بغيرهما) بالنسخ فلا تكليف أصلاً قيل : الارتفاع (بالفعل أي ارتفاع التكليف بإتيان الفعل نسخاً) يسمى فارتفاع هذا التكليف ليس بنسخ فلم يلزم نسخ جميع التكليفات، بل نسخ (لا  فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني ( البعض، وارتفاع البعض بالامتثال (وأجيب بأن النسخ إنما هو للتكليف المستمر، وهذه المعرفة غير مستمرة، لأنها ضرورة معرفة النسخ والضروريات تتقدر بقدرها، ولا يذهب عليك أن هذا إنما يتم لو أرادوا بنسخ الجميع نسخ المستمرة منها، ويصير حينئذ النزاع لفظياً، فإن الإمام غير منكر إياه، بل جوّزوا منع نسخ وجوب معرفة النسخ والناسخ فإذن : الجواب ما قد مر مع منع الوجوب لا غير وثانياً : كما أقول أن النسخ يحدث بعد التكليف) لأنهم عدم طار ونسخ الجميع كما رفع تكليفاً متقدماً على النسخ (أوجب تكليفاً آخر) وهو معرفة أن الناسخ خطاب الله ومعرفة النسخ (فوجد هذا التكليف (ثم ارتفع لأنه من الجميع التي نسخت ولهذا لا يلزم التسلسل فإنه إن لم يرتفع هذا التكليف بنسخ الجميع واحتاج إلى ناسخ آخر وجب معرفة هذا الناسخ، فلا بد لنسخه من ناسخ ،آخر وهكذا، وأما إذا كان نسخه بنسخ الجميع فلا محذور (فتأمل) وهذا أيضاً غير وافٍ لأنه قد سلم أن نسخ الجميع أوجب تكليفاً آخر لا بد من امتثاله ، انتساخه قبل الامتثال وإلا لما حصل المقصود من التكليف وبعد الامتثال لا يبقى على الذمة شيء حتى ينسخ، فلا يصح أن يكون ارتفاعه، لأنه من الجميع فافهم.
Issue: (It is not permissible according to the Hanafis and Mu'tazila to abrogate the ruling of an act whose goodness or evil does not admit removal, such as the obligation of faith, the prohibition of disbelief, and all false beliefs. And it has passed before that you said: All according to the Mu'tazila except the Jabba'iyya are like that because the goodness and evil of every act according to them are due to the essence of the act, and what is due to the essence does not change. You said: What is due to other may overcome what is due to essence, so what is due to essence may be overridden, like the coldness of water (and it has passed) in the principles of rulings. (And it is permissible) to abrogate the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief (according to the Ash'aris) who follow Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (and among them the Shafi'is, for there is no goodness or evil according to them except by law). So faith and disbelief are equal to them, and what the law makes obligatory is good and what it prohibits is evil, and therefore they permitted abrogation of obligations rationally. (Except Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify him all, said: It is obligatory to know the secret of abrogation and the abrogator, and it is an obligation. It was said in response: We concede that that knowledge is necessary, but (it is not obligatory upon the mukallaf to acquire that knowledge, rather it is obligatory upon Allah rationally) according to the principles of the people of I'tizal, or it is a grace on His servants, and if it is not obligatory upon the mukallaf then there is no obligation upon him. (I say: It is obligatory) upon the mukallaf to believe that the abrogator is speech from Allah (and if not) i.e., if it is not obligatory, then he would act upon the abrogated, and if he acted upon it he would certainly sin, for acting upon the abrogated is forbidden. (So this belief is required of him) and it is an obligation. (So ponder). And it was objected by ... firstly: because when he assumed that Allah's informing of the abrogation is obligatory, then he would not approach acting upon it, so he would not sin, and if he acted upon it despite this knowledge, then the obligation upon him does not help in preventing this sin. And secondly: because the assumption is the absence of obligations entirely, not by obligation nor by prohibition. So if we assume the absence of this knowledge and acting upon the abrogated, then no sin follows. How could this state be like the state of absence of prophethood? All acts are permissible, so acting upon the abrogated and the abrogator are equal, so no sin. Yes: if this knowledge were absent, one would fall into the trouble of acting upon abrogated rulings with no benefit, leading to futility, but that does not necessitate the obligation of this knowledge, for there is no impossibility according to the Ash'aris in Allah causing His servants to fall into futility, so understand. (And the response to the Imam's statement is: firstly, as they said: If he knows both, the obligation of both is removed due to its cessation after the act, by agreement between us and him. And the obligation has been removed by other than them, by abrogation, so there is no obligation at all. It was said: The removal by the act, i.e., removal of obligation by performing the act as abrogation, is called such; so this removal is not by abrogation, so abrogation of all obligations does not follow, rather abrogation of some, and removal of some by compliance. (And it was answered: abrogation is only for continuous obligation, and this knowledge is not continuous, because it is a necessity of knowing abrogation, and necessities are limited to their extent. And you should not be unaware that this is valid only if they intended by abrogation of all to mean abrogation of the continuous ones. Then the dispute becomes verbal, for the Imam does not deny that. Rather they permitted preventing abrogation of the obligation of knowing the abrogator and abrogation. So then: the response is what has passed with the prevention of obligation only. And secondly: as I say that abrogation occurs after obligation, because they are a contingent non-existence. And abrogation of all, as it removed an obligation prior to abrogation, necessitated another obligation — that is knowing that the abrogator is speech of Allah and knowing the abrogation. So this obligation existed, then it was removed because it is among those that were abrogated. Therefore no infinite regress occurs, because if this obligation were not removed by abrogation of all and needed another abrogator, then knowledge of this abrogator would be obligatory, and so on infinitely. But if its removal is by abrogation of all, then no problem. (Reflect). And this is also insufficient because it has been conceded that abrogation of all necessitated another obligation that must be complied with, abrogation of it before compliance, otherwise the purpose of obligation is not achieved, and after compliance nothing remains on the liability to be abrogated. So it is not valid that its removal is by abrogation of all, so understand.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a dispute on two issues: (1) the permissibility of abrogating essential acts like iman and kufr, and (2) whether knowledge of the nasikh (abrogator) is obligatory on the mukallaf. The Hanafis and Mu'tazila hold that acts whose goodness or evil is intrinsic (like iman and kufr) cannot be abrogated because their moral value is inseparable from their essence. The Ash'aris, who deny intrinsic moral value, allow abrogation of any ruling, including iman and kufr, since all moral categories are determined by divine command. Imam al-Ghazali adds that one must know the secret of naskh and the nasikh, but a counter-argument states that such knowledge is not obligatory on the mukallaf; rather, it is Allah's obligation (according to Mu'tazila) or a grace (according to Sunnis). The author then argues that this knowledge is indeed wajib on the mukallaf to avoid acting on an abrogated ruling, which would be sinful. Objections and responses follow regarding the necessity and continuity of this obligation, with detailed arguments about whether naskh of all obligations would entail infinite regress.

Key Terms
حسن وقبح (husn wa qubh): Goodness and evil of an act; Hanafis hold they are intrinsic, Ash'aris say they are determined by divine law.
الناسخ (al-nasikh): The abrogating revelation (Quranic verse or hadith) that supersedes an earlier ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Hanafis forbid abrogation of the obligation of faith?
A) Iman is wajib and wajib cannot be abrogated.
B) The goodness of iman is intrinsic to its essence.
C) The nasikh must be mutawatir.
D) Iman is an act of the heart and cannot be abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that acts like iman have intrinsic moral value, making their rulings immutable; this is a direct consequence of their rationalist ethics.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
8 min
The Obligation to Know the Nasikh: A Usul Dispute
Dispute on the obligation to know the nasikh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the debate on whether knowing the nasikh is obligatory on the mukallaf, and evaluate the arguments involving infinite regress and divine grace.

Core Idea
Knowing the nasikh is obligatory to avoid acting on abrogated rulings, but its necessity is contested based on whether it prevents sin or leads to futility.

The passage then turns to a second dispute: Is it obligatory (wajib) for each mukallaf to know the nasikh (abrogating text) and the fact of abrogation? Imam al-Ghazali argues it is wajib, but the author engages in a dialectic examining whether such knowledge is required, given that divine abrogation may render it moot or lead to infinite regress. The discussion weaves together Mu'tazili and Ash'ari principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim of Imam al-Ghazali
Imam al-Ghazali states that it is wajib to know the secret of naskh and the nasikh.
This is a strong position making such knowledge a personal obligation.
2
State the counter-objection
The objectors argue that such knowledge is not wajib on the mukallaf; it is either Allah's obligation (according to Mu'tazila) or a grace (according to Ash'aris).
This shifts the burden from human to divine.
3
Analyze the author's argument for wajib
Without this knowledge, one might act on the abrogated ruling, which is sinful. Thus, this knowledge is a necessary condition to avoid sin and therefore wajib.
The author assumes acting on mansukh is always haram.
4
Examine the first objection
If Allah informs the mukallaf, he would not act on the abrogated; and if there are no obligations (like before prophethood), acting on the abrogated is not sinful. So the wajib is not necessary.
The objection challenges the necessity claim.
5
Examine the response and the issue of infinite regress
The response argues that the obligation to know the nasikh arises only after naskh, and if all obligations are abrogated, this knowledge obligation is also removed, preventing regress.
The passage ends noting this response may be insufficient.

الجميع واحتاج إلى ناسخ آخر وجب معرفة هذا الناسخ، فلا بد لنسخه من ناسخ ،آخر وهكذا، وأما إذا كان نسخه بنسخ الجميع فلا محذور (فتأمل) وهذا أيضاً غير وافٍ لأنه قد سلم أن نسخ الجميع أوجب تكليفاً آخر لا بد من امتثاله ، انتساخه قبل الامتثال وإلا لما حصل المقصود من التكليف وبعد الامتثال لا يبقى على الذمة شيء حتى ينسخ، فلا يصح أن يكون ارتفاعه، لأنه من الجميع فافهم.
Issue: (It is not permissible according to the Hanafis and Mu'tazila to abrogate the ruling of an act whose goodness or evil does not admit removal, such as the obligation of faith, the prohibition of disbelief, and all false beliefs. And it has passed before that you said: All according to the Mu'tazila except the Jabba'iyya are like that because the goodness and evil of every act according to them are due to the essence of the act, and what is due to the essence does not change. You said: What is due to other may overcome what is due to essence, so what is due to essence may be overridden, like the coldness of water (and it has passed) in the principles of rulings. (And it is permissible) to abrogate the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief (according to the Ash'aris) who follow Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (and among them the Shafi'is, for there is no goodness or evil according to them except by law). So faith and disbelief are equal to them, and what the law makes obligatory is good and what it prohibits is evil, and therefore they permitted abrogation of obligations rationally. (Except Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify him all, said: It is obligatory to know the secret of abrogation and the abrogator, and it is an obligation. It was said in response: We concede that that knowledge is necessary, but (it is not obligatory upon the mukallaf to acquire that knowledge, rather it is obligatory upon Allah rationally) according to the principles of the people of I'tizal, or it is a grace on His servants, and if it is not obligatory upon the mukallaf then there is no obligation upon him. (I say: It is obligatory) upon the mukallaf to believe that the abrogator is speech from Allah (and if not) i.e., if it is not obligatory, then he would act upon the abrogated, and if he acted upon it he would certainly sin, for acting upon the abrogated is forbidden. (So this belief is required of him) and it is an obligation. (So ponder). And it was objected by ... firstly: because when he assumed that Allah's informing of the abrogation is obligatory, then he would not approach acting upon it, so he would not sin, and if he acted upon it despite this knowledge, then the obligation upon him does not help in preventing this sin. And secondly: because the assumption is the absence of obligations entirely, not by obligation nor by prohibition. So if we assume the absence of this knowledge and acting upon the abrogated, then no sin follows. How could this state be like the state of absence of prophethood? All acts are permissible, so acting upon the abrogated and the abrogator are equal, so no sin. Yes: if this knowledge were absent, one would fall into the trouble of acting upon abrogated rulings with no benefit, leading to futility, but that does not necessitate the obligation of this knowledge, for there is no impossibility according to the Ash'aris in Allah causing His servants to fall into futility, so understand. (And the response to the Imam's statement is: firstly, as they said: If he knows both, the obligation of both is removed due to its cessation after the act, by agreement between us and him. And the obligation has been removed by other than them, by abrogation, so there is no obligation at all. It was said: The removal by the act, i.e., removal of obligation by performing the act as abrogation, is called such; so this removal is not by abrogation, so abrogation of all obligations does not follow, rather abrogation of some, and removal of some by compliance. (And it was answered: abrogation is only for continuous obligation, and this knowledge is not continuous, because it is a necessity of knowing abrogation, and necessities are limited to their extent. And you should not be unaware that this is valid only if they intended by abrogation of all to mean abrogation of the continuous ones. Then the dispute becomes verbal, for the Imam does not deny that. Rather they permitted preventing abrogation of the obligation of knowing the abrogator and abrogation. So then: the response is what has passed with the prevention of obligation only. And secondly: as I say that abrogation occurs after obligation, because they are a contingent non-existence. And abrogation of all, as it removed an obligation prior to abrogation, necessitated another obligation — that is knowing that the abrogator is speech of Allah and knowing the abrogation. So this obligation existed, then it was removed because it is among those that were abrogated. Therefore no infinite regress occurs, because if this obligation were not removed by abrogation of all and needed another abrogator, then knowledge of this abrogator would be obligatory, and so on infinitely. But if its removal is by abrogation of all, then no problem. (Reflect). And this is also insufficient because it has been conceded that abrogation of all necessitated another obligation that must be complied with, abrogation of it before compliance, otherwise the purpose of obligation is not achieved, and after compliance nothing remains on the liability to be abrogated. So it is not valid that its removal is by abrogation of all, so understand.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a dispute on two issues: (1) the permissibility of abrogating essential acts like iman and kufr, and (2) whether knowledge of the nasikh (abrogator) is obligatory on the mukallaf. The Hanafis and Mu'tazila hold that acts whose goodness or evil is intrinsic (like iman and kufr) cannot be abrogated because their moral value is inseparable from their essence. The Ash'aris, who deny intrinsic moral value, allow abrogation of any ruling, including iman and kufr, since all moral categories are determined by divine command. Imam al-Ghazali adds that one must know the secret of naskh and the nasikh, but a counter-argument states that such knowledge is not obligatory on the mukallaf; rather, it is Allah's obligation (according to Mu'tazila) or a grace (according to Sunnis). The author then argues that this knowledge is indeed wajib on the mukallaf to avoid acting on an abrogated ruling, which would be sinful. Objections and responses follow regarding the necessity and continuity of this obligation, with detailed arguments about whether naskh of all obligations would entail infinite regress.

Key Terms
الناسخ (al-nasikh): The abrogating revelation that supersedes an earlier ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument that knowing the nasikh is wajib?
A) To avoid infinite regress.
B) To avoid acting on abrogated rulings.
C) To fulfill the secret of naskh.
D) To establish the continuity of obligations.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to know the nasikh is a logical necessity to prevent sin from acting on abrogated rulings, but its exact status remains debated within Usul al-Fiqh.

Abrogation of Perpetual Commands via Qiyas
Argument for abrogation of perpetual commands via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas to justify abrogation of a perpetual command and identify the textual category of the primary example.

Core Idea
A perpetual command is abrogable by analogy to a time-limited command.

The majority of usul scholars hold that a perpetual command can be abrogated, using qiyas on a time-limited command. This lesson unpacks that analogy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is whether a ruling that is explicitly perpetual (e.g., 'fast forever') can be abrogated. The majority say yes; some dissent.
This is a dispute in usul al-fiqh about the scope of naskh.
2
State the majority position
The majority of usul scholars (جمهور من أهل الأصول) hold that abrogation of a perpetual command is permissible.
They use qiyas as their main proof.
3
Examine the qiyas structure
The asl (original case) is 'fast tomorrow' (صم غداً), a command restricted by a specific time. The far' (new case) is 'fast forever' (صوموا أبداً), a command restricted by eternity. Both share the illa: they are commands with temporal restrictions that encompass parts of time.
The restriction in the analogized case is all eternity; in the original it is a specific day.
4
Apply the ruling
Since abrogation of 'fast tomorrow' is permissible before its restriction ends, by analogy abrogation of 'fast forever' is permissible before eternity ends.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illa is explicit.
5
Note the exception
The text mentions that if the command is a decisive text (nass mufassar), some scholars say it cannot be abrogated. But the majority disagrees.
This leads to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الجمهور من أهل الأصول على جواز نسخ نحو صوموا أبداً) أي الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد (لأنه كصم غداً) في تناول أجزاء القيد، إلا أن القيد في المقيس يتناول كل الأبد : وفي المقيس عليه البعض المعين، ونسخ نحو صم غداً، جائز قبل انتهاء القيد، فكذا نسخ : أبداً (بخلاف الصوم واجب مستمر أبداً إذا قيل لإنشاء الوجوب، وأما إذا كان خبراً فلا كلام فيه ههنا لأنه نص (مؤكد لا احتمال فيه لغيره وهو المفسر في اصطلاحنا، فلا يصح انتساخه (وفيه: أن النصوصية والتأكيد لا يمنع النسخ بنص آخر هو (أقوى منه) فإنّ النص المؤكد قصارى أمره ظهور الدلالة على المراد بحيث لا يبقى احتمال غيره، وأما ارتفاعه فكلا فافهم وقيل : هما سواء في عدم الجواز وعليه الشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبو منصور الماتريدي، والشيخ الإمام أبو بكر الجصاص، والشيخان الإمامان شمس الأئمة، وفخر الإسلام كذا قالوا لكن عبارة فخر الإسلام وأما الذي ينافي النسخ من الأحكام التي في الأصل محتملة للوجود والعدم فثلاثة تأبيد ثبت نصاً وتأبيد ثبت دلالة، وتوقيت، أما التأبيد صريحاً فمثل قوله تعالى : خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبدا [المائدة : ۱۱۹] وقوله تعالى : وَجَاعِلُ الَّذِينَ اتَّبَعُوكَ فَوْقَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَمَةِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ٥٥] يريد بهم الذين صدقوا به وبمحمد عليه الصلاة والسلام الملك العلام، وهذا والقسم الثاني مثل سائر شرائع محمد التي قبض على إقرارها، فإنها مؤبدة لا تحتمل النسخ، بدلالة أن محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام خاتم النبيين، ولا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ إلا بوحي على لسان نبي والثالث : وهو التوقيت انتهى كلماته الشريفة. وهذا يحتمل أن يراد بالتأبيد الأخبار بالتأبيد، كما يدل عليه تمثيله بالإخبارات وأخبار ختم النبوة (لأن التأبيد والنسخ متناقض وإن التأبيد يقتضي بقاء الحكم أبداً، والنسخ ينافيه، فإنه مقتض للارتفاع (قلنا : لا نسلم التناقض بينهما بل أحدهما يرفع الآخر، كطريان الضد، لأنهما إنشاء) ليس لهما محكي عنه حتى يتصور الصدق والكذب، وأما لزوم أخبار بقائه إلى الأبد فممنوع، من
Issue: The majority of usul scholars hold the permissibility of abrogating something like 'fast forever' — i.e., a ruling restricted by perpetuity — because it is like 'fast tomorrow' in terms of encompassing parts of the restriction, except that the restriction in the analogized case encompasses all eternity, while in the analogized-upon case it encompasses a specific part. And abrogation of something like 'fast tomorrow' is permissible before the end of the restriction, so likewise abrogation of 'forever' is permissible. (Contrary to the case if it is said 'fasting is obligatory perpetually' as a creation of obligation; but if it is an informative statement, there is no discussion here because it is a decisive text, confirmed, admitting no other probability, and it is al-mufassar in our terminology, so its abrogation is not valid. (And there is the point that decisiveness and confirmation do not prevent abrogation by another text that is stronger than it. For the confirmed text at most has a clear indication of the intent such that no other probability remains; as for its removal, no, so understand.) And some said: Both are equal in impermissibility. And upon this is the Shaykh al-Imam 'Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and the Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas, and the two Shaykhs Shams al-A'immah, and Fakhr al-Islam. Thus they said, but the expression of Fakhr al-Islam: As for that which precludes abrogation from rulings that are inherently subject to existence and non-existence, there are three: perpetuity established by text, perpetuity established by indication, and temporal restriction. As for explicit perpetuity, like His saying 'abiding therein forever' (5:119) and His saying 'and He will make those who follow you above those who disbelieve until the Day of Resurrection' (3:55) meaning those who believed in him and in Muhammad. And the second category like the rest of Muhammad's laws that are confirmed, for they are perpetual and do not admit abrogation, by the indication that Muhammad is the seal of prophets, and no prophet after him, and no abrogation except by revelation on the tongue of a prophet. And the third is temporal restriction. Thus ended his noble words. And this may mean that perpetuity is meant to be informative of perpetuity, as indicated by his example of informative statements and the news of the seal of prophethood. (Because perpetuity and abrogation are contradictory, for perpetuity necessitates the continuation of the ruling forever, and abrogation contradicts it, for it necessitates removal. (We say: We do not concede the contradiction between them; rather one removes the other, like the occurrence of an opposite, because both are creative statements, having no reported subject such that truth and falsehood could be conceived. As for the necessity of informing of its continuation forever, it is denied.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of abrogating perpetual commands (ta'bid). The majority of usul scholars, through qiyas, analogize a perpetual command like 'fast forever' to a time-limited command like 'fast tomorrow': since a time-limited command can be abrogated before its time expires, so can a perpetual command before eternity ends. Some, like al-Maturidi, al-Jassas, and others, argue that both are equally non-abrogable if the perpetuity is explicitly stated in a decisive text (nass mufassar). However, the commentator rejects the claim of contradiction, stating that abrogation is not contradictory to perpetuity because both are creative statements (insha'), not reports (ikhbar) with truth values. Thus naskh simply replaces one ruling with another, without contradicting any informative statement about eternity. Fakhr al-Islam distinguishes three categories: perpetuity by text, perpetuity by indication, and temporal restriction; only explicit perpetuity and the perpetuity of Shari'ah are non-abrogable due to the seal of prophethood.

Key Terms
التأبيد (al-ta'bid): Perpetuity; a ruling that is meant to last forever without end.
النص المؤكد (al-nass al-mu'akkad): A decisive, unambiguous text that has no probability of other meanings (al-mufassar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary analogy used by the majority to justify abrogation of a perpetual command?
A) Analogy to abrogation of wajib acts
B) Analogy to 'fast tomorrow' which is abrogable before its time ends
C) Analogy to abrogation of Quranic verses
D) Analogy to the seal of prophethood

Key Takeaway
A perpetual command (مؤبد) is abrogable by qiyas on a time-limited command, provided the abrogating text is stronger.

Counter-Opinion: Decisive Texts and Abrogation
Refutation of contradiction between perpetuity and abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Maturidi and others argue against abrogation of perpetual commands in decisive texts, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
A decisive text is immune to abrogation only if it cannot be overridden by a stronger text; the majority says it can.

While the majority uses qiyas to permit abrogation, some scholars like al-Maturidi hold that a perpetual command in a decisive text (nass mufassar) cannot be abrogated. This lesson examines their reasoning and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing view
Al-Maturidi, al-Jassas, and some Hanafi scholars (like Fakhr al-Islam in one interpretation) hold that a perpetual command in a decisive text is non-abrogable.
Fakhr al-Islam's three categories: ta'bid bil nass, ta'bid bil dalala, and ta'qit.
2
Understand their reasoning
They argue that perpetuity and abrogation are contradictory (تناقض). A text that states 'abiding forever' cannot be undone.
This is based on the idea that a report (khabar) would become false.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The commentator denies the contradiction: naskh is an insha' (creative statement), not a report. Thus, a later naskh simply replaces the earlier ruling without falsifying any report.
The text says: 'لا نسلم التناقض بينهما بل أحدهما يرفع الآخر'.
4
Examine the categories of perpetuity
Fakhr al-Islam distinguishes three types: (1) explicit perpetuity in text (e.g., 'خلدين فيها أبدا'), (2) perpetuity by indication (e.g., finality of prophethood), (3) temporal restriction. Only the first two block abrogation according to some.
The commentator notes that this may be limited to informative statements (ikhbar).
5
Conclude the dispute
The majority view prevails: even decisive texts can be abrogated by a stronger text. The notion of contradiction is rejected.
This is the operative ruling in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الجمهور من أهل الأصول على جواز نسخ نحو صوموا أبداً) أي الحكم المقيد بالتأبيد (لأنه كصم غداً) في تناول أجزاء القيد، إلا أن القيد في المقيس يتناول كل الأبد : وفي المقيس عليه البعض المعين، ونسخ نحو صم غداً، جائز قبل انتهاء القيد، فكذا نسخ : أبداً (بخلاف الصوم واجب مستمر أبداً إذا قيل لإنشاء الوجوب، وأما إذا كان خبراً فلا كلام فيه ههنا لأنه نص (مؤكد لا احتمال فيه لغيره وهو المفسر في اصطلاحنا، فلا يصح انتساخه (وفيه: أن النصوصية والتأكيد لا يمنع النسخ بنص آخر هو (أقوى منه) فإنّ النص المؤكد قصارى أمره ظهور الدلالة على المراد بحيث لا يبقى احتمال غيره، وأما ارتفاعه فكلا فافهم وقيل : هما سواء في عدم الجواز وعليه الشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبو منصور الماتريدي، والشيخ الإمام أبو بكر الجصاص، والشيخان الإمامان شمس الأئمة، وفخر الإسلام كذا قالوا لكن عبارة فخر الإسلام وأما الذي ينافي النسخ من الأحكام التي في الأصل محتملة للوجود والعدم فثلاثة تأبيد ثبت نصاً وتأبيد ثبت دلالة، وتوقيت، أما التأبيد صريحاً فمثل قوله تعالى : خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبدا [المائدة : ۱۱۹] وقوله تعالى : وَجَاعِلُ الَّذِينَ اتَّبَعُوكَ فَوْقَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَمَةِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ٥٥] يريد بهم الذين صدقوا به وبمحمد عليه الصلاة والسلام الملك العلام، وهذا والقسم الثاني مثل سائر شرائع محمد التي قبض على إقرارها، فإنها مؤبدة لا تحتمل النسخ، بدلالة أن محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام خاتم النبيين، ولا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ إلا بوحي على لسان نبي والثالث : وهو التوقيت انتهى كلماته الشريفة. وهذا يحتمل أن يراد بالتأبيد الأخبار بالتأبيد، كما يدل عليه تمثيله بالإخبارات وأخبار ختم النبوة (لأن التأبيد والنسخ متناقض وإن التأبيد يقتضي بقاء الحكم أبداً، والنسخ ينافيه، فإنه مقتض للارتفاع (قلنا : لا نسلم التناقض بينهما بل أحدهما يرفع الآخر، كطريان الضد، لأنهما إنشاء) ليس لهما محكي عنه حتى يتصور الصدق والكذب، وأما لزوم أخبار بقائه إلى الأبد فممنوع، من

النص المؤكد (al-nass al-mu'akkad): A decisive, unambiguous text that has no probability of other meanings (al-mufassar).
الإنشاء (al-insha'): Creative statement that brings about a legal ruling, as opposed to a report (khabar) that describes a state of affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi majority's argument against the claim that perpetuity and abrogation are contradictory?
A) They are both reports, so they cannot conflict.
B) They are both creative statements; one can replace the other.
C) Perpetuity is not really perpetual.
D) Abrogation only applies to non-decisive texts.

Key Takeaway
Even a decisive text (nass mufassar) can be abrogated by a stronger text; there is no contradiction because both are creative statements.
