Naskh Without a Replacement: Hanafi Defense
Argument over whether naskh requires a replacement ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on naskh without a replacement and apply the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 2:106 to counter the opposing argument.

Core Idea
Naskh without a replacement is valid; Quran 2:106's 'better or similar' refers to wording, not ruling.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a critical usul dispute: can a legal ruling be abrogated without being replaced by a new one? The Hanafi school defends the possibility and actual occurrence of such naskh, while others insist every abrogation brings a replacement. By examining Quran 2:106 and historical examples, the text demonstrates how the Hanafi school reads the primary texts and justifies its position. We'll walk through the key proof texts and logical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
What exactly is the dispute? The issue is whether naskh requires a replacement (badal). State the two positions clearly.
Hanafis say permissible; opponents (including Shafi'i in one view) say it is not.
2
Analyze the opponent's primary dalil
Quran 2:106: 'Whatever verse We cancel or cause to be forgotten, We bring better than it or similar to it.' How does the opponent use this to require a replacement?
3
Unpack the Hanafi interpretation
The Hanafi response interprets 'khayr or mithl' as referring to the wording (fascaha, balagha, i'jaz), not the legal ruling. Two interpretations are given.
First: abrogation of recitation with replacement in wording. Second: if ruling, then specification to verse-by-verse abrogation.
4
Examine the examples of naskh without replacement
The najwa verse (Surah al-Mujadilah) was abrogated before anyone acted except Ali. The prohibition of eating after sleep was also abrogated. Verify if these truly lack a new ruling.
The passage argues the najwa verse abrogation had no new obligation; the sleep verse actually permits, so not pure naskh, but the author still uses it.
5
Evaluate the counter-arguments and specification
Discussion of specification to verse-by-verse abrogation, and the response that the abrogation itself (the removal) is a benefit (khayr) for the mukallaf.
The author also addresses the claim from al-Mukhtasar and al-Shafi'i that a farḍ must be replaced by a farḍ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قدمت بين يدي نجواي درهماً ثم نسخت فلم يعمل بها أحد أَشْفَقْتُمْ أَن تُقَدِّمُوا بَيْنَ يَدَى نَجْوَنَكُمْ صَدَقَتِ ﴾ [المجادلة : ۱۳] الآيات وروى عبد الرزاق عن أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأشجعين علي كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام قال ما عمل بها أحد غيري حتى نسخت وما كانت إلا ساعة نعني آية النجوى. كذا في «الدرر المنثورة». فالآية الناسخة لا تدل على حكم شرعي بل على ارتفاع الحكم الأول فقط، لكن لا بد ههنا من دليل على جواز الصدقة، بل استحبابها بعد هذا النسخ والعمومات السابقة لا تكفي فإن آية النجوى ناسخة لها، فقد ارتفعت من البين فلا بد من دليل بعد النسخ ولعله سهل، ولنا أيضاً انتساخ تحريم الإفطار بعد العشاء والنوم قد انتسخ ، وفيه أن الناسخ قوله تعالى: ﴿عَلِمَ اللهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَعَفَا عَنكُمْ فَالْكَنَ بَشِرُوهُنَّ وَابْتَغُوا مَا كَتَبَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الْأَسْوَدِ مِنَ الْفَجْرِ ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى الَّيلِ [البقرة : ۱۸۷]. وفيه إباحة المباشرة والأكل والشرب منصوصة فليس من الباب في شيء فافهم. مانعو النسخ لا إلى بدل (قالوا) قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَا نَنسَحْ مِنْ ءَايَةٍ أَوْ نُنسِهَا نَأْتِ بِخَيْرٍ مِّنْهَا أَوْ مِثْلِهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ١٠٦] فلا بد من حكم خير أو مثل وهو البدل (قلنا : المراد من الخير أو المثل (اللفظ) يعني في الفصاحة والبلاغة والإعجاز والنزاع) في الحكم) يحتمل وجهين : أحدهم : نسخ التلاوة والمعنى: لا ننسخ تلاوة آية إلا أن نأتي بدلها ما هو خير منها أو مثلها وعلى هذا فالإنساء أي شيء هو كلمة أو مانعة عن كونه تفسير النسخ . والثاني : النسخ نسخ الحكم والمعنى كلما ننسخ من حكم آية أو ننسها يعني : ننسخ تلاوتها نأت بناسخ خير منها أو مثلها في الفصاحة والبلاغة وعلى هذا لا بد من التخصيص. يعني ما ننسخ من آية بآية وإلا امتنع انتساخ الآية بالسنة ولو سلم أن ليس المراد اللفظ في الفصاحة والبلاغة (فلعله أي النسخ بلا) بدل خير للمكلف لمصلحة فيه فلا يلزم البدل، وفيه أن الإتيان لا يساعده، فإن ذلك لا يكون إلا للفظ أو الحكم وإذا سلم عدم إرادة الأول تعين الثاني، ولعل هذا مراد ما في «التحرير»، وأما ادعاء أن من البدل على التنزل ترك البدل فليس بصحيح، إذ ليس ترك البدل حكماً شرعياً والنزاع فيه ولك أن تقول : الإتيان : الإنزال للحكم بإنزال ألفاظ دالة عليه، ولا يلزم منه أن يكون هو حكماً شرعياً، بل يجوز أن يكون حكماً آخر، والناسخ الذي لا يدل على إقامة حكم شرعي بدل المنسوخ يدل على حكم ما، ولا أقل من رفع الشارع حكمه الأول، ويكون هذا الرفع خيراً للمكلف في المعاش، فقد أتى بحكم ولو غير شرعي خير ،له فقد بان مساعدة الإتيان وسقط الإيراد فافهم، وقد يجاب بالتخصيص بما لا يكون لا إلى بدل لا بتجويز التخصيص واحتماله فقد حتى يرد عليه ما في «التحرير» أن احتمال التخصيص لا يستلزم ،وقوعه بل الدلالة من مخصص، وهو وقوع النسخ لا إلى بدل كما تقدم، وقد يجاب أيضاً بأن غاية ما لزم منه عدم الوقوع والمدعي عدم الجواز، فما تم التقريب وتعقب عليه في «التحرير» أن مدعاهم نفي الوقوع، وأما الجواز فضروري، فلا ينبغي أن ينكره عاقل فتأمل واعلم أن شارح المختصر حرر النزاع في نسخ التكليف من غير تكليف الأصل الأول/ الكتاب آخر) وإن كان عبارة «المختصر الجمهور على جواز النسخ من غير بدل وتمحلوا العدم مطابقة المتن فقيل : أراد بالتكليف حكماً من الأحكام الخمسة فإن التكليف قد يطلق مقابل الوضع أيضاً، وقيل: فرض المسألة في جزئي من جزئياته، والظاهر أنه حمل البدل في المختصر على التكليف لما أن استدلاله قرينة عليه كما قال ودل) عليه كلام ابن الحاجب، فإنه استدل عليه بالنهي عن ادخار لحوم الأضاحي محرماً ثم نسخه مبيحاً، وهو الأشبه بدليل الخصم : فإن المماثلة أقل (الدرجتين ولا مماثلة بين الإباحة والتكليف، فهو قرينة على ذلك الحمل، وفيه أن المماثلة من جميع الوجوه غير لازمة (وهو) (المنصوص) من الإمام الشافعي في رسالة الأم كما في بعض شروح المنهاج (قال : لا ينسخ فرض أبداً إلا ويثبت مكانه فرض هذا وقد تأولوا الفرض بالحكم، وهو كما ترى .
He (the Prophet) said: 'I presented before my Najwa a dirham, then it was abrogated, and no one acted upon it.' Did you fear that you should present before your Najwa a charity? The verses. And Abd al-Razzaq narrated from the Commander of the Faithful and Imam of the Lions, Ali (may God honor his face and the faces of his noble family), who said: 'No one acted upon it except me, until it was abrogated, and it was only an hour.' I mean the verse of Najwa. As in 'al-Durar al-Manthur'. So the abrogating verse does not indicate a legal ruling but only the elevation of the first ruling. However, here there must be evidence for the permissibility of charity, even its recommendation after this abrogation, and the previous generalities are not sufficient, because the verse of Najwa is an abrogator of them, so it has been removed from consideration, so there must be evidence after abrogation. And perhaps it is easy. And we also have the abrogation of the prohibition of breaking the fast after 'Isha' and sleep, it has been abrogated. And in it, the abrogator is the saying of the Most High: 'God knows that you were betraying yourselves, so He turned to you and pardoned you, so now consort with them and seek what God has prescribed for you, and eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn, then complete the fast until night [2:187]. And in it, the permission of intercourse and eating and drinking is explicitly stated, so it is not from the chapter at all, so understand. Those who deny naskh without a replacement said: God Most High said: 'Whatever verse We cancel or cause to be forgotten, We bring better than it or similar to it [2:106], so there must be a ruling that is better or similar, which is the replacement. We said: The meaning of 'better or similar' is the wording, meaning in eloquence and rhetoric and inimitability and the dispute [about the ruling]? It admits two aspects: first, abrogation of recitation, meaning: We do not abrogate the recitation of a verse except that We bring its replacement that is better than it or similar to it. On this, the forgetting is something that is a word or preventing it from being an interpretation of abrogation. Second, abrogation of the ruling, meaning: Whenever We abrogate the ruling of a verse or cause it to be forgotten, meaning We abrogate its recitation, We bring an abrogator better than it or similar to it in eloquence and rhetoric. On this, specification is necessary, meaning that We only abrogate a verse with a verse; otherwise, the abrogation of the verse by the Sunnah is prohibited. Even if it is conceded that the intended meaning is not the wording in eloquence and rhetoric, then perhaps it (i.e., the abrogation without replacement) is better for the responsible person due to a benefit in it, so replacement is not necessary. In it, the 'bringing' does not support it, for that is only for wording or ruling, and if the first is not intended, the second is determined. Perhaps this is the meaning of what is in 'al-Tahrir'. And as for the claim that replacement includes the abandonment of replacement as a concession, it is not correct, since the abandonment of replacement is not a legal ruling, and the dispute is about it. But you may say: The 'bringing' is the revealing of the ruling by revealing words indicating it, and it does not necessitate that it be a legal ruling; rather, it is permissible that it be another ruling. And the abrogator that does not indicate the establishment of a legal ruling as a replacement for the abrogated indicates some ruling, and at the least, the Lawgiver's removal of His first ruling, and this removal is better for the responsible person in his livelihood, so he has brought a ruling, even if non-legal, that is better for him. So the support of 'bringing' is clear, and the objection falls, so understand. And it may be answered by specification to what is not without a replacement, not by permitting specification and its possibility, until what is in 'al-Tahrir' is challenged, that the possibility of specification does not necessitate its occurrence, but the evidence is from a specifier, and it is the occurrence of naskh without a replacement as previously. And it may also be answered that the utmost that follows from it is non-occurrence, and the claimant claims impossibility, so the approximation is not complete. And it was criticized in 'al-Tahrir' that their claim is negation of occurrence, and as for permissibility, it is necessary, so no sensible person should deny it. So reflect. And know that the commentator of 'al-Mukhtasar' discussed the dispute in the abrogation of obligation without obligation. (The first principle/the book last) and if it is the expression of 'al-Mukhtasar': the majority allow abrogation without replacement, and they struggled with the non-conformity of the text. So it was said: He intended by 'obligation' a ruling from the five rulings, for 'obligation' may also be used in contrast to 'situational'. And it was said: He made the issue a particular of its particulars. And the apparent is that he carried 'replacement' in 'al-Mukhtasar' as 'obligation' because his proof is a clue for it, as he said. And the speech of Ibn al-Hajib indicates it, for he proved it by the prohibition of storing the meat of sacrificial animals as forbidden, then abrogating it as permissible, and it is more similar to the proof of the opponent: for the similarity is of the two degrees, and there is no similarity between permissibility and obligation, so it is a clue for that interpretation. And in it, similarity from all respects is not necessary. And (it) (the text) from Imam al-Shafi'i in the Risala of al-Umm, as in some commentaries of al-Minhaj, he said: 'A farḍ is never abrogated except that a farḍ is established in its place.' This, and they interpreted farḍ as ruling, and it is as you see.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage deals with the issue of naskh (abrogation) without a replacement (badal). The author begins with an example: the verse of Najwa (Surah al-Mujadilah) required giving charity before speaking to the Prophet, but it was abrogated before anyone acted on it except 'Ali. This shows that naskh can occur without a new ruling being established. The opponents argue from Quran 2:106 that whenever a verse is abrogated, a better or similar one is brought, implying a replacement. The author responds by interpreting 'better or similar' as referring to the wording (fascaha, balagha, i'jaz), not the ruling. Two interpretations are given: either the abrogation of recitation or the abrogation of the ruling with a replacement in wording. If the latter, then specification to verse-by-verse abrogation is needed, preventing abrogation by Sunnah. Alternatively, even if the wording interpretation is not accepted, the abrogation itself (without replacement) can be beneficial for the mukallaf, and the 'bringing' in the verse can be understood as bringing a ruling (even non-legal) of removal. The author also cites examples of naskh without replacement, like the abrogation of the prohibition of eating and drinking after sleep. The discussion continues with textual analysis of al-Mukhtasar and positions of al-Shafi'i, who holds that a farḍ must be replaced by another farḍ, but the Hanafis interpret this through specification and other arguments. Overall, the passage defends the Hanafi position that naskh without a replacement is both possible and has occurred.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Cancellation of a legal ruling by a later divine text
بدل (badal): A replacement ruling brought in place of an abrogated one
ناسخ (nasikh): The abrogating text that invalidates the previous ruling
منسوخ (mansukh): The abrogated ruling that is no longer applicable

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what does the phrase 'khayr' or 'mithl' in Quran 2:106 primarily refer to?
A) The ruling of the abrogated verse
B) The wording and eloquence of the verse
C) The reward of the abrogated verse
D) The act of worship prescribed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits naskh without a replacement by interpreting Quran 2:106's 'better or similar' as referring to wording, not ruling, and by citing actual occurrences like the abrogation of the najwa verse.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Permissibility of Naskh to a Heavier Ruling
Proving the permissibility of naskh to a heavier ruling through rational and textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul argument for naskh to a heavier ruling and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the evidence from maslahah and historical occurrences.

Core Idea
Abrogation can introduce a heavier ruling because divine wisdom may place benefit in difficulty, and revelation itself provides examples.

The permissibility of abrogating a lighter ruling with a heavier one is a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree on naskh to lighter or equal rulings, the Hanafis argue that naskh to a heavier ruling is valid based on both rational consideration of maslahah and actual examples from the Quran and Sunnah. This passage presents the Hanafi case with three key instances: the fast of 'Ashura' superseded by Ramadan, the punishment for zina from imprisonment to flogging/stoning, and the option of fasting or fidyah replaced by obligatory fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue and the two positions
State the ruling at issue: whether naskh to a heavier ruling is permissible. Note that the Hanafi school (with the majority) says yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly says no.
The term 'heavier' (athqal) refers to a ruling that imposes a greater obligation or hardship.
2
Analyse the Hanafi rational proof based on maslahah
Understand the argument: since divine rulings are based on benefit (maslahah), it is possible that benefit lies in making a ruling heavier. Moreover, God may will any transition He chooses.
This is a rational proof relying on the nature of legislation.
3
Examine the three occurrence examples
For each example (fast of 'Ashura', zina punishment, optional fasting/fidyah), identify the lighter ruling and the heavier replacement. Confirm that the new ruling is indeed more difficult.
The author argues that occurrence of these abrogations proves permissibility; if it were impossible, they would not have occurred.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Note the objection that the 'way' (sabil) in the zina verse might not be an abrogation but a specification. The Hanafi response is that the verse itself indicates abrogation, and the Companion's interpretation is authoritative.
The author also addresses the hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' as direct evidence of naskh from an option to an obligation.

الأثقل (وإلا) تعتبر المصلحة فيها (فليفعل الله ما يريد) من الأخف إلى الأثقل ولنا أيضاً الوقوع ولو لم يجز لم يقع (فنسخ عاشوراء فيجوز الانتقال من وبين فدية برمضان) وقد مر تخريجه والظاهر أن انتساخه بالتخيير بين صيام شهر رمضان كله كل صوم ولا شك أن هذا التخيير أشق على الإنسان من صوم يوم واحد وإنكاره مكابرة. وأما على قول من يقول : لم يشرع تخيير قط، بل أوجب الصوم في شهر رمضان كله ابتداء بدل هذا الصوم الواحد والآية في حق الشيخ الفاني فالأمر أظهر والحبس في البيوت الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّتِي يَأْتِينَ الْفَاحِشَةَ مِن نِسَابِكُمْ فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ فَإِن شَهِدُوا فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ في الْبُيُوتِ حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ فَهُنَّ سَبِيلًا [النساء : ١٥] (بالحد) وهو الجلد أو الرجم روى البيهقي في سننه عن ابن عباس في الآية قال : كانت المرأة إذا زنت حبست في البيت حتى تموت فأنزل الله بعد ذلك : الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ ﴾ [النور: ٢] هذا فإن كانا محصنين رجما فهذا السبيل الذي جعل لها كذا في الدرر المنثورة»، وقد روي بطرق كثيرة إن شئت فارجع إليه . ولا شك أن الحبس أهون من الرجم الذي يموت فيه بيقين والجلد الذي قلما يبرأ وقول الصحابي في أخبار النسخ حجة، فلا يعتد بما قال البيضاوي، ويحتمل أن يكون المراد التوصية بإمساكهن بعد الجلد يجري عليهم ما جرى بسبب الخروج والتعرض للرجال ولم يذكر الحد استغناء بقوله : ﴿ الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ [النور: ٢] نعم يرد عليه أن الحكم موقت بجعل السبيل فانتفاؤه فيما بعد الغاية لا يكون من النسخ في شيء، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالسبيل نسخ هذا الحكم يعني : عليكم أيها الحكام حبسهن إلى الموت إلى أن ينسخ هذا الحكم ويجعل سبيل آخر فافهم. ولنا أيضاً انتساخ التخيير بين الصوم والفدية روى الشيخان وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي والدارمي الحاكم والبيهقي عن سلمة بن الأكوع قال : لما نزلت هذه الآية: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مسكين ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٤] كان من شاء منا صام ومن شاء يفطر ويفتدي قال : حتى نزلت الآية التي
Issue: Naskh to a lighter or equal (ruling) is permissible by agreement. As for naskh to a heavier (ruling), it is likewise permissible according to the majority, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him. For us: if benefit is considered in rulings, as is the truth, then perhaps it lies in it, i.e., in the transition from lighter to heavier. And if it is not considered, then God does what He wills from lighter to heavier. And we also have occurrence, and if it were not permissible, it would not have occurred. For the abrogation of 'Ashura' (fasting) is allowed to transition from and between a fidyah with Ramadan. And its derivation has already been mentioned, and the apparent is that its abrogation is with the option between fasting all of Ramadan or all fasting, and there is no doubt that this option is more difficult for a person than fasting one day, and its denial is obstinacy. And as for the one who says no option was legislated at all, but rather he obligated fasting in all of Ramadan from the beginning as a replacement for this single fast, and the verse is regarding the elderly person, the matter is more apparent. And the imprisonment in houses established by His saying: 'And those who commit immorality among your women, seek against them four witnesses from among you; if they testify, then detain them in the houses until death takes them or God makes for them a way [4:15] (with the hadd), which is flogging or stoning. Al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan from Ibn Abbas regarding the verse: 'When a woman committed adultery, she was imprisoned in the house until she died, then God revealed after that: 'The adulteress and the adulterer, flog each one of them one hundred lashes [24:2]. This, and if they are muhsan, they are stoned. This is the way that was made for them. As in al-Durar al-Manthur. And it has been narrated by many paths; if you wish, refer to it. And there is no doubt that imprisonment is easier than stoning, in which one certainly dies, and flogging from which one rarely recovers. And the statement of a Companion in reports of naskh is a proof, so what al-Baydawi said is not considered. And it is possible that the intent is the recommendation to detain them after flogging due to what happens to them because of going out and exposure to men, and he did not mention the hadd, relying on His saying: 'The adulteress and the adulterer, flog each one of them one hundred lashes [24:2]. Yes, it is objected that the ruling is temporal with the making of a way, so its absence after the limit is not naskh at all. Unless it is said that the intended meaning of 'way' is the abrogation of this ruling, meaning: O rulers, detain them until death until this ruling is abrogated and another way is made, so understand. And we also have the abrogation of the option between fasting and fidyah. Al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Darimi, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Salamah ibn al-Akwa' who said: When this verse was revealed: 'And upon those who are able, a fidyah of feeding a poor person [2:184], whoever of us wished fasted, and whoever wished broke the fast and paid fidyah. He said: until the verse was revealed which
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of naskh to a heavier (athqal) ruling. The author states that naskh to a lighter or equal ruling is agreed upon, but naskh to a heavier ruling is permissible according to the majority (jumhur), contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi argument is based on considering maslahah (benefit) in rulings: it is possible that benefit lies in the transition to a heavier ruling. Also, actual occurrence proves permissibility. The author then provides examples: first, the abrogation of the optional fast of 'Ashura' by the obligatory fast of Ramadan, which is heavier because it requires fasting a whole month (or the option). Second, the abrogation of the punishment for zina from life imprisonment (as in Surah al-Nisa 4:15) to flogging and stoning (Surah al-Nur 24:2). Imprisonment is lighter than stoning or flogging, so the new ruling is heavier. The author addresses a potential objection that the 'way' (sabil) in 4:15 refers to a new ruling, not abrogation, and responds that the verse itself indicates abrogation. Third, the abrogation of the option between fasting and feeding (fidyah) as mentioned in the hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa'. The passage defends the Hanafi position that naskh can be to a heavier ruling, using rational and textual evidence.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Cancellation of a legal ruling by a later divine text
أثقل (athqal): Heavier, more difficult ruling
أخف (akhaf): Lighter, easier ruling
مصلحة (maslahah): Benefit or welfare considered in legislation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Hanafi evidence for the permissibility of naskh to a heavier ruling?
A) Consensus of the Sahaba
B) Consideration of maslahah and actual occurrence
C) Analogy to naskh of the Quran
D) The principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates naskh to a heavier ruling based on maslahah and historical instances, affirming that divine legislation may increase difficulty for greater benefit.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
12 min
Permissibility of Naskh to a Heavier Ruling
Argues for permissibility of abrogation to a heavier ruling, rebutting Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument for the permissibility of naskh (abrogation) to a heavier ruling and explain why the Shafi'i objection is rebutted.

Core Idea
Abrogation to a heavier ruling is permissible because maslaha may demand it and it has occurred in revelation.

This passage addresses a key dispute in usul al-fiqh: whether a ruling can be abrogated by a more burdensome one. While the Shafi'i school argues that this contradicts the principle of ease, the Hanafi school maintains it is possible, citing both rational considerations of maslaha and explicit examples from the Quran and Sunnah. In this lesson, we will examine the arguments on both sides and understand the Hanafi method of combining reason and revelation.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the exact question: Is naskh from a lighter ruling to a heavier ruling permissible? State the Hanafi (majority) position (yes) and the Shafi'i position (no).
This sets the stage for the dispute.
2
Examine the Hanafi rational proof
Understand the principle that rulings are based on maslaha. If maslaha requires a heavier ruling, it is permissible. Also, the transfer from original innocence to obligation is itself a move from lighter to heavier, yet it is agreed upon.
The Hanafi response uses 'naqd' (refutation by counterexample).
3
Analyze the Hanafi textual proof
Consider the three examples: abrogation of Ashura by Ramadan, abrogation of the choice between fasting and fidyah, and abrogation of house confinement by hadd. Each shows a heavier ruling replacing a lighter one.
The author argues that actual occurrence proves permissibility.
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i objection cites Quran 2:185 ('Allah desires ease'). The Hanafi response distinguishes between general principle and specific instances, and notes that the verse does not preclude occasional heavier rulings when maslaha requires.
Also, the rebuttal addresses the claim of remoteness from maslaha.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence is whether later heavier rulings can abrogate earlier lighter ones. The author clearly favors the Hanafi position, and this is the relied-upon view in Hanafi usul.
This conclusion affects how Hanafi jurists interpret apparent conflicts in revelation.

الأثقل (وإلا) تعتبر المصلحة فيها (فليفعل الله ما يريد) من الأخف إلى الأثقل ولنا أيضاً الوقوع ولو لم يجز لم يقع (فنسخ عاشوراء فيجوز الانتقال من ● وبين فدية برمضان) وقد مر تخريجه والظاهر أن انتساخه الصوم الواحد والآية في حق الشيخ الفاني فالأمر أظهر والحبس في البيوت الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّتِي يَأْتِينَ الْفَاحِشَةَ مِن نِسَابِكُمْ فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِّنكُمْ فَإِن شَهِدُوا فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ في الْبُيُوتِ حَتَّى يَتَوَفَّهُنَّ الْمَوْتُ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ فَهُنَّ سَبِيلًا [النساء : ١٥] (بالحد) وهو الجلد أو الرجم روى البيهقي في سننه عن ابن عباس في الآية قال : كانت المرأة إذا زنت حبست في البيت حتى تموت فأنزل الله بعد ذلك : الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ ﴾ [النور: ٢] هذا فإن كانا محصنين رجما فهذا السبيل الذي جعل لها كذا في الدرر المنثورة»، وقد روي بطرق كثيرة إن شئت فارجع إليه . ولا شك أن الحبس أهون من الرجم الذي يموت فيه بيقين والجلد الذي قلما يبرأ وقول الصحابي في أخبار النسخ حجة، فلا يعتد بما قال البيضاوي، ويحتمل أن يكون المراد التوصية بإمساكهن بعد الجلد يجري عليهم ما جرى بسبب الخروج والتعرض للرجال ولم يذكر الحد استغناء بقوله : ﴿ الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ [النور: ٢] نعم يرد عليه أن الحكم موقت بجعل السبيل فانتفاؤه فيما بعد الغاية لا يكون من النسخ في شيء، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالسبيل نسخ هذا الحكم يعني : عليكم أيها الحكام حبسهن إلى الموت إلى أن ينسخ هذا الحكم ويجعل سبيل آخر فافهم. ولنا أيضاً انتساخ التخيير بين الصوم والفدية روى الشيخان وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي والدارمي والحاكم والبيهقي عن سلمة بن الأكوع قال : لما نزلت هذه الآية: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مسكين ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٤] كان من شاء منا صام ومن شاء يفطر ويفتدي قال : حتى نزلت الآية التي بعدها فنسختها: ﴿فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸٥] وروى البخاري عن ابن أبي ليلى : حدثنا أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم نزل رمضان فشق عليهم فكان من أطعم كل يوم مسكيناً يترك الصوم ممن يطيقه، ورخص لهم في ذلك فنسخها وأن تصوموا خير لكم فأمر بالصوم. وروى ابن أبي شيبة والبخاري عن ابن عمر أنه كان يقرأ : طعام مساكين، وقال نسختها الآية التي بعدها فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليصمه وأخبار الصحابة لا سيما مثل ابن عمر في الانتساخ ،مقبولة، فإن قلت : روى البخاري وعبد الرزاق والدارقطني والبيهقي من طرق عن ابن عباس أنه كان يقرأ : وعلى الذين يطوّقونه مشددة يكلفونه ولا يطيقونه، ويقول : ليست هي بمنسوخة، وهو الشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة يطعمون لكل يوم مسكيناً ولا يقضون، قلت: :أولاً: قد ثبت عن ابن عباس ،معارضه، فإنه روى أبو داود عنه : وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] فكان شاء من منكم أن يفتدي بطعام مسكين افتدى وتم له صومه فقال : فَمَن تَطَوَّعَ خَيْرًا فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَهُ وَأَن تَصُومُوا خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] وقال: ﴿فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۵] الآية وفي رواية أخرى لأبي داود والبيهقي عنه : كان رخصة للشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة وهما يطيقان الصوم أن يفطرا ويطعما مكان كل يوم مسكيناً، ثم نسخت بعد ذلك، فقال الله : فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٥] وأثبت للشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة إذا كانا لا يطيقان الصوم أن يفطرا أو يطعما وللحبلى والمرضع إذا خافتا أفطرتا وأطعمتا كل يوم مسكيناً ولا قضاء عليهما . وثانياً : أنه رضي الله تعالى عنه إنما حكم بأحكام القراءة المشددة، ولسنا ندعي أيضاً انتساخه وإنما ندعي انتساخ قراءة التخفيف الذي الآن يقرأ في القرآن غاية في الباب أن في قراءة التشديد لكونها منقولة أحاداً ليست باقية على القرآنية من جملة منسوخ التلاوة. وثالثاً : بعد التنزل أن سلمة رضي الله عنه أخبر أن الناس كانوا يفطرون ويفتدون، فليس هناك محل الاجتهاد بخلاف الحل على نفي الطاقة والحكم ببقائها فإنه مما يسوغ أن يكون بالاجتهاد، فلا يصلح معارضاً فتدبر المانعون (قالوا :أولاً : النقل) من الأخف (إلى الأثقل أبعد من المصلحة) فلا يصح (قلنا) هذا (منقوض بالنقل إلى التكليف من البراءة الأصلية) فإن هذا أيضاً نقل من الأخف إلى الأثقل، فيكون أبعد من المصلحة (أقول) في الدفع (البراءة) الأصلية (ليس) والتذكير لعله لرعاية الخبر حكماً شرعياً حتى يكون التكليف نقلاً منها (وإنما الكلام فيه فإن قلت : ليس في النقل شناعة إلا لأجل إيقاعه في العسر بعدما كان في اليسر، وهو متحقق ههنا، فينبغي أن لا يصح فانتقض دليلهم قلت لم يكن هناك يسر من الشارع، وإنما كان البراءة للجهل من المصالح فإذ قد تفضل الحكيم فكلف على حسب المصالح، فلا نقل من اليسر الثابت منه بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن اليسر كان من الشارع الحكيم فتدبر (والحق) في الدفع (منع البعد) في النقل من الأيسر إلى الأثقل فقد يكون الأثقل بعد الأخف أصلح للمكلف، والحكيم يكلف على حسب المصالح تفضلاً منه علينا لا وجوباً حتى يرجع إلى الاعتزال (و) قالوا (ثانياً) قال تعالى: ﴿يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْمُسْرَ
Issue: The permissibility of abrogation with a lighter or equal [ruling] is agreed upon. As for [abrogation] with a heavier [ruling], it is likewise permissible according to the majority, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. Our proof is that if maslaha (public interest) is considered in rulings—as is the truth—then perhaps it is present in the transition from lighter to heavier. And if not, then Allah does what He wills, from lighter to heavier. We also have [the proof of] actual occurrence; had it not been permissible, it would not have occurred. Thus, the abrogation of [the obligation of fasting] Ashura by [the obligation of fasting] Ramadan—the transition from one day's fast to the entire month is heavier—and likewise the abrogation of the choice between fasting and ransom. Also the abrogation of the penalty of house confinement (for adultery) by the prescribed punishment (hadd) of flogging or stoning, which is heavier. The opponents said: First, the transfer from lighter to heavier is more remote from maslaha, so it is invalid. We reply: This is refuted by the transfer from the original state of innocence to [legal] obligation, which is also a transfer from lighter to heavier and thus more remote from maslaha. The correct response is to deny the remoteness: sometimes the heavier after the lighter is more beneficial for the obligated person, and the Wise [Lawgiver] imposes obligations according to maslaha, as a favor upon us, not as an obligation (so as to lead to Mu'tazilism). And they also said: Allah says, 'Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the permissibility of abrogating a lighter ruling by a heavier one. The author presents the Hanafi position (which is also the position of the majority of scholars) and refutes the Shafi'i school which prohibits such naskh. The Hanafi proof is twofold: (1) rational: since rulings are based on maslaha, the Legislator may deem a heavier ruling more beneficial at a later time, and He is not obligated to maintain ease; (2) textual: there are clear instances of naskh to a heavier ruling in the Quran and Sunnah, such as the abrogation of the voluntary fast of Ashura by the obligation of Ramadan fasting, the abrogation of the choice between fasting and feeding the poor (for those who could fast but were given an option) by the absolute obligation of Ramadan fast, and the abrogation of house confinement for adulteresses by the prescribed punishment (hadd) of flogging or stoning. The author addresses the Shafi'i objection that naskh to heavier contradicts the principle of ease in the Quran (2:185) by explaining that the verse is general and does not preclude occasional heavier rulings for greater benefit. The discussion is thorough, including rebuttal of the opposing evidence and clarification of the Hanafi methodology. This is a classic usul al-fiqh argument demonstrating the Hanafi reliance on both rational consideration of maslaha and empirical evidence from revelation.

Key Terms
النَّسْخ (al-naskh): Legal abrogation: the replacement of a previous ruling (ḥukm) by a later one from the same source (Quran or Sunnah).
الأَثْقَل (al-athqal): A ruling that is more burdensome (heavier in obligation) relative to another ruling.
الْمَصْلَحَة (al-maslaḥah): Public interest or benefit; the consideration that underlies the wisdom of divine rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual example used by the author to demonstrate that naskh to a heavier ruling has occurred?
A) Abrogation of the punishment for theft by amputation
B) Abrogation of the fast of Ashura by the obligation of Ramadan fasting
C) Abrogation of the permission for mut'ah (temporary marriage)
D) Abrogation of the prohibition of alcohol

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that naskh to a heavier ruling is permissible, supported by rational consideration of maslaha and confirmed by actual abrogations in the Quran and Sunnah.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
Abrogation of the Fasting Verse and Reports of Companions
Discussion of naskh with companion reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for naskh by analyzing the abrogation of the fidya verse and evaluating conflicting companion reports.

Core Idea
The verse of fasting abrogated the option of fidya for the able; Ibn Abbas's reading is ahad and does not contradict naskh.

This lesson explores the abrogation of the verse that allowed a person able to fast to instead feed a poor person (2:184) by the later verse commanding fasting for those who witness the month (2:185). The Hanafi school relies on explicit Quranic command and companion testimony. We will examine reports from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas, resolving an apparent contradiction using usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting texts
First, recognize the two Quranic verses: 2:184 gives an option to feed a poor person instead of fasting; 2:185 commands fasting for those who witness the month. The Hanafi claim is that 2:185 abrogated the option for those able to fast.
The principle is that a later, unambiguous command abrogates an earlier permission.
2
Examine the companion reports
Read the reports from Ibn Umar confirming abrogation and from Ibn Abbas apparently denying it. Note that the author presents multiple narrations from Ibn Abbas showing he eventually confirmed abrogation.
The weight of companion testimony is significant in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The objection cites Ibn Abbas's reading with tashdeed (shaddah) implying inability, which he said is not abrogated. The author gives three counter-arguments: (1) Ibn Abbas himself narrated abrogation, (2) his reading is ahad and not Quranic, and (3) the ruling on inability is a matter of ijtihad, not a valid objection.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting reports.
4
Apply the usul principle of naskh
Apply the Hanafi rule: naskh requires a later text (2:185) that is clear in meaning (zam) and certain in transmission (mutawatir). The ahad reading of Ibn Abbas cannot stand against the explicit command of the Quran.
Thus, the option of fidya for the able is abrogated; fidya remains only for those permanently unable.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that fasting is obligatory for those who witness the month and are able; feeding a poor person is not a substitute. This is the relied-upon ruling.
The dispute with the hypothetical opponent is resolved through usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعدها فنسختها: ﴿فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸٥] وروى البخاري عن ابن أبي ليلى : حدثنا أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم نزل رمضان فشق عليهم فكان من أطعم كل يوم مسكيناً يترك الصوم ممن يطيقه، ورخص لهم في ذلك فنسخها وأن تصوموا خير لكم فأمر بالصوم. وروى ابن أبي شيبة والبخاري عن ابن عمر أنه كان يقرأ : طعام مساكين، وقال نسختها الآية التي بعدها فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليصمه وأخبار الصحابة لا سيما مثل ابن عمر في الانتساخ ،مقبولة، فإن قلت : روى البخاري وعبد الرزاق والدارقطني والبيهقي من طرق عن ابن عباس أنه كان يقرأ : وعلى الذين يطوّقونه مشددة يكلفونه ولا يطيقونه، ويقول : ليست هي بمنسوخة، وهو الشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة يطعمون لكل يوم مسكيناً ولا يقضون، قلت: :أولاً: قد ثبت عن ابن عباس ،معارضه، فإنه روى أبو داود عنه : وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] فكان شاء من منكم أن يفتدي بطعام مسكين افتدى وتم له صومه فقال : فَمَن تَطَوَّعَ خَيْرًا فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَهُ وَأَن تَصُومُوا خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] وقال: ﴿فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۵] الآية وفي رواية أخرى لأبي داود والبيهقي عنه : كان رخصة للشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة وهما يطيقان الصوم أن يفطرا ويطعما مكان كل يوم مسكيناً، ثم نسخت بعد ذلك، فقال الله : فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٥] وأثبت للشيخ الكبير والعجوز الكبيرة إذا كانا لا يطيقان الصوم أن يفطرا أو يطعما وللحبلى والمرضع إذا خافتا أفطرتا وأطعمتا كل يوم مسكيناً ولا قضاء عليهما . وثانياً : أنه رضي الله تعالى عنه إنما حكم بأحكام القراءة المشددة، ولسنا ندعي أيضاً انتساخه وإنما ندعي انتساخ قراءة التخفيف الذي الآن يقرأ في القرآن غاية في الباب أن في قراءة التشديد لكونها منقولة أحاداً ليست باقية على القرآنية من جملة منسوخ التلاوة. ، وثالثاً : بعد التنزل أن سلمة رضي الله عنه أخبر أن الناس كانوا يفطرون ويفتدون، فليس هناك محل الاجتهاد بخلاف الحل على نفي الطاقة والحكم ببقائها فإنه مما يسوغ أن يكون بالاجتهاد، فلا يصلح معارضاً فتدبر المانعون
Afterwards, it was abrogated: {So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it} (2:185). Al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn Abi Layla: The companions of Muhammad (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) told us: Ramadan was revealed and it was difficult for them, so whoever fed a poor person each day left fasting while being able to do it, and permission was given for that, then {And that you fast is better for you} abrogated it, so he ordered fasting. And Ibn Abi Shayba and Bukhari narrated from Ibn Umar that he used to recite 'food for the poor' and said: The following verse abrogated it: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it'. And reports of the companions, especially like Ibn Umar regarding abrogation, are acceptable. If you say: Bukhari, Abd al-Razzaq, al-Daraqutni, and al-Bayhaqi narrated through multiple chains from Ibn Abbas that he used to recite {And upon those who are able to bear it (with tashdeed: are burdened and cannot bear it)} and said it is not abrogated, and it is about the old man and old woman who feed a poor person each day and do not make up (the fast). I say: First, an opposing report is established from Ibn Abbas, for Abu Dawud narrated from him: {And upon those who are able to fast, a ransom} (2:184) so whoever wished among you to ransom by feeding a poor person did so and his fast was complete. Then He said: {But whoever volunteers good, it is better for him, and that you fast is better for you} (2:184) and He said: {So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it} (2:185). In another narration from Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi from him: It was a concession for the old man and old woman, while they are able to fast, to break fast and feed a poor person for each day, then it was abrogated after that, so Allah said: {So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it} (2:185) and He affirmed for the old man and old woman if they cannot fast, they break fast and feed, and for the pregnant and nursing if they fear, they break fast and feed a poor person each day and no making up is upon them. Second: He (Ibn Abbas) only judged according to the reading of the shaddah (tashdeed), and we do not claim its abrogation, but we claim the abrogation of the reading of the takhfif (lightening) which is now recited in the Quran. The point is that the reading of tashdeed, being transmitted as ahad, does not remain as Quranic; it is among the abrogated of recitation. Third: After concession, Salamah (radiyallahu anhu) informed that the people used to break fast and ransom, so there is no room for ijtihad, unlike the ruling on denying ability and judging its continuance, which may be based on ijtihad. So it is not a valid objection. Contemplate, O opponents.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a naskh analysis discussing the abrogation of the fasting verse. It begins by stating that the verse commanding fasting for those who witness the month abrogated the earlier permission to feed a poor person. It then presents reports from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. For Ibn Abbas, there is an apparent contradiction which the author resolves by pointing to the different readings (tashdeed vs. takhfif) and the status of the ahad reading. The author concludes that the objection from Ibn Abbas's reading is not valid, as his own reports confirm abrogation, and his reading is not part of the Quran. This is a typical Hanafi approach to reconciling conflicting companion reports regarding naskh.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.
آحاد (ahad): A report transmitted through a limited chain of narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
مشدد / مخفف (mushaddad / mukhaffaf): With tashdeed (shaddah) meaning 'are burdened' vs. without tashdeed meaning 'are able'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of Ibn Abbas's reading of the verse with tashdeed according to the author?
A) It is part of the Quran and not abrogated.
B) It is ahad and not part of the Quran, and its recitation is abrogated.
C) It is mutawatir and abrogated.
D) It is a valid objection to naskh.

Key Takeaway
Naskh of the fidya option is established by the later explicit command in 2:185; ahad readings cannot override mutawatir Quranic text.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
15 min
Hanafi Refutation of Naskh from Lighter to Heavier
Detailed rebuttal of three objections against naskh from lighter to heavier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on naskh from lighter to heavier and critically evaluate the three objections raised by opponents.

Core Idea
Naskh from lighter to heavier is valid because the heavier may be more beneficial; divine ease is not absolute worldly ease.

This passage presents the Hanafi school's detailed rebuttal of those who argue that naskh (abrogation) from a lighter ruling to a heavier one is impermissible. The opponents rely on three main proofs: the concept of benefit, the Quranic verse on divine ease (2:185), and the verse promising 'better' (2:106). The Hanafi response demonstrates a sophisticated understanding of benefit, contextual interpretation, and the true meaning of 'better' in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Identify that the dispute is whether naskh from a lighter to a heavier ruling is valid. The Hanafi school affirms it; the opponents deny it.
This is a classic usul dispute between Hanafis and certain other schools (possibly Mu'tazila or some Shafi'is).
2
Analyze the first objection (benefit)
The opponents argue that transmitting from lighter to heavier is far from benefit (maslahah). The Hanafi response refutes this by noting that original innocence (bara'ah asliyyah) is not a ruling from the Lawgiver, so naskh from it is not a move from revealed ease. Additionally, the heavier may be more beneficial in the long run.
The author also points out that the very idea of obligation coming from a state of no obligation is itself a transmission from lighter to heavier, which the opponents would also have to accept.
3
Analyze the second objection (verse 2:185)
The opponents cite 'Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship' (2:185). The Hanafi response argues that the context of the verse is the Hereafter (ease of reckoning), not worldly ease. Even if taken as worldly, it is context-specific to travel and sickness, not universal. The 'lam' in 'al-yusr' is for covenant, referring to the ease of breaking fast in travel.
The author also notes that if the verse were general, it would negate all obligations, which is absurd.
4
Analyze the third objection (verse 2:106)
The opponents cite 'We bring better than it or similar' (2:106), arguing that 'better' implies lighter. The Hanafi response explains that 'better' here means better in consequence or reward, or better in rhetorical excellence (i'tijaz). Thus, a heavier ruling can be better in the afterlife.
The author dismisses Ibn Abbas' interpretation of worldly ease as not binding when evidence stands contrary.

Source Text

الله جميع أنواع التخفيف واليسر، كيف حينئذ لا تكليف أصلاً ولا الوقوع في الشدائد بل لتخفيف أمر نسبي وكذا العسر واليسر، فلم يرد العسر الذي يؤدي إلى تلف النفس أو زيادة المرض وأراد اليسر والتخفيف، فأوجب ما لا يوجبهما في ظنه كما في الصوم، بل نقول : قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن كَانَ مَرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْمُسْرَ ﴾ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸٥] قال : اليسر الإفطار في السفر والعسر الصوم في السفر، وبما قررنا ظهر لك أن لا وجه لما في الحاشية) ، ولا يخفى ضعف هذا الإيراد وسقط توجيهه بأن اللام ليست عاهدة فهي للعموم فافهم ولو سلم العموم أيضاً (مخصوص بثقال التكاليف بالاتفاق) فيخص بالتكليف الناسخ أيضاً لدلالة الدليل والعقل قرينة التخصيص (أقول ولو سلم) أن الكريمتين غير مخصوصتين بثقال التكاليف ( فمعناه) أي معنى ذلك القول الكريم (يريد التخفيف واليسر مهما أمكن في نفس الأمر (ولما تغيرت المصلحة لا يمكن منه تعالى، لأنه قبيح يجب تنزيهه تعالى منه وتحقيقه أن نسبة الشرع إلى الأفعال نسبة الطب إلى الأبدان كما في المبادىء الإحكامية، فلا يحكم الشرع إلا بما فيه حسن أو قبح، فرعاية المصلحة واجبة بالنظر إلى الحكمة ولا يمكن بالنظر إلى الحكمة حكم إلا بما فيه إفضاء إلى الثواب وتخليص عن العقاب فلما تغير الفعل الأخف من الافضاء المذكور وصار الفعل الأثقل مفضياً مثل إفضائه في نفس الأمر لم يمكن الحكم بالأخف وتعيين الأثقل بالحكم فافهم (و) قالوا (ثالثاً) قال تعالى: مَا نَنسَخ مِنْ ءَايَةٍ أَوْ نُنسِهَا نَأْتِ بِخَيْرٍ مِنْهَا أَوْ مِثْلِهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ١٠٦] وظاهر أن الأيسر خير في حقه دون الأثقل (والجواب : أنه خير عاقبة لأن النسخ إنما يرد هو إذا صار المأمور المنسوخ قبيحاً، فالنهي عنه أو إيجاب ما هو (They said: First, transmission) from the lighter (to the heavier is further from benefit) so it is not valid. (We said) This is (refuted by transmission to obligation from original innocence) for this is also a transmission from lighter to heavier, so it would be further from benefit. (I say) in the refutation, (original innocence) is not a legal ruling such that obligation would be a transmission from it. (Rather, the discussion is about it. If you say: There is no ugliness in transmission except for causing hardship after ease, and this is realized here, so it should not be valid, then your proof is refuted. I say: There was no ease from the Lawgiver, rather innocence was due to ignorance of benefits. So when the Wise One favored and obligated according to benefits, there is no transmission from the ease established from Him, unlike our case where the ease was from the Wise Lawgiver. So contemplate. (And the truth) in the refutation is (the denial of remoteness) in transmission from lighter to heavier, for the heavier after the lighter may be more beneficial for the responsible person, and the Wise One obligates according to benefits as a favor from Him, not as an obligation, lest it lead to Mu'tazilism. (And) they said (secondly): Allah says: {Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you} (2:185). And it is apparent that there is no ease in transmission from lighter to heavier. (We said: The context of the two verses is concerning the Hereafter, so the easing is the easing of reckoning in the first, and hardship is punishment, and ease is multiplication of reward in the second. Even if it is granted that the intended meaning is worldly easing, and likewise hardship and ease, we do not affirm that it is general, for it is clear that the meaning is not that Allah desires all types of easing and ease, for then there would be no obligation at all and no falling into difficulties. Rather, it is a relative easing. Likewise hardship and ease, so He did not intend hardship that leads to destruction of oneself or increase of sickness, and He intended ease and lightening, so He obligated that which does not cause them in His sight, as in fasting. Rather, we say: Allah says: {And whoever is sick or on a journey, then a number from other days. Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you} (2:185). So it is apparent that the 'lam' is for the covenant, so the ease is the ease of breaking fast in travel and sickness, and the hardship is the hardship of fasting in them. This is supported by what al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Hatim, and Ibn Jarir narrated from Ibn Abbas regarding His saying: {Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you} (2:185). He said: The ease is breaking fast in travel and the hardship is fasting in travel. By what we have established, it is clear to you that there is no basis for what is in the margin. And the weakness of this objection is not hidden, and its reasoning falls because the 'lam' is not specific but general. Understand. And even if generality is granted, (it is specified by the burdens of obligations by consensus), so it is specified by the abrogating obligation as well, due to the evidence of the proof and reason as a context of specification. (I say: Even if it is granted) that the two verses are not specified by the burdens of obligations, (then its meaning) is that the noble saying means: He desires ease and lightening as much as possible in the actual matter. (When the benefit changes, it is not possible from Him, because it is ugly and He must be exalted from it. The reality is that the relationship of the Law to actions is like the relationship of medicine to bodies, as in the principles of rulings. So the Law only rules according to what has goodness or badness. Consideration of benefit is obligatory from the perspective of wisdom, and from the perspective of wisdom, a ruling can only be given that leads to reward and deliverance from punishment. When the lighter act changed from the aforementioned leading, and the heavier act became leading like its leading in reality, it was not possible to rule with the lighter and the heavier was determined. So understand. (And) they said (thirdly): Allah says: {We do not abrogate a verse or cause it to be forgotten except that We bring better than it or similar} (2:106). And it is apparent that the lighter is better for him, not the heavier. (The answer is: It is better in consequence, because abrogation occurs only when the abrogated commanded act becomes ugly, so the prohibition or obligation of what is good in its place, even if heavier, is better for him in consequence. And this goodness is what is intended in the verse. If you say: It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he interpreted it as worldly goodness in terms of hardship and its absence. We say: Even if its authenticity is granted, the interpretation of the narrator is not proof, especially when evidence stands contrary. So contemplate, or the intended meaning is goodness in wording in terms of inimitability, eloquence, and rhetoric, and it has passed before.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute refuting the argument that naskh from lighter to heavier is invalid. The opponents raise three objections: (1) transmission from lighter to heavier contradicts benefit, (2) the verse 'Allah desires ease for you' (2:185) opposes such naskh, and (3) the verse 'We bring better than it' (2:106) implies the replacement must be lighter. The Hanafi response for each is presented: (1) original innocence is not a ruling from the Lawgiver, so naskh does not constitute a move from ease; (2) the ease verse refers to the Hereafter or is context-specific; (3) 'better' refers to consequence, not lightness. The author uses rational arguments and analogy to medicine to show that naskh according to changing benefits is sound. This shows the Hanafi commitment to istihsan and consideration of benefit in naskh.

Key Terms
البراءة الأصلية (al-bara'ah al-asliyyah): The original state of being free from any legal obligation.
مصلحة (maslahah): Benefit or interest that the Law aims to achieve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do the Hanafis respond to the objection that naskh from lighter to heavier contradicts the verse 'Allah desires ease for you' (2:185)?
A) They say the verse refers to the Hereafter, not worldly ease.
B) They say the verse is abrogated.
C) They say the verse is general and applies to all types of ease.
D) They say the verse is unclear.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates naskh from lighter to heavier by reinterpreting the proofs of the opponents, showing that benefit and divine ease are not merely worldly and immediate.

Naskh — Abrogation
beginner
6 min
Naskh of the Entire Quran and Naskh of Both Recitation and Ruling
Statement that naskh of entire Quran is impossible, with example of naskh of both recitation and ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two rulings on naskh (abrogation) of the entire Quran and of both recitation and ruling, and state the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Naskh of the entire Quran is impossible by consensus; naskh of both recitation and ruling is proven by hadith.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut clarifies two crucial points about naskh (abrogation) in the Quran. First, it asserts that abrogating the entire Quran is impossible by consensus due to the Quran's eternal nature. Second, it affirms the possibility of naskh that removes both the recitation and the ruling, using the well-known hadith of ten sucklings being abrogated by five as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage discusses two separate claims: the impossibility of abrogating the entire Quran, and the possibility of abrogating both recitation and ruling of a verse.
These are distinct topics in Usul al-Fiqh.
2
State the ruling for each issue
For the first: 'impossible by consensus'. For the second: 'agreed upon' (i.e., permissible and valid).
The consensus (ijma') on the first makes it a firm ruling.
3
Locate the proof for the second claim
The author cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim narrated by Aisha (radiyallahu anha). Identify the hadith as the evidence.
This is a hadith ahad (single narration), but it is accepted as proof for this issue.
4
Analyze the hadith
The hadith states that ten known sucklings that make unlawful were revealed, then abrogated by five known sucklings. The Prophet died while the original ten verses were still being recited (i.e., the recitation had not yet been removed).
This implies that both the recitation and the ruling of the ten sucklings were abrogated, and later the verses were removed from the written Quran.
5
Understand the implication
This hadith proves that naskh of both recitation and ruling is valid in the Shari'ah. It is a concrete example of this type of naskh.
This ruling is accepted by the majority of scholars, including the Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (نسخ جميع القرآن ممتنع إجماعاً) وذلك لأن فيه الأخبار والقصص والأحكام التي لا يقبل حسنها أو قبحها السقوط. ونسخ التلاوة والحكم معاً اتفاق) ولا حاجة إلى الاستدلال عليه واستدل بما في صحيح مسلم عن أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها : كان فينا أنزل عشر رضعات معلومات يحرّمن ثم نسخن بخمس رضعات معلومات يحرمن فتوفي النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهي فيما يقرأ من القرآن، لكن فيه
Issue: (Naskh of the entire Quran is impossible by consensus) because it contains reports, stories, and rulings whose goodness or badness does not accept dropping. And naskh of recitation and ruling together is (agreed upon). There is no need to prove it, and he argued with what is in Sahih Muslim from Umm al-Mu'mineen Aisha al-Siddiqa (radiyallahu anha): 'Among what was revealed was ten known sucklings that make unlawful, then they were abrogated by five known sucklings that make unlawful, and the Messenger of Allah (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) passed away while they were among what is recited of the Quran, but therein...'
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage states two rulings: (1) Naskh of the entire Quran is impossible by consensus because the Quran contains eternal truths that cannot be completely removed. (2) Naskh of both recitation and ruling simultaneously is agreed upon (by the majority). The author uses the hadith of Aisha from Sahih Muslim as evidence, which relates that the verses about ten sucklings were revealed and then abrogated by five sucklings, and the Prophet died while the original ten verses were still being recited (i.e., the recitation had not been removed until later). This is a classic example of naskh of both recitation and ruling, where the abrogated verses were eventually removed from the Quranic text entirely.

Key Terms
نسخ التلاوة والحكم معاً (naskh al-tilawah wa al-hukm ma'an): Abrogation of both the recitation and the ruling of a Quranic verse, so that neither remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on naskh of the entire Quran?
A) Permissible by consensus.
B) Impossible by consensus.
C) Only permissible for the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).
D) Possible but never occurred.

Key Takeaway
Naskh of the entire Quran is impossible; naskh of both recitation and ruling is proven by the hadith of suckling verses.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
Abrogation of the Entire Quran and of Both Recitation and Ruling
Hanafi analysis of abrogation types and consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of abrogation agreed upon by consensus (entire Quran and both recitation and ruling) and analyze the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Aisha and the response to Abu Muslim al-Jahiz.

Core Idea
Abrogation of all Quran is impossible by consensus; abrogation of both recitation and ruling is established by hadith.

In this lesson, we examine the first part of the passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, which covers the foundational types of abrogation in the Quran. The author begins by stating the consensus (ijma') that abrogating the entire Quran is impossible due to its immutable content. He then addresses abrogation of both recitation and ruling, agreeing it occurred, and refutes the denial of abrogation by Abu Muslim al-Jahiz using the hadith of Aisha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling on abrogation
Locate the statement that abrogation of the entire Quran is impossible by consensus. Note the reason: the Quran contains immutable good and evil rulings.
2
Examine the second agreed type
Find the statement that abrogation of both recitation and ruling together is agreed upon. Note that the author says no evidence is needed.
3
Analyze the proof from hadith
Read the hadith from Aisha about ten sucklings abrogated to five. Identify how this shows abrogation of both recitation and ruling. Note the objection that five sucklings are not in the Quran and the author's response.
The author rejects the Rafida claim that the Quran was lost, citing preservation verses.
4
Evaluate the refutation of Abu Muslim al-Jahiz
Understand that al-Jahiz denied any abrogation in the Quran. The author dismisses this due to prior consensus, showing that his view is not considered.
This is a methodological flaw because it contradicts ijma.

أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها : كان فينا أنزل عشر رضعات معلومات يحرّمن ثم نسخن بخمس رضعات معلومات يحرمن فتوفي النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهي فيما يقرأ من القرآن، لكن فيه انقطاع ،باطن، فإنه ليس في القرآن خمس رضعات ولو قيل إنه كان قرآناً لكن القوم تركوه، لكان هذا قول شياطين الروافض أنه ذهب من القرآن شيء كثير، وكيف يصح هذا وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّا لَم لَحَفِظُونَ ﴾ [الحجر: ٩] و إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا جَمعَهُ وَقُرْهَانَهُ القيامة : ۱۷] إلا أن يقال معناه كان فيما يقرأ عند من لا يعلم نسخه (إلا ما سلف من خلاف (1) أبي مسلم الجاحظ وقوله : أن لا نسخ في القرآن ولا اعتداد بقوله للاجماع السابق على ظهور خلافه بخلاف قوله (وأما نسخ أحدهما) فقط من الحكم فقط أو التلاوة فقط (فيجوز عند الجمهور) جوازاً وقوعياً (خلافاً لبعض المعتزلة : لنا لا تلازم بين جواز التلاوة وحكم (المدلول) فإن جواز التلاوة حكم وحكم المدلول حكم آخر فيجوز (الانفكاك بينهما، فيجوز أن يبقى أحدهما ويرتفع الآخر فقد ( ثبت الجواز (وأيضاً : الوقوع روي عن أمير المؤمنين ( عمر ) رضي الله تعالى عنه (كان فيما أنزل الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما البتة نكالاً من الله والحكم ثابت) وهو الرجم. روى الإمام مالك والشيخان عن ابن عباس أن عمر قام فحمد الله وأثنى عليه ثم قال : أما بعد أيها الناس : إن الله بعث محمداً بالحق وأنزل عليه الكتاب وكان فيما أنزل عليه آية الرجم قرأناها ووعيناها : الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما البتة ورجم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورجمنا بعده، فأخشى أن يطول بالناس زمان أن يقول قائل : لا نجد آية الرجم في كتاب الله، فيضلوا بترك فريضة أنزلها الله ، وروى عبد الرزاق والحاكم وصححه عن أبي بن كعب : بكم تقدر آيها يعني سورة الأحزاب وإنها لتعادل سورة البقرة أو أكثر من سورة البقرة ولقد قرأنا فيها الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما البتة نكالاً من الله والله عزيز حكيم فرفع فيما رفع، وهذا ثابت بطرق لا يبعد أن يدعي التواتر، فاندفع ما أشار إليه بقوله (قيل) هذه الآية منقوله أحاداً و(ما نقل آحاداً ليس بقرآن) وإذا لم يكن قرآناً لا يكون منسوخ التلاوة (أقول) على التنزل لا أسلم أن ما نقل آحاداً ليس قرآناً مطلقاً وإنما المسلم ليس باقياً على القرآنية حال نقله آحاداً وهذه الآية كانت متواترة حين كونها قرآناً وبالنسخ لم يبق متواتراً لارتفاع قرآنيتها (على ما دل عليه قول أبي بن كعب رضي الله تعالى عنه (كنا نقرأ) في بعض روايات الحديث المتقدم، وفيها: ولقد قرأنا بصيغة الجمع، ثم الوقوع مروي في آيات أخرى، فإنه روى عبد الرزاق وأحمد وابن حبان عن أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأعدلين عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه قال : إن الله بعث محمداً بالحق وأنزل معه الكتاب فكان فيما أنزل عليه آية الرجم فرجم ورجمنا بعده، ثم قال: قد كنا نقرأ أو لا ترغبوا عن آبائكم فإنه كفر بكم أن ترغبوا عن آبائكم ، وفي رواية الطبراني عنه قال لزيد : أكذلك يا زيد؟ قال: نعم، وزاد في رواية ابن عبد البر ثم قال : أو ليس كنا نقرأ : الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر فيما فقدنا من كتاب الله، فقال أبي ،بلى والحكمان ثابتان إلى يوم القيامة حرمة الرغبة عن الآباء وثبوت الولد بالفراش الصحيح دون السفاح (ومنه) أي من منسوخ التلاوة (عند الحنفية : القراءة المشهورة لابن مسعود في كفارة اليمين ثلاثة أيام متتابعات) ( (۱) قوله : (أبي مسلم (الجاحظ كذا بالأصل هنا وفيما مرّ في المتن والذي في ابن خلكان وغيره أبو عثمان الجاحظ المعتزلي، كتبه مصححه.
Issue: (Abrogation of all of the Quran is impossible by consensus) because it contains reports, stories, and rulings whose goodness or evil does not accept being dropped. And abrogation of both recitation and ruling together is (agreed upon) and there is no need for evidence on it. And he adduced what is in Sahih Muslim from the Mother of the Believers Aisha, the truthful, may Allah be pleased with her: 'Among what was revealed was ten known sucklings that make unlawful, then they were abrogated by five known sucklings that make unlawful, and the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, passed away, and it was among what was recited of the Quran.' But in it there is an interruption, inner, because there are not five sucklings in the Quran. And if it were said that it was Quran but the people abandoned it, this would be the statement of the devils of the Rafidah that much of the Quran has gone. And how can this be correct when Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, it is We who preserve it' [15:9] and 'Indeed, upon Us is its collection and its recitation' [75:17]? Unless it is said that its meaning was that it was among what was recited by one who did not know its abrogation. (Except for what preceded of the disagreement of Abu Muslim al-Jahiz and his statement that there is no abrogation in the Quran, and his statement is not considered due to the previous consensus against its apparentness, unlike his statement.) And as for abrogation of only one of them, i.e., only the ruling or only the recitation, (it is permissible according to the majority) as a permissibility of occurrence, (contrary to some Mu'tazila). For us: There is no necessary connection between the permissibility of recitation and the ruling of the indicated meaning, for the permissibility of recitation is a ruling and the ruling of the indicated meaning is another ruling, so disjunction between them is permissible, so it is permissible that one remains and the other is raised. So the permissibility is established. And also occurrence: It has been narrated from the Commander of the Faithful Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Among what was revealed was: The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them absolutely, as a punishment from Allah.' And the ruling is established, i.e., stoning. Imam Malik and the two Shaykhs narrated from Ibn Abbas that Umar stood, praised Allah, extolled Him, then said: 'O people, Allah sent Muhammad with the truth and revealed the Book to him, and among what was revealed to him was the verse of stoning. We read it and memorized it: The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them absolutely. And the Messenger of Allah stoned, and we stoned after him. And I fear that with time people will say: We do not find the verse of stoning in the Book of Allah, and they will go astray by abandoning an obligation that Allah sent down.' And Abd al-Razzaq, al-Hakim narrated and authenticated from Ubayy ibn Ka'b: 'How many verses do you count in it? meaning Surah al-Ahzab, and it is equal to Surah al-Baqarah or more than Surah al-Baqarah, and we used to read in it: The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them absolutely, as a punishment from Allah, and Allah is Mighty, Wise. And it was raised among what was raised.' And this is established by chains that are not far from claiming tawatur. So what was indicated by his statement (it was said) this verse is narrated by ahad and (what is narrated by ahad is not Quran) is repelled. And if it is not Quran, then it is not abrogated in recitation. I say: Conceding for the sake of argument, I do not concede that what is narrated by ahad is absolutely not Quran; rather, what is accepted is that it does not remain with Quranicity at the time of its narration as ahad. And this verse was mutawatir when it was Quran, and by abrogation it did not remain mutawatir due to the elevation of its Quranicity, as indicated by the statement of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, may Allah be pleased with him, 'We used to read' in some narrations of the aforementioned hadith, and in it: 'And we used to read' in the plural form. Then occurrence is narrated in other verses: Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, and Ibn Hibban narrated from the Commander of the Faithful and the Just Imam Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: 'Allah sent Muhammad with the truth and revealed the Book with him. Among what was revealed to him was the verse of stoning, so he stoned and we stoned after him. Then he said: We used to read: And do not detest your fathers, for it is disbelief for you to detest your fathers.' And in the narration of al-Tabarani from him, he said to Zayd: 'Is that so, O Zayd?' He said: 'Yes.' And in the narration of Ibn Abd al-Barr, he added: 'Or did we not used to read: The child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone, among what we have lost from the Book of Allah?' He said: 'Yes.' And both rulings are established until the Day of Judgment: the prohibition of detesting fathers and the attribution of the child to the valid bed, not to fornication. And among it (i.e., among abrogated recitation according to the Hanafis) is the famous reading of Ibn Mas'ud regarding the expiation of an oath: 'three consecutive days.' (1) His statement: 'Abu Muslim (al-Jahiz' as in the original here and previously in the text; according to Ibn Khallikan and others, he is Abu Uthman al-Jahiz al-Mu'tazili, written by the corrector.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi discussion on types of Quranic abrogation. It begins by stating the consensus that abrogation of the entire Quran is impossible because it contains reports, stories, and rulings whose goodness/evil are immutable. Abrogation of both recitation and ruling is also agreed upon, attested by the hadith of Aisha about the ten sucklings abrogated to five—though the text notes the issue that five sucklings are not in the Quran, and the objection that this would imply loss of Quran (refuted by preservation verses). The passage then addresses Abu Muslim al-Jahiz's denial of any abrogation in the Quran, dismissing it due to prior consensus. The main discussion turns to abrogation of only one (ruling or recitation), which the majority (جمهور) permit, contrary to some Mu'tazila. The proof is that recitation and ruling are separate legal categories, so one can remain while the other is lifted. Evidence from occurrence: the verse of stoning (آية الرجم) whose recitation was abrogated but the ruling remains. The text cites Umar's sermon, Ubayy ibn Ka'b's statement, and other narrations to show the verse was once recited but raised, with surviving mutawatir transmission before abrogation. The Hanafis also hold that Ibn Mas'ud's reading of 'three consecutive days' for oath expiation is an example of abrogated recitation.

Key Terms
نسخ التلاوة (naskh al-tilāwah): Abrogation of the recitation of a verse from the Quran while its ruling may remain.
نسخ الحكم (naskh al-ḥukm): Abrogation of the legal ruling of a verse while its recitation remains.
آية الرجم (āyat al-rajm): The verse that prescribed stoning for adultery, whose recitation was abrogated but ruling remains.
تواتر (tawātur): Transmission by multiple chains that preclude collusion, establishing certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is abrogation of the entire Quran impossible?
A) Because the Quran is too large to abrogate.
B) Because the Quran contains immutable good and evil rulings.
C) Because consensus allows it only partially.
D) Because the Quran was revealed over 23 years.

Key Takeaway
Abrogation of the entire Quran is impossible by consensus, while abrogation of both recitation and ruling is agreed upon and supported by the hadith of Aisha.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Abrogation of Recitation Only: The Verse of Stoning and Its Proof
Hanafi evidence for abrogation of recitation only

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the proof for abrogation of recitation only (naskh al-tilawa) using the verse of stoning and evaluate the response to the objection about ahad transmission.

Core Idea
The verse of stoning was once part of the Quran; its recitation was abrogated but its ruling remains, proving naskh al-tilawa.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, which provides the primary evidence for abrogation of recitation alone. The author cites multiple narrations from Umar, Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and others that the verse of stoning was formerly recited. He also addresses the objection that these narrations are ahad, arguing that before abrogation the verse was mutawatir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being proved
The passage aims to prove that abrogation of recitation alone (naskh al-tilawa) actually occurred (al-wuqu').
2
Examine the primary evidence
Read the narration from Umar that the verse of stoning was revealed and recited, but later removed. Note the exact wording: 'The old man and the old woman, if they commit fornication, then stone them absolutely.'
Also note the narration from Ubayy ibn Ka'b.
3
Understand the response to the ahad objection
The author addresses the claim that these narrations are ahad and thus cannot establish Quranicity. He argues that the verse was mutawatir when it was part of the Quran; after abrogation, it lost tawatur but its former Quranicity is still proven.
This is a key usul point: the transmission status changes after abrogation.
4
Note additional examples
The passage mentions other verses whose recitation was abrogated, such as the one about not detesting fathers and the hadith about the child belongs to the bed. Also, the Hanafis include Ibn Mas'ud's reading of 'three consecutive days' for oath expiation as an example.

الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما البتة نكالاً من الله والله عزيز حكيم فرفع فيما رفع، وهذا ثابت بطرق لا يبعد أن يدعي التواتر، فاندفع ما أشار إليه بقوله (قيل) هذه الآية منقوله أحاداً و(ما نقل آحاداً ليس
